O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	To you, my very dear son, I have completed this book that is the end of the knowledge of medicine together with its fullness, and I have made an end of it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I will complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work of hands is lost in our region and is alienated from all things in every way, the science and craft are perished, and nothing remains of them but the small descriptions in books by the ancients that the hands have corrupted.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes the errors and vanities, and are closed the intentions and is alienated the sciences.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems that I wish to revive it together with the organization of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of cautery instruments, and the other tools of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is lost.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And one who undertakes [this] must be skilled in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, to know the judgment of members, their forms and connections and separations of them, having knowledge of bones, nerves, joints, and the number of bones, and the movement and resting places, and the location of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason, Hippocrates says that names with the noun are much, and with work is little; similarly in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the beginning of this book that one who is not knowledgeable about the matters previously mentioned, should be careful not to err and not to operate on humans; thus I have seen many times more of those who engage themselves in this science and abandon their knowledge and sense experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish man who cut open one abscess of scrofula from the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of her neck; therefore so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in her hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another man who pulled an arrow from an old man, and the arrow was large; it took a piece of the bladder with it, and the man died within four days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the arrow, and knew well that if it were cut he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And there was another physician who took care of one of our land's dukes, who had his leg broken and with the break had an open wound. And this ignorant physician pulled the fracture above the wound using strong force, and he did not allow any callus to form at the wound, but he let it in such a state; and he commanded that it should not be dislocated; and he waited until the leg became completely swollen and the toes came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to help him, and I hurried to come and dislocate the leg; and when I dislocated it, it was at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all ways of corruption were already confirmed or the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the member was completely destroyed.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there is another type of sore that becomes swollen, then inflamed due to the malice of its dominion.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	When a sore that is full of melancholic humor is not in the place where it can all be removed, one should not touch it with iron.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: one in which there is danger in many situations; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	 Because it is necessary that you protect yourself so that the foolish do not speak ill of you, take your arms in your bosom, and treat your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best means, so that through God's grace you come to salvation and be praised; and leave the diseases that are full of severe pain aside; and remove your weapons from those that make you doubt, and have faith within you so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	 Galen advises in some of his admonitions: "Do not take care of evil diseases lest you be called a foolish person.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 "I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauterizations and anti-fever medicinal cauteries, and they are ordered from the head down to the feet; and of the forms of instruments, and of iron cauterizing tools, and of everything necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and of blistering and wounds, and of the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and they are ordered and of the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters are about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and they are ordered from the head down to the feet, and of the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, as we remember the work, it is necessary that I tell you the quality of the aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of help, and the harm, are the longest and most subtle words and secret responses; and many wise men spoke about this, and agreed with it; and they did not reveal their answers easily, for I shorten it.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery helps universally to all complexions where there is matter, whether it be two complexions: namely, hot complexion with matter, and dry complexion with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry conditions, some say that cautery is a great help; while others say the opposite: that cautery is of no use for illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to cure hot diseases with heat or dryness; and it is said by those who say the opposite that cautery provides great help for hot and dry diseases in humans.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you understand the body of a man and his moisture with the nature of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it once by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every way, do not interfere except those who have tested it and know by long usage the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of human complexions, and their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the occurrences and duration of times; we do not fear other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the people gathered together and agreed upon the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cautery with fire is one of the secrets of healing and has greater goodness than cautery with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not harm any other member unless it touches the one being burned.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	 Burning medicines pass from one member to another by spreading, and bring severe diseases upon the afflicted limbs; and unfortunately, fire may kill the patient due to its high temperature and the goodness of its substance, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	I have found this by experiment and through the length of service and study that I have put into my art, and it is above the truth of things; therefore I excuse myself for the length of my speech, because I do not wish to reveal the secret concerning fire and its nature, and the quality of work, how it subdues diseases of bodies, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; take this into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, when it is appropriate to perform fire cauterization, and they choose friends.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate in all times, because the harm occurring is due to the help of cauterization; and indeed, if cauterization is for necessary pains except when it cannot wait until a greater evil comes upon the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think ever, dear son, as foolish people do; for a disease that is healed by cauterization has no return; and they say it this way, but it is not as they believe, because cauteries are nothing but medicine that changes the complexion, dries the humors that cause pain, and is worth more than other medicines because of its speed in action and the virtue of its work and dominance.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it often happens that the sick person comes according to their complexion and the nature of the disease and its power; and superfluities are gathered within him through the consumption of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are administered where there is little excess and moisture, as in the case of cauterization for pain, and similar things; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the rear of medicine, but they do not believe that cauterization is useful after other treatments; however, their beliefs are false, and cauteries are the rear of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment for any illness and they are ineffective, then we administer cauterization, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is clear that cauteries are the rear of medicine, not as the opinion of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancient ones said that cauteries made of gold are more effective than those made of iron, and they did not say this lightly because of the quality of gold and the highness of its substance; and they said that the heads of cautery do not cause putrefaction, but this is not true, for I have proven it, and I found that it is true in some men; and cauteries made of gold are more effective than those made of iron, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And nevertheless, when you heat instruments of gold, you are not sure when it is hot from the color of the gold, and sometimes it cools down; and if heated too much, it causes fire; and thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore, we use iron cauteries which have been prepared according to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have ordered this chapter concerning the head from neck to feet, so that the path may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	for the olive oil poultice
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and coldness on the brain, and it is used because of a disease called "soda," and because of many humors that flow from the head to the eyes and ears, and due to numerous dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and indeed for all diseases that come from coldness, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a soluble medicine, cleansing the head four or five times, according to what the virtues and age and the patient's condition can bear; and then make the patient lie down with his head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him lie crosswise between your hands, place his hands on a soft surface; after that, put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and where your thumbs meet, it will bleed, then heat the cautery called "olivare," which is as follows:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and move your hand up and down while gradually turning it; then lift your hand immediately, if you see a little bone; and if you do not see it, continue to heat the cautery as I have told you until you see the bone; after that, take one pinch of wool and place it in soft cotton within, and put it on the spot, and let it remain for three days; afterwards put a soft cloth soaked in butter on it; and let it remain until the burn is healed; afterwards treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And as the ancients said, when an overwound wound remains longer, it drains more; and therefore, help it to heal faster.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some said that one should let the fire cautery burn part of the bone and then heal what is burned from the bone and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others said that the cautery should be let burn above and push as hard so that a piece of bone is removed as wide as a walnut, which women put in their vaginas because the fluids come out faster; then the wound should be left open for a long time; after that, it should be healed and cured.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauteries do not seem good to me altogether, except in some men where there is fear; and it seems to me that I should leave them; for the head is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we have witnessed in other members; and even when the head of the patient is weak by nature, the first appearance of cautery seems safer and more beneficial to me, and from this use I work towards salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the chronic and long-lasting pain comes in the head, the patient should use wormwood and pills called "cochie", and purgatives of the head, oils, and plasters; and if they perform the cautery as we have said before, it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's shoulder is of strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize below it with a small amount as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After performing the cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as mentioned before, and perform one cauterization known as "vasselz"; it is one place where bellows are put; align your hand so you do not see beyond the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak more about this later; and the cauterizations of the horns should be finer than those used for the midline of the head, and here is the shape:
dou cautere dou chief	head cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in a part of the head and the disease spreads to the eye, and the head is purged with various medicines, and other treatments as I have said in the division of diseases are done but it brings no benefit; then cauteries are applied according to two ways, namely medicine heat and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery of medicine heat is as follows: take a hot iron and remove the bark from it for about two inches, apply one piece to each head, then place the affected area on top of the heated iron in such a way that you can lower the iron onto the skin; when it has been lowered, hold it firmly and leave it for twelve hours; then release it and treat the wound with linen dipped in butter for two or three days.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with ointments until it heals; and if you see that this does not work, do as I have written for using medicines which burn or for the tenth treatment of burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	 The iron cautery is made in this way.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Heat the cautery as follows:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	It is called "clos" because the head of it is shaped like a claw or has about one finger's width of curvature and a small appearance; place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand firmly while you heat the iron slightly, until half of the thickness of the tip is burned; remove your hand to avoid burning the arteries, which are outside, and let out an abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Place cotton in oil and apply it for four days; then put dampened cotton in butter, and then treat the spot with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this inflammation with a cautery called "cultellare," at its tip, be careful not to cover the artery in this inflammation that is not old.
de emigraine	of migraines
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When treating migraines as we have previously mentioned in the division of diseases and it does not improve, and you find that cauteries before mentioned in medicine and iron do not help; then it is necessary that you heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it becomes white; and press gently along the side of the vein for half a finger's length, remove your hand once, hold steady so as not to cover the artery or reach the bone; watch out for the jawbone which mutes when eating, and avoid nerves having sight of the muted part and spasm coming to the patient, also watch out for bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or bleeding greatly fears and especially those who do not know and have not been trained and experienced; leave the procedure in progress; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it should be found in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not help the disease and the patient is enduring, cauterize it on the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals; and if you see, administer the cautery mentioned earlier or in the chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from cold and it has been treated with soluble medicines and other remedies as we have said in the division, and the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "poins", here is its form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After touching all around the sick ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and moving slightly away from the root of the ear since you have marked its position; and place 10 hot cauteries around each ear; after healing the wound until it is healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	The torture that should be cured by fire is not suitable for those that move due to flux, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not make a fire treatment for things that come from scab or nerve spasm.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this type of torture that moves due to flux from the eyes and purges of the head and gargarismes, it is not worth it, therefore you should cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one in the root of the ear, another slightly further back from the temple, and the third at the corner of the mouth; put the cautery in the part that opens healthy, and make the cautery towards the top of the ear a little below the horn, and another in the temple as long as a thumb; leave the cautery for as long as half of its length is burnt; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the type of cautery we have mentioned earlier, but it is a little more subtle and requires that the knife be slightly thicker; after curing the place as I have previously said, let it be healed when it is clean.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then do four cauterizations: two on the two corners of the head, one at the base of the head, one where it is called "vessel" as we have said before, and the last one on the mouth of the stomach; and treat them as we have said before.
de litargie	When paralysis is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then do four cauterizations: two on the two corners of the head, one at the base of the head, one where it is called "vessel" as we have said before, and the last one on the mouth of the stomach; and treat them as we have said before.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	In this illness, give the patient large yews and round pills with crushed cereal; afterwards, shave the head of the patient completely, and put mustard plaster on the occiput which is written or prepared as a plaster; and this is the way of cauterization: if you do it in this manner as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy in this way, it is good; if not, make four fire cauterizations on the head, descending down to the neck, and leave a space of one finger's width between each cauterization. Treat them as you would others, and if you see any abscess, make one cauterization in the middle; and if necessary, two more on the two horns, and treat until it is healthy. The one that is called "olivare" should be as I said before.
de la froidor dou chief	from the frost of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head of the patient must be cleaned with years and what has been mentioned before; after that, rub the head of the sick person, then make cauterization on the head and one on each horn, and one at the back and two on the spine of the neck. If you need more, and the body is wet and the patient is suffering, and the disease is spreading, make four cauterizations on the spine of the back; leave it until the most painful part is burned, then withdraw your hand; after that, treat until it is healthy, and let the cautery called "olivare" be as mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to treat the brain with years (a kind of mineral) and other cures as we have said in the division when the patient is strong and able to bear taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot endure it, make them gargle and chew a treatment to dissolve the brain often with good foods; afterwards, place the head in a mill and do one cautery as we have said before, and one cautery on the navel, and one on each horn; and if the patient is outside (meaning dead) and able to endure it, do cauteries as I have said for the person who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive oil as I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is suffocated (or drowned), make a fine cautery thus:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When the superfluidities or corrupt moisture (phlegm) flow excessively and are thick, then cauterize with such cauteries as we have said for those who suffer from paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the superfluidities decline towards melancholy and the body of the sick person is moistened, then give him something to drink that purifies the brain, according to what has been said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the king (the patient), make a linen bandage well made, such as a circle, put it on his head; cross the sick person, and hold him tightly from all sides; presently iron the linen, using old cheese rennet; heat the cloth gently so that the sick person can bear it; after emptying the circle inside the head, let it cool; and do this to the patient once a week with good governance, until he is well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	 If you wish to cauterize [something], make multiple punctures throughout the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	 This method of cauterizing increases the brain greatly; then put on top a moistened cotton in butter and linseed oil.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eyes come first with the signs I mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something purifying the head, keep it away from all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe more than once while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that, instruct the patient to lean back and perform cauterization on his head, and make two cauteries on the temples where the discharge is coming from both eyes or one; and burn all veins and arteries beneath the skull, and let the cautery be long according to the size of the temple. Be careful of bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it with your power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and the incision of the cautery how to perform it; and sometimes they make cautery or hot iron beneath the two bones at the back.
dou cors des larmes	The heart of the tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the eyes are old and accustomed and they are above the veins, or in the hollow of the arteries that appear outside the head; and it is clear that it is due to superfluous cold phlegmatic fluids, then do the cautery as I have said at the beginning of this work: one cautery on the forehead, two cauteries on the temples, and two cauteries or hot iron beneath the two bones; and if it is necessary, cauterize skillfully above the brow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	The heart weeps within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat the patient according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give a sick person three hot poultices; after these, roast the head, and make a cautery or olive oil cautery, and make two cauteries called "clavilis" above the shoulders, a little below the hairline; and beware of the artery that you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	 When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize this cautery which is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	 Thus, this is its form:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish to perform two cauteries on the two sorcerers as long as they are like sorcerers; and do not leave your hand except when the third part of the paper is burned, according to the way that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair which pricks the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes the hairs of the oils are converted into a thorn and prick oil; and in such cases cautery is performed according to two methods: namely by fire or by hot medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	The patient should be instructed to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they have grown and are even, then put the patient on a clean surface; after that, draw a figure of the hairs like the leaves of myrtle, with the beginning of the sign cut away from the hairs; then place cotton soaked in egg white and musk oil on top of the oil, then heat the iron cautery in this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing the figure that you have drawn many times so that the hair is burned in that place; and the signs of health for the work are that you see the paper recede, and the hairs rise to the tip of the oil; then leave your hand, and let it rest for 3 days, then soak the cotton in butter until the burn is removed; afterwards heal with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And after that, hairs may come up, and the paper is softened then begin the cautery on the same place again, as you did before; and if the hairs are curled, cauterize them until the paper is raised to its natural level, and they are straight, and do not prick the hairs with oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of burning medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make parchment in the shape of the myrtle leaf; then take French soap and hot water, each one .З., grind them together well; and do it quickly, so as not to cool, then spread the mixture over the shape you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and put the hairs on top of the parchment; and if the patient can only withstand one drop of oil, you should work with one, and if in both cases; and place cotton dipped in egg white beneath the oil; and the head of the patient should be healthy and your hand mostraring over the medicine, and press one finger and move it all the time when the patient feels a bite from the medicine, for it bites like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a while, remove the medicine from your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	 And when the mordication is passed, lift up the shoulder blade and see if the paper is raised in the same way as it was raised by fire or by incision; and if it is so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is not so, then apply more medicine to the shoulder blade or the medicine has not worked yet, until your efforts are even and your eyes are steady; then put on moistened cotton in butter until the burns are healed, after cure the shoulder with an ointment called "dyafenis" and another one, until it is healthy.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	 And if you need to protect yourself well in your work, keep a great watch so that the medicine does not fall into your eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	 And if the paper becomes damp afterwards and the hairs prick in the oil, start the medicine again on that part which has been moistened properly, as you have done before; afterward cure it until it is healed; and this is the shape of the comb for the vervain herb:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the hairs of men are different in size and according to this, your treatments should be adapted; and do not deviate from the correct path for those who study this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When treating a fistula as mentioned in the classification of diseases, and your treatments do not help at all, then you must cauterize it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head on a clean surface, and have the assistant hold his head between their hands so that it does not move or tilt to one side; then place a moist cotton ball in egg oil or fresh linen on the cautery site; then heat the cautery until it is hot but not red-hot, shaped like the tip of a feather, pointed at the end, and as long as necessary for your work; however, the shape does not matter too much, what matters is that it is pointed. If you wish, it can be straight from one end to the other or in the shape of a tent; but whatever the shape, the tip is most important for your task.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it is open and draining pus, drain it, and dry it; if it is closed, open it, and drain foreign matter; then place the heated cautery on top of it carefully, making sure your hand does not slip; place the cautery in the fat of the oil and let it corrode.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	 If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	 If that's not the case, start the cautery again once more and if needed, let it rest for three days; then put cotton soaked in butter on top of it, and treat with the drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is still not healed, apply corrosive medicine to expose the bone; and the king shall act according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	 And there is a kind of fire cautery that none of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	 For the fistula, open it and then put in the substance called camelian in that form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make it in the amount of one cubit; hold your hand or cannula firmly, and do not let the patient move, so that the melted lead does not spill onto his eye; and you must put oil on the patient's cotton soaked in egg white or vinegar: the lead will heal the fistula, and the wound will be cured by marvelous healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	 And if the fistula is healed by the fire cautery that we have said, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	 If not, then it is necessary to administer butter to the nose and bring the fistula back towards the nose in accordance with what is appropriate according to its own place.
des crevaices en levres	cavities in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there appear cavities in lips called "hairs", and the same happens in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cavities as we have said in the divisions, and the treatment does not help, then scald a small, sharp-edged cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it quickly into those hollows until it reaches the bottom; afterwards, treat the area with turpentine until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	For the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes at the root of the throat or in the eye, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth, after it becomes pustular and grows and turns into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not improve: then you must have .i. cautery according to the size of the fistula; after opening or draining the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron is hot at its base and where it ends; and do this once or twice, after curing as we have said in treatments, until it is healed; and if it is healed, that's good; and if not, you must discover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	The movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are moistened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicine but it is of no use, then put the head of the patient in your lap; afterwards, heat up the cautery as will be described below, put a cane on the tooth; and insert the heated cautery deeply into the tooth, hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat approaching the root of the tooth; afterwards, remove your hand and repeat the cautery according to your desire; afterwards, fill the mouth of the patient with salt water and tie it up for an hour and rinse vigorously.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in such a manner, the moving teeth are confirmed, and the gums softened are held back, and the moistures are dried up.
de la dolor des dens	Of the pain in the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain in the teeth comes from cold or wetness, and there is coldness or fever, and medicines do not work, then it will be necessary to use a cautery according to two methods: a cautery of butter and a cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	A cautery of butter is as follows: you take butter from a cow, and the tip in an iron or horn spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the point of a tent (a small sheet), and moisten it in boiled butter, and put it quickly on the painful tooth and hold it until it becomes cooled; and do so often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see the cotton and wool becoming cold in cold butter, put it back on the tooth and put hot iron near the root of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	 The cautery combined with fire is such that you take a wire of iron or brass, and it should be thick so that the flame does not reach the patient's mouth; after heating the cautioner, let the form come as follows, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled; do this often, for the pain will be alleviated that day itself or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And it is necessary that the patient fill their mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cautery, and then draw out the hot iron; and this is the shape of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery for the head that you want, and according to what you can do; and this is the shape of the cane:
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When scrofulas are of cold and wet pus, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery as described below and make it have openings for the smoke to issue from the other side; and place the hot iron on the abscess where needed until it reaches the bottom of the abscess. If the abscess is small, use a correspondingly smaller cautery, and leave it in for three days; apply moistened cotton soaked in butter until the pus is removed. After that, cure the wound with ointments and salves until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	 The shape of the arm:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	 When the frost conquers the channels of the arm, and especially when it comes from cold constitution, then it is necessary for the patient to be bled first with resolving medicines; afterwards, make a cautery at the root of the neck, but do not go near the neck, and be careful not to burn too much.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then make another cautery at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and let it be the cautery called "clavicle" from which we have the shape previously mentioned; and cure the place as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	When the moisture conquers over the channels of the throat, especially when it comes from cold complexion, then the patient should be purged first with soluble medicines. After that, perform cautery at the base of the tongue, but be careful not to go too close to the throat, only a little. Then, perform one other cautery at the jointure of the neck and the head of the spine, using the shape as we have described before. And heal the place as we have said before until it becomes healthy.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When the illness of throat is due to cold moisture, and the patient does not have fever or heat, and the illness is old, then two cauteries should be performed on the forceps in visible places; and one other cautery between the breasts; and let the cauteries which is called "clavile" have the form as we have said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 And if you see, make a cautery by pricking all over the cautery called "points" from which the shape is previously mentioned in the ear disease; and let the points be up to 30 or thereabouts.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	 After curing the shoulder according to what was said before, let the cautery be at three intervals according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because the cauteries are lighter, since you make four together.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After holding the patient on his back and on his side; after heating the iron that is inside the hollow of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated within, then apply the heated cautery in the shape described by these two nerves (nerve roots) here:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the iron up to the ribs, and bring forth four figures with the cautery made of three nerve roots; because the figure of cauterization consists of several cauteries; and these nerves are according to the subtlety of a tendon, and this is the shape of the cautery that has three nerve roots:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is dislocated above this nerve, for which there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After applying the cautery, crush it with oil; afterwards make the patient rest and do not move the limbs for long periods until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 If it is dislocated above (the shoulder), which happens rarely, then make a cautery on the thick part of the large cautery rod, or many cauterizations at the base with smaller ones.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 For the joint is put back in place, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When there are many coldness and moisture in the stomach that cause it to become cold to its complexion, and many catharrs are multiplied for him, and in common ways of treatment it does not help; then the patient should lie on his back, and extend his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 After that, he makes three fire cauterizations under the hip-bone at the size of a finger, for each cauterization using a pointed tool, and two more cauterizations away from the two sides until the shape of the cauterizations forms three angles, with enough space between them so they do not stick together when pus is released; and the shapes of the cauterizations should be sharp enough to pierce the two parts of the kidney, and the shapes of the cauterizations should be adjusted according to this form:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if you wish to cauterize with a large cauterizer in the stomach according to this form, and he who fears that cauterizer, cauterize by pressing and holding on the stomach at the point according to the amount you see; then cauterize it completely, which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the healing of the wound has taken place, when it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	 When the liver experiences pain from coldness, moisture and large ventosity, when it is forced to move away from its natural complexion due to excesses; and the patient is treated as we have said in divisions, but it does not benefit him, then the patient must be made aware of his illness; and a sign for three cauterizations according to this form, figure, and quantity should be given on the liver, near the hypochondriac region, where the ribs of the body come; and there should be space between each cauterization, the size of a thumb; and the cauterizations should be long, not pressed too hard with your hand; and only the halves of the coal should be burned, and the patient must lie on his back; and if he cannot, then he should be lying down, and stretch out his legs, and lift up his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And if your wish is, cauterize these cauteries with the knife, if you are skillful and wise in the art, but do not dare too much because you would burn all over the body; and it should not reach the boil, for the place is very subtle there, and the wise can see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 When there is an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is in the liver's flesh or the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient does not feel much pain; but if it is in the membrane, then the pain is madness-like.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 And when this cure is over, the patient should lie on his head; and then press firmly at the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery that is similar to a radish, as shown in the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 And apply the fire cautery until the flesh is burned, and stop at syphac, so that it can be completely removed; afterwards, cure according to the cure of abscesses until it becomes healthy; and it should not be used for this cautery by anyone except those who have studied medicine for a long time, and many times these diseases have been cured by them.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Then it can be boldly operated, and nevertheless I seem to think that more benefit is obtained by letting it rest.
dou cautere de pleuresin	the cautery for pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancient ones said one should make incisions with cauterizations of the root of Acorus calamus (Aristologe), and in this manner: take a long root of Aristologe, as large and as long as your thumb; moisten it in oil, immerse it in fire, and cauterize one cautery between the armpit and neck, and two small cauteries a little below where the beard is; two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, leaning back slightly; one cautery on the side of the pain, and one more on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on the sides of the pain away from the cautery which is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but rather make an opening as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	 And some old people say that anyone uses the fire cautery resembling a razor, and they heat it up and place it between the ribs until it reaches an abscess; and the pain subsides, as we have said in the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	 But in this work, there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the sickness of the mice that we have spoken about in the divisions of cures and it does not help, then apply three ways of cautery that are all good.
