Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	 In the first way, you make three or four cauterizations, aligning them according to the length of the mouse (as we have said before about the liver-shaped cautery); and do not hurry with your hand for the entire cauterization, and let the patient be aware of their back; and another way of cauterizing is that you heat the cauter which has two nerves, as we showed in the dislocation of the shoulder; and cut off the fat that is next to the mouse, or the sides where the sick person's pain comes from, and lift the elevations from the fat according to the fat, according to the length of the body, and the cauter should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	 After, place the two inflamed nerves so that their holes are pierced from the other side, and then draw out the cautery, and thus there will be four. If you see, if you cauterize the entire cautery at three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	 Afterwards, treat it when it has had purulent discharge for a long time, and this is what the other treatments mentioned before do.
de ydropisie	Of hydropisy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	 The cautery is not effective against dropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	 When the cure is performed according to the methods that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not benefit, then you must perform four cauteries around the abscess, one above the stomach, one above the liver, one above the spleen, two at the bottom of the back near the spine, and one where it hurts; and the cauteries should be close to the thick part of the abscess.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the cautery open to expel pus for a long time, do not neglect the care of the patient after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions (healing and relief of pain) will come together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is like the claw that we have shown before; and the one for the back should be olive-shaped, as it was explained earlier.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	 When the feet are swollen in someone who is dropsical and filled with water citrus, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and dip your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	 And do not go too deep in, thus would force the water citrus out, and let the cautery be in this shape:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After doing two cauteries on each leg with the tip of the knife; and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and the other outside, in the leg; and leave the cauteries above for a while to heal, until the water heals; then treat the other wounds as we have said.
de la menoison	of the swelling
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the swelling of the belly comes from cold and moisture, and the digestive and retentive qualities that are in the stomach and intestines are hindered, and cannot be cured by means of treatments; and you see the patient suffering greatly and of strong constitution, then make one large cautery on the stomach according to what was spoken before about the stomach cautery, and the circular cautery; and four subtle cauteries around the belly, one subtle cautery clavicle, and two cauteries on the flanks.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the elbow, and one on each joint, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, for the treatment is beneficial where there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	 When the hemorrhoids are founded or several, and are old and filled with large cold and moist corrupted humors, and have been treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not help if you do cauteries: III on the spine of the back, which is completely withdrawn from almecdate pocket and pocket in triangular form, and the cautery under the buttocks II should be; and if you think that the stomach is cooled, and the meat is not cooked, and one sees the face swell up, then the stomach should be given a large cautery, as it has been said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen to the entire length of the cautery; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After curing the shoulder when it is healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the carnositis called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you apply the cautery to althelul (possibly an herb), heat the cautery which seems like a razor, and then place it all around the althelul, covering it; leave your hand there so that the cautery reaches the opening of the vein, causing it to close; do this once or twice, and if there is much althelul, cauterize each one as we have said; after that, heal with ointments until they are healthy; and if you cauterize a large cautery on alchatim (possibly a lesion), it will have more aid.
de plaie mal curee	of an improperly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	If the patient cannot bear any incision or opening, as we will explain in its place, this disease comes that can only be cured by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	 If any abscess comes, that is swollen and filled with pus and corrupted moisture, you must probe it entirely using a delicate test, and ensure that you know the extent to which it has spread.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	 After sharpening the cautery that resembles a razor, put it into the abscess according to the size that the pus has entered, and continue burning until the body is burned and corrupted, once, or two or three times, depending on the amount of pain; be careful not to burn the nerves that are there, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	 If the abscess goes to the body of the bladder or intestines, be careful with these places, and do not perform it elsewhere except in a healthy place, and think that it is not perspicuous; after curing the shoulder when it is healthy, if the shoulders are sewn and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the shoulder is healed completely; and if the matter has not been removed, then know that the shoulder is broken, and corrupted bones will form; and thus like one of those whom we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	This text appears to be discussing a medical treatment for a kidney-related issue based on the context of "la vesie" (bladder) mentioned earlier in the text. The translation provided above translates the given sentence as follows:
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain in the kidneys comes with large swelling and does not improve in women, then you must perform cautery on both sides of the kidneys using the clavicle-shaped cautery as mentioned before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be four cauteries in a line, and it will provide more help.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and soft due to coldness or moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then you make a fire cautery on the part outside the bladder, where the hair of the penis begins, one on the right side and one on the left side, and each cauterization should be as long as the knuckle; and make one cauterization behind the back, or two if necessary; and the cauterizations should be pointed in shape according to the aforementioned form.
de la marris	of the marriage (or wife)
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the matrix (uterus) is cold and moist and does not allow conception, and the flowers (ovum) are corrupted and their term delayed; and when they come, there is great pain: then it is necessary to perform four cauteries around the womb, as described in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries behind the back; and let the cauterization be with a needle, as described.
de la hainche	When the loins (lower back) are swollen and painful: then it is necessary to make four incisions, one above the other, on both sides of the lower back, from the waist to the buttocks; and the wound must be washed with warm water and vinegar.
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the swollen loins (lower back) descend to the abdomen and move out of their place due to this, and the signs are that one thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found in the region of the hernia, then you must cauterize the patient on the lower back at one cautery, similar to a circle, and mark the location around the hernia so that the hernia is within the circle; and let the cauterization be like the one used for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this fire cautery is not present for you, make four large olive oil cauterizations instead, and let them be as deep as all the others; heal it until it heals.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the hernia
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hernia of the groin, and it is due to coldness and moisture; the patient is cured by what we have said in the division, but the cure is not effective, and the disease is old: therefore, you must purge the patient with pills made from foul herbs or other good-seeming pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	 After that, make cautery; and the manner of cautery is according to two ways: namely, with burning medicines, and cautery by fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	 Cautery by fire is according to many ways, one of which is such that you cauterize three triangular cauteries on the boil of the haunch in this manner, and make deep and large incisions between each cauterization, leaving enough space for a thumb, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes cautery is made in the middle on the head of the haunch, so there are four as follows:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize with the circular cautery that we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the thigh; but make it so that the circles enclose the entire thigh, and all the fat surrounding it is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	 And this is the way it is done in sciatica, when the pain remains in the loin, and does not reach the thigh nor the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 If it reaches the thigh and the leg, have II cauteries there where the pain is, and let the patient say that the pain remains; and the cautery should be a lancet, and the thickness of the coal burned should be thin; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two feet or near the ankle, cauterize it where they feel the pain 3 inches or 4 inches away from the place called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, do more; and if the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a fire cautery with a cutlery or circular cautery, but take good care in all your cauteries that you do not let the cautery burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient any greater harm or contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	 And I myself have seen more who have performed cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they let it stay so that the leg became swollen and the toes as well, and they were pierced and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	 After a stomach solution where he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	 And if the pain is in two places at once, make a cautery in one and the other, as follows.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	 And the wise will say regarding the cautery of the groin, as follows: make this iron and its tip be as thick as a thumbnail or slightly less, and between these points should be the width of a nut (poce); and these points should be above each other, like nuts, and have the handle well-made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be scalded until it is all red and blisters, and then place it on top of the sick person's haunch bone, turning it towards the healthy side; and cauterize once with one hot iron, leave it for three days; then make a plaster of butter, keep the wound open for a long time; afterwards cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use this cautery sparingly due to the fear of its gaze, and few do so; yet it is a good cautery, which can withstand it, and in places where it adheres.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	 The cautery of burning medicine is to make the instrument between the points where it descends from the edge of the opening, and it should be made of iron or copper for a long length; at the top, there should be two nuts; and there should be space between each one equal to the thickness of a dove's egg; they should be turned over and above, and join together in this way:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	 After placing the boil on the patient lying on one side, hold your hand above the boil; then pour between the two circles of hot water that has been heated in a pot, and leave it for an hour, and let the patient endure the heat and burn from it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For it heals as if by fire; and when the inflammation has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and gently lift the boil from the heat, and leave for three days; then apply butter so that the black scab is removed; and leave for three more days until the pus drains out; and this would be the final aid after the cure of ointments until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	 And if the pain has spread to the thigh or the leg, perform the instrument that binds according to what you have done in the haunch strongly; and this is the method of the hot plaster, and I have written it or treated it regarding the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	 Take quicklime and hot coals, an equal amount of each, grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	 or it has a small hole covered so that the tip of a needle can enter; and place one pot on top of another well weighed pot, and put soft plaster on top of the lime and coals as much as you have previously kneaded with your hand; and leave it like that until the powder settles down and becomes wet or the upper pot is weighed, then take all that plaster, and pour it over the coals and over the lime as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	 And then if it (the dislocation) is much agitated and treated with various medical procedures and fire cauteries of other members, because it does the same work as fire, and also with other medicines that one cauterizes well the inflammation in such a way as tesisie, honey and aniseed, and chalk with soap; all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	 And Galen tells us of a cure in which a nobleman was cured of the pain of the inflammation and sciatica, and he highly praises it, and says that no other treatment was done, and that he became well at one time when this treatment was made, and he bathed as he instructs below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	 And he says in this manner that you take the powdered green veratrum (litargirioide) and mix it with a little fat, and apply it to the inflammation and to the thigh and to the leg where the pain is, and hold it; leave it for three hours until the patient no longer feels the burning sensation.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	 And then make him enter the bath until his body is slightly warmed up, and let him lie down, and the pain will go away completely and he will be cured.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	 Know that no one should use such fire cautery medicine unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	 And Dioscorides said that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's fat, it helps very much; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	 Take linen and anoint it with old oil, and place it over the furrow that is between the toe of the foot and the one called foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	 After taking dry goat's fat, heat it on fire until it becomes charcoal, and place it on the linen, and let it stay; repeat this process again, and do not stop until you think by your senses that it reaches the hainche, and that the pain is ceased; and this method of cautery is called "cautere de chievre".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or striking or excessive bleeding, or from similar causes of cold matter spreading, none of these similar symptoms are worth cauterization, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	Then, after the patient has been bled of foul pills or similar substances, three lines should be signed on the back where the pain is located, and in each line 5 or more cauterizations according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and the cauterization should be made according to the cauterization known as "poins"; and if you see, make 4 cauterizations or 3 according to the medium-sized cauterization in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes to young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a narrow anus when they defecate, and fear; you will find it in the last spine of the back and in the appearance that comes above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to heal it, cauterize it with the fire cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	 The cautery makes every part of the spine swell up.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	 And if you see, cauterize around the spine with a cautery puncturing it two or three lines apart, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	 After curing the place until it is healed as we have said, beware of applying a cautery in the area where there is nerve damage.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain in the joints is due to moisture that affects every member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which are called "podagre" properly, and when it is caused by cold and medicines cannot cure it, it is cured by cautery as follows: make the patient sit down near the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	 If it is necessary to prick the belly of the thigh, make the cauterization all over the cautery that they call "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if the pain comes up to the genitals and other joints, which happens often, cauterize over each thigh with three or four cauteries on each part, using an olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do more, but don't hold your hand too far that the coal of the fire is not burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	 And if the pains descend to the thighs and back, administer the fire cautery as described in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	 And if the pains are at the hands, make small incisions two finger-widths apart; and if there is no more pain in the fingers, make incisions above each joint and above the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the elbows or up to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and think about medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	 For if you give good care and you cleanse with purging, it will heal with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the sinus (or sinew)
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the rupture happens in the bladder, and the bowels descend into the cavity and this is new, if you wish to treat it, then it must not eat that day; and let him use things which relax the stomach, so that the feces descend from his stomach; afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his anus as long as the bowels are repaired, and reinsert them with your fingers, and sign over the rupture on the bone of the thumb, and at all a sign that is similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery in the form given here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	 until it becomes white and flows out pusules.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	 Then straighten the bones to their place; and the minister holds his hand above that they do not return backwards; and work well the thighs on the patient, and put the cushion and the sergeant under him on the thighs, and the other one on the foot which holds the hands; then place the cautery on the sign throughout your whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, try again until you come to the bone; be careful that the bones do not crack when you perform the cauterization; and beware that you do not burn him; and so that the patient does not die or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	 And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	 And the cauteries for children should be fine-tuned according to their size, and for adults also large according to their measure; after three days, cure the leaching of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed; after that, cure it with other salves until it heals, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days so that the wound heals well; and it is necessary that his dressings be left long, so that the boils do not protrude when he gets up to go to rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	 And after forty days, when he wants to get up, bring him a well-made cloth and keep it for another forty days; let him have good rest, so that he does not work too much and be careful of excessive drinking and eating, and of too high fever; and if he follows this instruction, he will heal completely.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	 And I shall tell you after the cure of tailor in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of abdominal rupture
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	 When roundworms come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then perform the cautery of the cautery according to its quantity, and let it be burned one third degree; afterwards cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized at three angles according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	 but first mark the beginning and make a line above the roundworm, and another below, and then hold your hand all over the entire cautery iron.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	 But the first cauteries are lighter and easier to move.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	 When pain comes in any limb, either from falling or being struck, and the pain lasts a long time, and the cures of medicine are of no avail, then it should be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cauteries should be according to the length of the limb, its smallness and fragility, and its virtue and location for twisting and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	 If the first incision heals well, that's good; but if the same incision needs another treatment over it, you should do so because it is customary for the affected member to heal in time, which is why you must perform the cauteries as long as the patient is healing.
de meselerie	In mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	 The illnesses are sometimes relieved by cautery with great help, and especially those that originate from the corruption of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	 Can you see the patient being cauterized? Take care if the illness is at the beginning, and if it is cured as we have said in the division, and it neither festers nor remains, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the patient, then perform V cauteries on the head: First lift the head to your lap, and the other toward the forehead at the end of the hair; and II on the II horns, and I behind the neck; and leave your hand so that the cautery reaches the bone, and so that the scabs come out from within so that the vapors of the gross humors can escape; and cauterize on the mouse according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mixture is scattered everywhere; it clearly perishes, you should cauterize with the cauteries that we have mentioned earlier, namely one cautery on the neck, two cauteries on the spine of the neck, six cauteries on the spine of the back, one large one on the hip and one smaller one, two on the shoulders, two on the hips, two on the shins, one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; beware of the nerves that are above the last rib, do not burn them; sometimes a person cauterizes a bone in the fist, and one in the stomach bone, and another in the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	 And know that the more you do of cautery, the more help it provides, and it benefits them; and know that the sick do not feel pain from cautery as the healthy do, because their bodies are already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	 And it is necessary that the cautery be large and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in ways of iron-working.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	 After curing the wound with wheat flour with honey and other treatments until it is drained.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When inflammation appears in any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but it is not drained, then you do cauterization on the member according to its size and the smallness or largeness of the member; and let the cauterization be slightly deep into the flesh. Then cure it with oil until it is drained.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	 And sometimes one makes a fire cautery at the hand, foot, and back, at the nerve's opening that renders the limb immobile, and thus the skin is cut open; and no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	When a tumor appears on any member and it is treated with medicine, oils, and plasters, but it does not heal, then the cautery is made on the limb according to its size; and the cautery may be superficial or deep into the flesh; then cure it with poultices until it heals. And sometimes a cautery is performed in the hand, foot, back, at the nerve's exit that makes the limb immobile, thus removing the tumor; however, no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about members and the nerves moving the body.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease known as "albaras" grows, and the medicine does not work on it, then cauterize with a deep cautery until the blister disappears and its color changes; then treat with flour and lentils mixed with rose oil and banana leaves, along with cow blood and almond blood, each in equal parts; mix everything together and bind with cloth, and apply to the affected area until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of scrofula by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When a boil begins and you want to stop it, if you cauterize, do so with the cautery that resembles a circle, all around the boil's circumference.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 And yet the wise say that one should cauterize in the middle of the boil; and yet I do not find it good because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen once; a more direct thing is that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circle", as we said earlier about cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	the swelling that cannot grow or spread
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	 When someone has a disease called "adubelati," which is slow to heal or because of the superfluity it causes, or because of the age of the patient when they are decrepit (meaning very old) and have little blood, or because of the time; and you see it hastening to heal: then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by pricking; afterwards, leave it.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 Then let it heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced completely by the cautery, then heat the cautery according to this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 Keep your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have pierced through, and let these cauteries be such that the patient feels them only in such a way that the course of the pus is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the cure when he is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure for fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 Another form of disease is called "corrosion", and it is nothing but an erosion of a limb, for it consumes the limbs as fire dries up dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 If you see this disease in a place that can be treated with cautery along with fire, then heat the cauteries little and big, according to what is necessary at the location where the disease is; after cauterizing all parts until you reach all the corruption and nothing remains of it, so that everything corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then leave it for three days, and put soft powdered cauterized leaves on the affected areas, crushed with oil until the burns from the fire are removed and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After the treatment of worms producing char (sores or ulcers).
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 And if after three days you see that healthy sores do not appear, it is good; and if not, start the cautery on the lesion that remains in the corrupt flesh.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 This method has sometimes been cured with hot medicines instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless, fire cautery is more helpful, and I have already said the cure for hot medicines in the section on the plague: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	the worms that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 Often times, through the feet, a disease arises which is called "closed," according to our understanding, and it is a large thing filled with pus that swells the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the cauteries for this disease are of two kinds.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 That is to say, cautery with fire and cauterization with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 Cautery with fire consists of heating the cauterization iron to the same temperature as a ploughshare, made of good iron that can pierce through all sides and has fine edges; after it is heated, place it on top of the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the point of the nail; leave it in this position for three days until it begins to purge pus; then make a plaster of wild herbs boiled with oil, and leave the plaster on it all night, and the nails will shrink and be uprooted from their roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal the shoulder with an ointment soothing warm salve until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 And if it has been turned outward by the body, and this happens often in hands and feet, then you must bring hot cautery; it is done like this: take a cane of tar or iron, or a pen from a candle, and place it on the nail and althea, that is to say against warts; and place the cane so that it surrounds completely, then put a little hot coal there, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the cane comes to the root of the nail, and may find the hot coal deep penetration to the root; and let the patient endure a little bite of hot coal for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will rot out completely with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 Follow another method while you are heating all those [affected] within the body, then treat them with ointments that soothe pain.
li cure dou trembler	the one who cures trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles due to cold or fever of quartain, or from another [cause], it is necessary that you apply 4 or 5 cauteries along the spine of the back, 1 between each spine; and 1 cautery on the shank, and 1 on the stomach with an olive-leaf cautery; this will make him stop trembling, and hasten his recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of rotten boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 Occasionally, on the outside of the body appear baths, or pustules that come from large corrupt matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 First, when they appear, it is necessary to make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery made from mirtle wood, so that its point is immersed in fire, or from long aristolochia root, or with lenticulaire cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 And sometimes they cauterize at the beginning when they appear in this manner, and they cannot grow further, but the superfluous matter from which they come is broken up, and they become healthy; however, it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great outflows of blood from the cut artery at the wound that comes to the outside, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cautery of a limb, and similar things; and it is a very bad thing to let it flow.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And even if it happens to anyone, hasten to place your index finger on the wound of the vein and hold it very tight so that the blood is stopped under your finger, and no more juice flows out; then take olive oil cauteries, both small and large ones until they are all red; then take .i., either large or small depending on the size of the wound and where the artery is running, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery in place until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a leap happens when you place your thumb over the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take immediately one other cautery that are by fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing one after the other until the vein is completely drained; and watch that you do not burn the nerve that is exposed, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when the vein dries up from the artery, it cannot be well stopped if the artery is large, except by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strongly tied string, or by medicines placed on it that have the power to stop blood; and let it be tied and constricted accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings a tightening of the ligature with cloth or puts something hot on it, or similar things, will not benefit if there is no profit.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone who has no mirror or medicine present, you should place your finger on the wound of the vein as we have said and stretch it out until it is tightened over the wound and the vein; and do not move it, but the cold moist should often be applied to make it very cold so that the blood congeals and thickens and remains; and make inquiries ahead about the person who needs cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	In the first chapter we have told you about all diseases in which fire cautery or burning medicine is needed, and we have explained their uses, causes, instruments, forms of cauteries; and I have put that chapter up to the thighs and will proceed in this chapter by the same path for those things that are easier to understand.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauterizations, and for this reason greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 And I warn you not to take foolishness upon yourself.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 For many ways of people come in treatments.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 There come those who are so sick with their disease that they die quickly due to the frenzy they find in their illness, and from the greatness of its malignancy; and these should be feared.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	 And among these there are those who give you their advice and say, "Wait, I am cured"; but the illness is deceitful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 You should not easily consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more trust in your honor than in your desire, and do not act recklessly but wisely with those from whom you are certain, and with whom you can learn; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients to convert salvation; and this will help you acquire good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, Our Lords grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to inspire with the holy inspiration of his hand, come.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Furthermore, I have divided this chapter into sections by chapters, according to what is before or in the chapter of cauteries, which I have described for you from head to feet, because you will find it easier to understand those matters which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	This disease often comes to children during childbirth and when the head of the child is forced too hard; sometimes it happens because of reasons we do not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone other than children, and all those I have seen hurried towards death; therefore, it seems to me that I should waste less effort on such treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and it grew larger every day until it could no longer support itself; and the moisture collected under the skull between the skin and the bone; and the treatments are such that if the moisture is between the skin and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make a large incision in the head; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture runs out; and here is the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you observe the edges where the abscess is located at each part, and when you press it with your hand inside, and it does not respond: then you must make four incisions in the middle of the abscess, according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 And after the incision, remove all the moisture thoroughly.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 After the incision, draw out the pus with linen and powders, put vinegar and oil on it, and let it stay like this until the fifth day; then open it up, cure the wound with poultices and ointments, let the swelling decrease, and give the patient dry meat without moisture for as long as the member is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look where the abscess is largest, and gather the pus; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore, incise where the abscess is open, and drain the pus, and do as you can; but avoid covering the artery; and let blood flow, so that the patient dies a natural death from loss of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of scrofula
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When a certain disease called "cataract" affects the eyes or becomes worse, and medicine treatment is of no help, then the last resort is the cautery by cutting into the 2 arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	 Therefore, when you wish to cover it, the patient should bend down over his head; then rub the area with a rough linen cloth until the arteries appear, then tightly bind the patient's neck with the cloth; look where the veins bulge, and check that the veins on both sides are behind the ears, and the pulses are located there; then mark the places of the pulse, then prick one and the other with a sharp spatula of two fingers deep, until the incision reaches the bone, and this should be done at the base of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it (the artery), push the spatula underneath the artery and cut through it (the artery).
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when a vein is cut, it jumps out continuously towards the top.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And if the artery does not open up by itself, you must measure the space of three fingers, then press and proceed to the bone; and what amount of blood needs to be let out is 6 cubic centimeters, and occasionally a little more or less, depending on what the patient can endure, and the filling of the artery; then examine the wound: if it remains above the bone without swelling, if the pus that comes out of an abscess does not come, then hold the wound closed and bound, and apply ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	of emigration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes with a sharp catarrh, due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples and a feeble and aged headache, and it is treated by means of medicine cures but does not improve; then we should open the arteries of the temples and cauterize them as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extraction is that the patient leans backwards over his temples, and listens to the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well by beating, and is not easily retracted except in some cold-natured people; and if it has been retracted, the patient should tighten his neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and moisten the area with hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula of the following shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	 Then lightly scrape the skin to reach the artery, then pull it upward with pliers, and remove carefully the cloths that are under each part; and if the artery is delicate, turn it to the point of the scissors, then apply the cut from that part according to the amount of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	 If it is not cut, it cannot heal entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from the 5th finger joint, up to the 3rd joint; and if the arteries are large, you must tie it with a thick double silk thread so that pus does not come before the wound is closed, and there is bleeding; then cut off the excess between the 2 tendons at that hour itself, and if you see, cauterize the cauterizer scalpel up to the bone as much as the joints are cut; and this is the mutilation work, if the patient does not have fever and he is of a hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauteries is aid for finishing the sores: because it is of greater help to sores.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, one must fill the place with old cotton and put on tight bandages; and when you loosen them, cure it with dry medicines that make pus, and bandages, until it is healed; and if there is no incision of the artery as much as you work, hurry to cover it with cauterization, or use vitriol and strain it with your hand so that the wound does not become infected; and if you do not have this present, put your finger on the place until it freezes, and scrape the place with cold water until it stops, and strained as necessary; and the mutilated and easier in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this sharp cautery with two parts, but they should be well thickened to keep longer its heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the instrument (strumens) is too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And should have between the two blades, one thick of space, and when you have marked with incision on both sides, and you place the heated iron for as long as it comes to the bone, and cut the vein in two leagues; and they should be kept apart because they are not welded from this cautery throughout; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes flow out of the veins that are on top of the face near the head, and no medicine helps in treating it, you see the patient's face turning pale with shivering, as if with fever; and when they are tender and moist so that the eyelashes fall off, the eyelids are scalded by the tears, then this kind of treatment is needed.
