Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 And they called it the "cured crushed", and you shall do to the patient who has this disease shave the hairs on his forehead, then make three equal incisions in the forehead according to the length of the forehead; one of the incisions should be as deep as necessary, along the middle line from the top to the nose, and the other two should be along the eyebrows parallel to the eyebrows, but avoid cutting the arteries that are near the brows; and keep your hand away from the lower jaws, and each wound should be the size of three fingers joined together; and prepare a piece of sponge and a lot of linen to soak up the blood, then insert the pointed spatula through two parts as shown here:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is across the temple up to the second incision; and scrape all the fat that is between the two cuts right to the bone, then do another thing from the mid-incision up to the other second one, and then pull out this spathule.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert the instrument called "cultellaire" into the first incision. It is very sharp on one side and soft but not sharp on the other, and it has this shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And strike the rib cutting towards the chest cavity, and the rib becomes soft towards the bone, and push it until it comes to the middle opening.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And sew all the vessels that descend from the head to the base of the incision until it is complete to where the opening of the chest cavity is, and then continue in the middle opening to the other side; and then extract blood evenly, and press the location for the blood taken; then put a tent of old cotton in each opening, and put damp linen soaked in vinegar, oil, and asafoetida on top, and ensure that no pus comes in; and on the third day remove the sutures, and apply large amounts of cold tamarind juice, then ointment with basilicon and rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	The root of the hairs
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Whenever a sharp catarrh commonly comes, you see the thin and small hairs, dimming the vision, and burned paper; and the hair follicles itch, and where the head is painful with severe pain, and the patient coughs; then know from these symptoms that those substances and the catarrh do not come from anywhere other than many veins, and the cure for this is to open them.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And you are to instruct the patient to bend their head backward, then make a wide cut across the forehead and another deep one in the back of the neck.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 From the temple on the left side to the temple on the right, make an incision as deep as the bone; move your hand away from the nerves that move when chewing; once the bone is exposed, drain all the blood onto a sponge; then insert between the two lips of the cut and put old cotton, and thread; then cover with damp cloths soaked in vinegar and oil, and avoid getting hot; once it has been removed, you must rub the bone until char begins to grow, then treat it with things that promote the growth of char.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take 2 parts of wheat flour and 4 parts of colophony, and make a poultice with it; administer it in these wounds to alleviate pain everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stoppage of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains, animals, stones or similar such as iron; seeds like peas, beans, lentils; liquid substances like water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When it falls into the ear, stone or any other thing that does not fit in the ear, does not grow within the ear, place the affected ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see a stone, apply some drops of violet oil or camphor oil, then induce extraction; have the patient cough and close the nostrils when coughing occurs, wrap the affected ear with pieces of cloth or wool around it, and hold it above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 Often, farting occurs with this treatment; if it does not, use fine forceps for extraction as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out at the hinges, that's good; if not, introduce extraction with a thin wire of small twisting; and if it doesn't jump out by that means, make a thread of wax and push the head of the thread or ear canal firmly, and stop up what is around the thread with soft wax so that the vein cannot enter with the thread; then pull forcefully, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it doesn't come out in this manner, take glue from where you can get it, put any tool suitable for this purpose on it, and put a piece of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or something similar and pull forcefully.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't jump out by any of the things we have said, hurry to incise the ear before an abscess forms and spasms; and the manner of incision is that you first cleanse the patient's head, then draw blood according to the strength of its virtue, then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear upward, and make a small incision in the root of the ear where the fat or flesh hangs; and let the incision be like a moon, until you reach the bone, then break it as far as your power allows, and suck the pus quickly into your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that swells and it cannot be extracted, introduce one thin and subtle spatula in this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 make an incision in that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 Do not make incisions if you believe the grain is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made several sections; then extract it with fine forceps and suction as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 In water then that falls into the ear, the patient should use warm cleansing with early condiments, and fill the ear with soft cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And let him lie on that same ear itself where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it jumps out because of this, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 If it does not jump out because of this, take many small and light stones according to the length of your finger, heat them slightly in the fire; and have the patient put one or two fingers into his ear, and press from another side with a stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop pressing the stones against each other until the water comes out completely, and then it jumps out entirely; and if you see, take string, and push one of the ears into the ear, and the other end takes fire as much as the string burns; then tie another string as long as the water comes out completely, as we have said in the previous section.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it has a small body like fleas and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it has a large body that can be felt, use the extraction method with tweezers; it is easier to remove lighter objects from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in treating distillations, and the treatment does not help, then you should look at the ear in the sun: if any worms appear, take them with fine tweezers, and if none appear, take a reed of this shape.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And it should be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And push the smaller head into the ear according to the severity of the patient's pain, then suck strongly on the whole cane; do this repeatedly until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if they do not come out, stop up around the cane with cotton as I have said earlier; and if they do not protrude as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective in expelling worms, and you will find or treat the distillations of such substances; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this apparatus, here is the method as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And make it of silver or tin narrow within and wide above to distill; and for pressing inside the distillation, one instrument made of tin is required; and if you see, take a grater and wrap it around the tip with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicines you have in the reed, and the reed should be in the ear; then push the grater with all the cotton inside, and press your hand evenly until the oil is distilled or boils out of the ear; and let the patient smell it within, and the distillation should be one pot heated by fire in this way that it is distilled in the ear; and ensure that it is not too cold, for the medicines will not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stoppage of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some imperfection in the ears; and this same thing happens to men by stoppage of a wound or pus coming from within the ear, and this stoppage comes completely into the ear at times when it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a drop or two of pus protruding, and it can be clearly seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, if it comes completely into the ear and cannot be seen, it is difficult to cure in various conditions, and in such cases, you must place the sick person's ear in the sun; look inside: if you see the obstruction clearly, open the affected area with this spatula-like tool that is shaped as shown below:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be cauterized and incised all around, both in front and behind, so that it does not touch the ear; if the swelling is of new flesh or cartilage of the ear, hold it with subtle forceps and strike gently until the flesh is completely burned out.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the tumor is fully within the ear, take a subtle razor lightly and heat it slightly with fire, then place it in the ear of the patient.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you feel the tumor that causes the patient discomfort in the ear, make a small incision carefully, ensuring not to injure the nerves of the ear; then insert a bandage according to the width of the wound and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound heals; take a linen patch and moisten it with rosewater, and sprinkle powder of vitriol over it; if you see the ear swelling, it is necessary to remove the linen patch and apply another moistened linen patch made of rose oil and beeswax until the swelling subsides; then heal it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding, which are either to treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper charcoal
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althelul that comes from the hairs when they are moist and dry, it is necessary to stretch them with tongs and tweezers, and then crush them with a spatula of their roots; then put vitriol powder on the place.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And without removing [the affected part], if you cauterize with the subtle cautery of lenticles, and after incision is necessary to be cauterized; and many times they heal, since nothing remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hailstone
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Often these things come in paper that resemble hail in shape and hardness, and because of this the disease is called "hailstone"; it is a mass of moisture in the upper and lower paper; the treatment is as follows: observe carefully if the hailstone moves from one side to another, and this can be easily determined; then make an incision from one side, peel off each part gently, grasp with tweezers, and crush.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 If you cannot cover it with something to pierce a little of the paper, cause no pain to the patient; and if the wound is large, gather it together in stitches, and cure it until it heals; and if it is small, do not apply force, as the humors restore it soon and cause harm.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the stone is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper and place the stone in tweezers, press it from both sides; and if the paper is pushed back by the incision, it does not matter; and when the stone is pressed, apply oil of brine to the affected area, and treat the wound of those who are injured until the patient recovers.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat from the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 Exinach is greased onto papers made of parchment above it, and this happens more often in children than adults, causing much pain to them, and they get catarrhs at dawn, and cannot bear the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; therefore, they lie on their faces immediately, sleep on top, and keep their papers under their eyelashes moistened so that the exinach oozes onto the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you push the joint with your fingers and feel it pop between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of work is that the patient places their head on your lap; and then take one linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the size required for each part, then place it over [them]; and press with your hands from both sides so that the parts are assembled within the circle; then make an incision in the middle of the moist area with a sharp spatula, and it should not be larger than the wound made during vein opening; and cut through the skin completely to expose the incised area; and in various positions the incised area comes from the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take a piece of coarse cloth between your hands and spread it apart until it is scattered; and ensure that you do not widen the incision or bring the spatula to the oil, do not pierce it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	If the incised area does not open at the beginning of the incision, raise it slightly; then spread it as we have said, then wet cloths with oil and water, and place them on the wound, and hold bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And if such people who grind mustard and place it over to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal him until he is sound.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If an abscess comes to the joint that is hot, then heal it with plasters softening until it is sound.
des poilz des papieres	of the papers' hairs
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper grows hairs other than its nature, and is nurtured, it harms the eyes, and brings about manners of diseases such as the accustomed tears and swelling of papers and albugine, to the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by medicine for ague according to that which is before in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by canes, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient's head on your sound side, then turn the paper with the oil on your left hand; if it is converted (turned), that's good; if not, push an awl through one filament (hair strand) of it; and cut the hair adjacent to the hair strands, and draw one filament above the entire paper, then scrape it flat; then make a hole in the part underneath the paper, beneath the hair, all the way from the large fold to the small; then extract one filament, and place a small tent of cotton and linen beneath the paper, then mark on the paper a figure like the thorn of blackberry, and note that the figure should be according to the quantity that you see will raise the paper which has been designated for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 If there is much paper needed according to the softness of the paper; then spread it all over the space you have marked, starting from the large blister up to the small one; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the onion into one of the two angles of the incision, then peel it all; then bring the two edges together with a stitch using an awl with fine linen thread, squeeze out the blood, and remove the excess threads on the two corners with something sticky, if you want to do this; otherwise, leave the suture and the threads for three or four days; then heal the wound without sutures with dry and binding substances, because the paper dissolves at the edge of the wound and merges with it, but the suture is rotten (as the ancients say), and this is a dangerous procedure; there is another way: and it is that you sign the paper with a shape like the leaves of myrtle, as we have described, with three onions cut off according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then bind (or tie) equally the parts which are above the small ones, according to the form shown here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 And if you cannot hold the pliers, and the parts are not even, take a needle with thread, and insert it through the figure; and place one end of the thread into the large wound, and the other end into the small, and arrange the threads equally between your fingers; then move your hand equally, and lift all the skin as you have described, then close the two lips of the wound by suturing, and let it heal until it is healthy; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with ointment and similar calming substances; and sometimes the hair of the papyrus becomes inverted: then use what we have said about the incision; but the suturing in one and the other is more complex.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for canines is as follows: You should fold the paper and place it inside as I have said, then make two canines by art, and two subtle threads of the same length as the paper and the width of a needle hole; take the two heads from two parts where you hold the threads; then put one on top of the other subtly over what is above the paper of oil, and bind the two canines from the two parts; leave it in this state for some days, and the skin that is bound will die and rot away, until it falls off.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it is delayed, if it is struck with force, then cure it until it heals; and when the wound is sutured, and the paper raised, and the hairs cannot be felt; and this is the shape of the two canines you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The workings are as follows: You take a fine needle and insert one thin thread of silk; then assemble the heads and place them together subtly, and make sure that the length of the threads is about one palm (5 inches); then tie another fine silk thread briefly to the end of the canine; then place the patient's head in your hand and ensure that the work is done in the sun, as this is a subtle and delicate procedure; then insert the needle into the entire sheath next to the natural hair root and pierce the paper immediately so that it pulls up the natural hair; then pull out the hair until it reaches the end of the canine, and put that hair in the canine, if there is one or more; then pull your hand until the hairs come out completely with the natural hair in the paper.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the shot (arrow or other projectile) is expelled but the hairs do not come out with it, you shall draw the shot beneath to its full length that you have ordered, until the shot comes forth through the wound and you see it by the sight of the eye; then, you shall draw out the shot and the string, close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair regrows in its place and flesh grows over it; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from a goat's beard with it, and let it be grown along with that which you leave, until it is distanced and then cut it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the purulence of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 When this disease which is called "alecratius" or the purulence comes in the eye, it occurs in two ways: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 It happens from a sudden blow to the wound, or cut, or burn, or similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 The method of the work in it is that you cut open the suture, disconnect the edges of it, put inside linen tents and tie it until it heals; and it should not be used in the treatment of it with things that dry and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 If you do that, the disease will be worse than before; but with things softening, such as fenugreek; and the roast of water or barley and flax seeds cooked, and then castor oil melted in any of the oils, and wrap it in a cloth, and apply it to that.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the key to your treatment is to ensure that the joint does not heal in its former shape; and this work that we have mentioned has no effect on this illness unless it corrects its shape so that it does not return to its former state.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the fat from the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This disease which truly is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 The accident arises from wounds and cuts and cauteries and things similar; and the method of work in it is that you take a needle with double thread, and poke it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left eye socket to the right one so that the threads come out through the two cheeks; then place the flesh over the whole needle, and apply a spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that's good; if not, take the razor and place it in the crack, and turn the paper, and make two cracks where the bone is within the paper; and let the edges of the two cracks be at the angles of the incision you made, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the shape will be as the shape of a letter with the name "Greek"; then remove that cartilage, according to its thickness where it is close to the paper, then join the two separated parts with a linen thread; then apply the medicine for softening and binding, as we have said before, until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a wound or stitching or cauterization, it is necessary that you make a deep incision under the hair of the paper, as mentioned before; then separate between the two layers of linen, as I have said; and the work should be done according to the shape of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters prepare any tool with all possible means to return the figure to its natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary for the work and tools in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	Sudden blow of paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture happens in the hands of men in such a manner that the paper above is glued with white oil and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the point of a razor beneath the paper, lift it up; and hold it with pincers, until you reach that which is at the root of the splinter, which should not be too sharp nor too jagged, so that the patient does not suffer from too sharp a splinter piercing the oil; and your incision, from which you scrape away the assembled mass, should be gentle, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and this entire assembly is healed, and at times it becomes infected with foul oil and produces pus and colic; then put between the paper and the oil a tent of linen, and place on the oil damp wool in abundance of egg; and after the third day use warm colic and healing ointments until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is of two types: one is nervous and resembles a hard horn, and another which is not nervous but resembles white frozen moisture; when it is touched by iron and cooked with tweezers, it cannot move; and both types begin towards the large root and grow little by little until they cover the entire nail bed and light and the movement of oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient places his head in your hand, then you open the eyes; take paper with your hand, then grasp the nail with tweezers of small double curvature and hold it above; then take a needle, put a horse hair or cow or bull hair and a strong thread on it; double the tip of the needle a little and pierce it into the nail, and poke it all through, tie the nail with the thread and hold it above, and shave off all the hair from the side of the nail that was under the cuticle and the silk to the hair up to the root, then crush the rest in the root of the big toe to a very subtle paste with small forceps, and leave the natural flesh or root, so that the corpuscles do not flow out as is customary; and sometimes the nail grows only at the onychium (the upper part of the nail) and along the sides, as we have said; then shave off all the substance of it in this way:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatumile does not touch the flesh and tear it apart, and that the pulp is not pierced; and after the incision, pour a little oil of sebum (oily matter secreted by skin glands) and collyrium (medicine used for eye problems), and leave it until the next day; then cure it as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the unguent can't enter, this resemblance of a nail is often cured with medicines; and they grow as I have told in the division, and if you see it covered, it works the oil of the patient, and take the spatulum lightly and sharp according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Gently press the nail above, and if you see that it does not soften and reason does not apply to it, distill from your mouth into the colyrium oil made of litargirio and red collyrium powder and sulfur, and let the oil rest until the next day; then repeat the work according to this same process until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes in the oil, as with an abscess, then let it drain, and cure the abscess hot until it is healed, then repeat the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh around the armpit harms in oil greatly, suspend it at the onion, and cut a part of it but not all, so that no tears come from it; then distill in the oil colyrium red which is made with litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that arises above the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 The first hairs of certain men sometimes grow red and cover the anus and adhere to paper and turn inwards, resembling a stone rose; and the operations are such that the patient places his head in the bowl, then you open the anus, and all that charred material suitable for this purpose should be removed and held firm with force; then cut the first layer of char, and go on cutting to the bottom using a razor until the end, ensuring not to wound the oil during the operation; and it should be the incision with the spatula as described in the incision of the nail and small forces used for removing flesh, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is complete and all the char is removed, use oil of linseed or you distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines, and put cotton with egg white on top to ensure that the wound is hot; and if something remains, and the flesh swells and you doubt that the wound is hot, leave the oil and treat the wound with calming agents for a hot wound; then return to your operation when it is healed, and do so whenever charred material adheres in the oil by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, it is necessary that you alleviate the cure of each oil with a natural remedy; and for an accidental treatment, in work with iron; do not put your hand in any of these treatments until you see that this member is strong enough for that work.
des voines des eulz	veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 Should the veins be red that are covered by oil, they will make their work visible and weaken the oil for all days.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 Then, it is necessary for the first to inspect if the oil, in which the scab is present, has any other disease apart from the scab; then treat the oil as follows: Instruct the patient to place their head in your hand, then press those veins all along the length according to your discretion, and let the incisions be subtle and twice the size of the scab according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two incisions by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then carefully apply force to those veins subtly, and squeeze the blood out hour after hour, until you see the veins move away from the oil; also ensure that the oil is not pricked by the tips of the lancets, and perform this task at noon in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your work so as to not spoil the veins; and when you have completed this, if it distills green and red collyrium for correcting those that remain affected by the sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot catch [or bind] all of it in that hour, make a plaster on the oil of soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is soothed and assured of healing, then resume according to this manner which is beforehand until it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula (small tube) of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire (a cyst or abscess) is called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and burning medicine as I said before, and it is not healed, there is a device within it that you should cut open on the abscess where it must break, and drain all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, if [the area] is ready with all the instruments as mentioned here; it is called "sharp head", and make a hollow [cavity] of about 1 inch deep, pointed like a chisel as shown in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	Then turn the bone corruption between your hands and press with your hand slightly to ensure that the corruption is removed; do this once, then restore the joint with medicinal poultice.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 If the lesion is sutured and pus does not appear, and the body of the bowel remains thus for 40 days without returning or becoming abscessed, and no bad accident occurs, as it is healthy; if this is not the case, there is no other remedy except to return the fistula to the neck as follows: Expose the bone again with a knife, and with hot medicines, and when it is exposed, take the iron fork according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and let the shaft be attenuated up to the head as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 Then place it on the bone of the dislocation, and move your hand away from the oil hole, then turn the lever completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it if you keep your hand on his neck; and then restore the joint with dry medicines as I have shown you, and when the flesh hardens and the joints soften, the matter goes to the neck; it is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	The translation of this line is: "of the oil's discharge" or "from the discharge of the oil".
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is completely open and there is no need to disturb the nose or reduce it, you must hold the patient; then clean the eye, then apply poultices or hot oil to help heal, then place the oil (a mixture of aconite, aloe, incense, and sarcolocca) on a linen thread and tie the eye, then apply ointment on bands and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths, fold each one in four, and then place one on top of another according to the amount needed by the eye; then tighten with a strong bandage and repeat the poultices to help heal without hurting; then remove the poultices and leave the tied eye for a day and night, and if the thread wears out, you must tie it tightly again; then remove the thread after the day and night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not; repeat the ointment, cloths, thread, and poultices until the eye is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The dislocation of a torn membrane
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in a torn membrane, they open up and fart like paper, similar to grains of resin and are visible; then you must cover it. The procedure is such that you insert an awl into the root of the affected area until it reaches above, then insert another awl where there is a double thread from the edge of the tear; pierce it, leaving the first awl in place according to its position; then tie the end of the double thread and wrap a part of the membrane around it, tightening it, then remove the awl and apply oiled linen cloth moistened with egg; leave it until the threads grow with the membrane, then cure the area with comforting substances until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is held closed by the membrane on both sides in a circular bandage of fabric until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear large, pierce it with a fine spatula coming from oil and remove the moisture and pus, then enter immediately; then pull out until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	From the bone of the oil (can mean "from a bone soaked in oil")
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This disease called "alcunnati" is not foreign but rather a tumor assembled in the oil, appearing like an abscess, but it is not an abscess; and the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared chair and straight, then take his head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the tumor come up to your eyes; then let it be stuck, and do not drain and let the light enter, and let the patient see things as he is accustomed; and if it does not drain below, know that it is an abscess, and if the draining of the tumor is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Make the patient sit between your hands, then take the thin spatula and press it against the corneal membrane on the affected spot, as long as the bubble persists; and when it bursts, distill into it hot sharp oil mixed with honey, or hot water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then treat it with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	diseases of the oil (can mean "diseases that occur from bones soaked in oil")
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have the resemblance of pimples in the separation, and that which is required to pierce; if you do so according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit cross-legged, away from light because of the sun, and hold the oil in one hand very tightly; then place the paper with the oil on your left hand if the eyes are on the left, or on your right hand if the eyes are on the right; then take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand if the eyes are on the left, or in your left hand if the eyes are on the right; then place the tip of the instrument under the cornea by a distance of about one fingerbreadth at the smaller tear duct, then push the almagda instrument firmly, and keep your hand steady until it pierces the cornea, and you will feel that almagda comes to an empty place; and it is necessary that the length of the path of almagda should be at the full length of the space between the pupil to the end of the black part; and this is the cornea of the oil; then you will see the bone in the paper due to the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then place the instrument up to the bone or to the wound, then press it gently.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 If it is to cut now, the patient sees it before him and the instrument in its oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 After resting for a moment, and if it is to cut again along the second vein, place the force with the instrument, and when it is well inserted and does not rise, press it gently by turning your hand little by little; then insert a small amount of gem-oil within it.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then pour oil made from hemp or dampened linen in rose oil and abundant egg, and bind with the oil of vinegar.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We and those of our time place on it a mixture of crushed egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, because there are some men who have too hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", which is shaped as follows:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 So, pierce the conjunctiva only and do not go too deep, but make it thin, then put in a moderate amount, as we have said; and upon completion of the work prepare the patient who will sleep on his back in a dark room; be attentive to all movements, give light foods, and do not move his head to either side, and bind him according to his position for three days; then unbind him in the same dark room and examine his sight, show him some things, and then re-bind him for seven days; and it is not advisable that you perform this in the hour of the cure or after the incision, but rather relax it, because the vein rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 When an abscess comes, you should lance the oil before the seventh day, and direct it to the one who soothes the abscess; and when it is soothed, you should then lance the eye and put gold or silver on its surface to cover for any duration of time, and stay always in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then leave the house little by little and convert to your condition; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Iram, who told us that in his land they pierce almond ointment, so that the pain subsides, but I never saw anyone do it in our land, nor have I ever read it in books of ancient times; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the resemblances of the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them see them; and they are from a rain properly speaking:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And be the heads of these from the same subtlety, and the rear parts in four angles pointed.
de la char sor le neis	of the chest on the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes born or are born various tumors, from which there are some that seem like scorpions with many legs; and if there is such a one or it has a tumor swollen in a dark color, and if the tumor is soft of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In that case, of those soft charms (or concoctions), and not too harsh, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands towards the sun; open his nostrils, and pour the unguent into those charms, and force them out; then take what you can hold with a sharp, slender spatula on one side, until you know that the charm is completely stopped.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be caught, open it with all sorts of subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if the abscess is swollen, or an arrow, seek aid as necessary; and if these are malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize until the wound is sealed and all charities are removed, then spit bile or hot vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If it doesn't open (the nostrils), moisture approaches up to the palace (brain), knowing that he is healthy; and if moisture does not pierce as necessary, know that there is pus growing in the bone above, to which the cautery does not come for cutting: then you should put a thick thread of linen, about two fingers apart, into his nostrils, and pull it through smelling until it comes out from the nose down his mouth; and many times do this to children at school, and it is an easy thing for him who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes from the nose in one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth in another hand, and know each other while they are with us who are at the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do as you know that the nose has been corrupted by corruption of flesh, then pull out the pus, drain the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nostril as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh; then put a plank splint on it for some days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, as one distills oils and medicines at the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it shall be of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and lead it thus; and if you see, make a closed cane, and let the tool be plain for purging the head; and have one handle on the head for holding when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the chest on the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often a disease named "telul" arises on the neck of the head and grows large over time until it is visible; therefore, it is necessary to treat it from the beginning, remove all pus, and then apply fire cautery or burning medicine to it; if it is not treated promptly when it first appears, and it becomes hard, dark, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an aggravated abscess, for when it is touched even once, the patient experiences great harm; and if the abscess is soft in texture but does not have a foul color, you can cover it entirely, let the patient relax without fear, and treat the surrounding area with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nails are cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when solution comes in one of these jointed cartilages, it is of little use, unless in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, when such a thing happens to anyone, one should look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then align the two lips to a stitch, heal it until it is healthy; and if the lips have already separated on both sides, you must cut all the parts of their flesh until they bleed, then align the two lips to a stitch, tighten it, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood and finely crushed incense on top; and place a piece of strong or other plaster holding it in place until it hardens, then heal it with ointment until it is healthy.
