Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is such that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as I have told you in abdominal stitching; or with thread, as I have mentioned before.
des apostemes des levres	for abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	When abscesses occur within the lips that are hard and grain-like, either small or large, then you must turn the lips and cut through each side with scissors and take it out with tweezers in each part; afterwards apply vitriol powder to the incision until the wound is cauterized; and then apply alum to heal the wound of dry things until it becomes healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the jaws
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often flesh grows adjacent to the jaws that the ancients call "albulus"; it must be held with tongs and cut at its root, leaving the vein or blood to flow; then apply vitriol powder or other drying and constricting powders on the place; and if the flesh returns after incision, which often happens, cut it a second time and cauterize it: it does not return again after cauterization; and these are the forms of the instruments for covering.
des sordens	boils
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, teeth or gums assemble together at the jaw, inside the mouth between the gums; these are ugly and rough; and sometimes the tooth is black and citron colored and sharp, until corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth is foul-smelling; then you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head should be in your lap, and peel back the teeth or the roughness that appears, as long as nothing remains; and in this way do with the blackness and the greenness, and the yellow and other stains, until they are removed; and if one removes what is at the root first, it is good; if not, then begin again the second day and the third, as long as you have everything removed; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments for cleaning, according to the work that shows, because the cleaner who cleans the teeth has other forms than the one who cleans between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you are treating the tooth from its pain, it is necessary that you pull slowly as much as you can, for this should not be done hastily; for this is a very high substance until there is no excuse to scrape.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Therefore, when the patient is compelled to draw teeth, one must be certain about the tooth to be pulled.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Many times the patient feels pain and thinks it is a toothache, and makes the good tooth come out; yet the pain does not go away until the bad one has been removed, for we have often seen this with holy men; and when you are certain that it is the dying tooth, then you must cauterize around the tooth at every interval. Use strong forceps to keep the gums from all sides; then rotate it with your fingers or subtle pliers at the first sign of movement, until it has been well dislodged, and firmly grasp the pliers; and hold the patient's head between your knees so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After the tooth has been correctly removed, if it does not fly out, take any of these instruments and gently push it in from all sides, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and eaten through, you must fill it with gauze where the hole is; and if you hold it gently with tweezers, so as not to break while squeezing; and you must work very carefully around the gumline to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 Be careful not to break it and leave a part behind, because returning it again due to the root's mischief will cause greater pain to the patient than the first time.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And beware that you do not act like ignorant people who, in their haste and audacity, break the cart sometimes, and do not bring the things we have mentioned; but they sometimes cause this great illness by the roots that remain or by the cart they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled out, wash the area with wine or vinegar and oil; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill it with pulverized vitriol; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, which initially silence the teeth, should be long points and thick handles, so that they do not twist when you pull the tooth; and these are their forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be large members which do not yield when drawn, and let them be made of hard iron and sharp-edged to hold fast.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains at its pulling, you must put on it soft cotton wool in butter for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 as long as the joints are softened, then insert the tongs called "algefri," with which the head resembles a beak of a vise; and within them, make it shaped like a limpet shell.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tongs, you must cut open the skin all around the root, and put the instrument called "althali," which is known as a pincers, there; this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	It should be large and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through these tongs, that is good; if not, help with all the instruments, and here are the shapes that follow:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument with two prongs, here is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are in front of the teeth, and of this tool that seems like large pincers, whose shape is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this tool should not break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and likewise other instruments which are not counted; and the wise masters skillfully find their own tool according to what their work and the sickness show, for there are such diseases where the ancient ones did not teach any instrument due to diversity among them; and if it breaks a chariot or another bone that it could have healed, then search for the instruments that are needed, which I told you, and help with gestures, of which this is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be large and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not slip, but can hold and remove; and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is pus in the bone, which is small, grind all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not as natural according to the body, and the shape is ugly, even in virgin women, then you must know that if the tooth has not erupted after the tooth, and it is not in the correct place, and it cannot be straightened or filed: then file it; and if it is near the tooth, take this instrument with the following form, and resembling a small beak, made of sharp metal at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the coping file should be used with much care for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file it with a small file like this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the file used to make needles; and with a light touch file the tooth little by little, so that it does not move too much when it emerges; then smooth the end in any way with any smoother, and if the tooth is excessively sharp and it bites the tongue, then you must file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth fall out
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the teeth fall out in front or by falling or crushing, and the patient cannot chew food without them spilling out, and you have cured them with constricting medicines, and it is of no use; then they must be held together with a golden thread, because silver threads become green and decay, but gold never changes; and the thread should be neither too thick nor too thin nor too small, according to the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are separated, take the thread and place it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the head between the separated teeth as many as there are, one or more, until you see clearly up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue the covering until the part where you began, and hold your hand skillfully and carefully, so that they do not move at all; and tie the knot at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then take the shoulder bones with wire using pliers, and assemble them, and place them back between the healthy joint; make sure it does not pierce the tongue, then leave it as tight as it can stay in place, if it dislocates or the wires break, secure it with another wire; if it remains and serves for its entire time, it is the shape of the teeth and the alignment of the two healthy joints, and the two muscles, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the teeth fall out and are put back in their place, freshly, as we have said; and do not let anyone interfere who is not wise and patient, and sometimes a tooth of bone from a cow or other animal is made and placed where the missing tooth was, and it is tied in as described above, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Occasionally there is a ligament that comes from under the tongue, which occurs naturally; or by accident due to a healed wound; and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, hold their head still, and lift the tongue; then take hold of the nervous ligament with a large grip, until the tongue dislocates from its place, if there is resistance or not, it is the result of a severe wound, in this case press the knife and take hold of that ligament; but make sure the cut is not too deep, because the artery is below; and when done, lift the jaw upwards with cold rosewater or cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue; and let the patient bite on it every night so the jaws cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if bleeding from a wound occurs, apply vitriol powder; and if the wound does not heal itself, use a slow-burning cautery (lentiginout), which is good for this purpose; then heal it with another remedy until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it of a thin color or black or hard, such that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer; and if it is spreading towards blanchor, and there is moisture, apply the incisors, and free it with a slender spatula from both sides. And if bleeding continues at your work, apply vitriol powder until it stops. Then return to your work until you remove all pus. Then lift up the swelling with warm rose water or cold water and treat it with other medicines until it is cured.
des apostemes de la gorge	From the abscess of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes boils (godath) come inside the throat which are called 'the two almonds', and they are properly called 'the two almonds'; when you treat them as we have said in the division, if they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and pale color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also because of the bleeding; but leave it until it becomes ripe, and then you will cut or break it open, or it would burst by itself; and if it is white in color again, and the root is fine, prepare the instrument for covering, but first check that the abscess's heat has subsided and been calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his shoulders be in alignment, and open his mouth wide, and the servant takes hold of it between his hands, and presses the tongue beneath the instrument, thus is its shape; and may it be of silver or fine iron as thin as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue to all this instrument, and if you see the abscess, take the hook and poke it into the almond, and pull it up more than you can; and pull anything from the cloth with it, then strike it on the instrument, as follows, which resembles a forceps; and even though the head is curved, one side to the other, and they are very sharp, and made of iron or brass:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the iron with pliers, of which form follows:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the iron with pliers, of which form follows:
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 Then treat a woman with an abscess that is inside the throat, specifically an abscess of small size; and I had pressed her throat closed so tightly that the woman could not exhale through the blocked passage, nor eat or drink, and would have died within a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had to be cut open through two of its passages (nostrils).
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 Therefore, I promptly, thrust into one eye-socket, then pulled it outwards, and also pulled a large piece of bone with it; afterwards, I reset the other socket that was pierced by the nose, opened its mouth and pressed its tongue; next, I thrust the bone back into these abscesses, took a portion of it, and no more blood flowed out except for a little; and thus, the woman's throat was closed off; and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease cutting away from that abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again and filled up the place I had emptied, until it became very large; then I tricked it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus, it stopped growing; and I left those parts, and only God did something with them afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When the arm is drawn back towards the eye and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thick and rounded, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is healed as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not improve, and you see that the abscesses are alleviated, and it is thin, you must cut it; and if it is rounded and not long, it should be collected (or removed); and if it is red, bloody, or black, you must make an incision for it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it (the abscess), according to the manner that I have said, of its bladder and its length, you must make the patient sit facing the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument which we have mentioned above; then stick the onion in the eye, pull it out, and cut it at the places where I have mentioned in the incision of the two apples.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And you must not cover any superfluity that is beyond the natural term; for if you cover more of it, it causes harm to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two anatomies, and cure it until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient fears to cover [it], then you must use an instrument for the cauterization to remove the fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 The manner of the cautery is sharp and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And the patient places his head in your lap, and then you press his tongue to the instrument that we have said or in the chapter of cautery, and hold it with a sharp hot iron, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and use the handle of this instrument, which has the following shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have a hair or oil pot where one puts the medicine, like the scoop of a spoon, and place the instrument on top of all the medicine over the eye; and let the patient lie on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine without it descending to the throat or the nose; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it on the eye for the amount of half an hour, until you see the pus and the inflammation of the medicine are soothed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the sheath over the wound, until the cotton adheres to the eye; and do this repeatedly, until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry for 4 or 5 days. And if you need to restart the cauterization with the medicine, restart it, and after the cauterization drain the pus around the eye with cotton wrapped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and wash it with cold water and heal it with gargarisms until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective by fumigation than by cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take camomile, yarrow, origanum, rue, and wormwood, and assemble them all or some of them in one pot, and place it on a fire to boil; the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and in the pot have one opening covered with fine cloth in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And let it be silver or lead, and let one of the heads be pushed into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is mortified; afterwards, the process often repeats, until the eye dries up, and make sure you do not perform this at the beginning of the abscess's eruption, for many things may occur; and do not do this unless at the decline of an abscess's eruption.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 If this instrument is not present, take a cane and insert an eggshell into the head so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; for the eggshell does not let the vapor harm the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times an arrow or bone lodges in the throat or somewhere else; therefore, you must draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with the whole instrument, so that you see the thing move; and if it does not open and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps this will loosen the thing through vomiting. Or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of cotton, or a radish root, or one morsel of dry bread; tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will stick, and then you will draw it out; and if it does not come out from what we have said, take one instrument made of wood in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it can enter more easily into the throat, and lift the head high; watch that you do not touch the epiglottis, that nothing harms it or push the bone inside; it is better if the patient pushes the instrument, because he can move it or the thing is air; if he pushes down, or pulls it all the way out, the instrument should be pulled out equally until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	the saliva from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 At no time is the saliva medicine, as I said in the division, through the treatment of medicines; and when it does not help, then look at the throat of the patient towards the sun, after you press his tongue with the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the saliva, draw it out with a very small spoon or subtle tweezers that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if that does not work, take a hollow cane, and put it in the patient's throat, then push or heat up the end of the cane and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And let the patient be anointed with water all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a full glass of cold water and open the mouth, pour it in without swallowing, move it around with your hand frequently; and as soon as the saliva feels the water, it will be expelled.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall as we have said, you should fumigate the patient with asafetida, using the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will yield results.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 The manner of fumigation is that you take the pot or one with charcoal inside, and cover it with a cloth pierced in the middle, and put the head of the instrument in it; then pour your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but comes directly to the nose; and now it will flow, and if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times; let the patient endure thirst, eat salted and alkaline food, and drink no water; and afterwards it will be necessary for it to come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the instrument for treating the nostrils is like curved tweezers to enter the throat; and resemble the beak of a syringe, and it should have abrasive limestone so that what it takes, it cannot release; here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many things that appear to be abscesses are, according to what is recalled later in this book from one and another, and they are different in perforation and incision; and it is in two ways that the one resembles itself, and of these that it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second way is for the sores that are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For abscesses of the head are other than those from the foundation, and abscesses in the cartilage are other than those that come at joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And if it is an abscess, it should not be pierced until the swelling is measured according to its completion; and if it is of such kind that it needs to be pierced when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, as abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when an abscess approaches joints and is left surrounded by it, there is a chance that the ligament and nerve of the joint become corrupt, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 For if an abscess is near the main member and you delay perforation until it is ripe, this will harm the main member; or if it is located at the base, piercing it in such a way that it is not yet ripe will result in no benefit, and there should be no perforation of an abscess without completion of digestion, except for one that is located at the base, which cannot penetrate and should be incised and drained to become a fistula and not heal within a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time of perforation of the abscess that is ripe according to its completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the subsiding of the fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the loosening and shrinking of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the perforation sit on a lower place nearer to the abscess, and where it has opened; and the perforation should be along the body length, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, in joints, nerves, arteries, and in all equal places where there is no hair growth.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that break, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 When an abscess is in a charnel (an open grave or pit), it is good to leave the perforation until it has been confirmed through complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it beforehand, the body will flow out with its pus, and it will be filled with much filth; and there is the danger of hardening the lips and suffocating from it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if any abscess that has been pierced according to the width of the body, as required by the limbs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 You must also prepare small abscesses, small wounds; and large abscesses, large wounds, and many cuts according to the similarity of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses that require the key, they should be sealed; when it has become as the napkins, and is dried up, you must do as with babies: and if there are those that have been cut into three angles, and those that are covered like the myrtle leaf, like arm abscesses; and if there are those that make a round incision, and other similar cuts and similar sealing.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 One who has no head, in the manner of an abscess superficially, you must pierce it completely; and when the abscess is large and it encloses a big cavity, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the cavity in that hour, but draw out only a part; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw nothing wrong; do this repeatedly with great care, many times, until the cavity is completely drawn out; likewise for those who are of weak constitution, or women, or small children, or old and frail men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 The sphincter occasionally spasms with the discharge of bile, which may accidentally kill the patient, and you should not worry about it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, beware of this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced the abscess, drain the wound, and check if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is large, bring strips of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess and there is much damage, it is necessary that you insert a strip in each one so that they come against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin and shaved around it, fill it with old cotton or linen gauze without moisture, tie it until the third day; then open it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold water and a linen cloth, wet it, and place on the site repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If bleeding continues during your work, administer treatment and care, and the powders I have mentioned in this book for the muscles or abscesses, and if it is winter, or the muscles or abscesses are very nervous, then place hot tents and damp cloths on them; and if it is summer, and the muscles are fatty, then place damp cloths on them in cold water and oil, or cold water and oil, for up to three days as we have said, and then lance the abscess and drain it, treating it until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	This must be known universally in wound treatments: now I have told you how to proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 For small abscesses on the head, our methods are as follows, similar to those in bags, like the knot of a grape, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that have fat and pus, similar to boils; and those that are hard and stony at the base, without any doubt if the arteries do not go against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of the cut [incision] is that you probe with any instrument that is called "entomissoire", from which the form comes afterwards, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 For if it contains moisture, they drain it by making a long incision.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is drained, they scrape the skin that contains it without leaving any hair, because it returns again if you leave some; then immerse cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; if not, in vinegar and linen, and use it on the wound and leave it until the next day; and those who are delayed will recover.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then continue with the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you are sure that it does not heal over; then treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 If the abscess remains hard with pus, squeeze it according to this shape, longly; and pour out your onions and the scorch from all sides, and put all your care to draw out the puss where it is located; and if the arteries oppose you, do as I told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And do the same with the abscess if it is pus-filled, and in cutting and treating as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And the opening on the abscess pierces and moistens it, it becomes lighter as there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And in some of these abscesses or sores, there is no moisture, and from those I have cut open or opened a sore of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a quartz stone, rough and discolored, and could not be broken; and if one were to cut it with anything, it would make the same wound as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses coming or head, whether those that come at the heads of children and at the roots of ears, they should be opened all the time depending on the case, to make the pus issue; and they are treated as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Often this abscess comes at the neck, under the armpits, and in glands, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and are hard, and are connected to each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And each scrophula is properly inside its own side, like the tumor and abscess of the head, as we have said; and the resemblances of these scrophulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that are malicious and do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In the case that you see it well-positioned in the body, and it resembles the color of the body, and is silent on both sides and is not hard to the touch neither at the neck nor at the artery or duct, and is not swollen; then you must cut through it, and peel off each part, and spread the two lips of the incision, if necessary, as we have said in head abscesses; and pull slowly and carefully to make sure you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and do not use the spatula or lancet too deeply, let the hands not slip, and look not too far ahead, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 If you puncture the vein or artery and it does not let you continue, put vitriol powder into the wound, or some powders that stop blood, and hold the wound closed; leave it until the abscess is calmed down, and the wound becomes soft and starts to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 When the wound is stopped bleeding, return to your work until you finish it; then check if there remain small scrofulas, if so, cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 If there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, you should not cut the scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it hang out without harm; then dress the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, and heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 If you cut the entire scrofula (the swelling), it is necessary that you close the two lips of the wound and sew them now, as there will be no excess remaining due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 It is necessary that you understand to cover the root and draw out pus, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulas that have excess, pierce there where the growth is more open; and pierce as was said before, in a dependent manner, then bring in tents with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply the ointment of healing charcoal until it heals.
de squinance	The patient should lie on his back, with the affected leg raised and supported by a cushion or similar object. Then, using a sharp instrument, make an incision from the groin to the knee, following the natural creases of the thigh. This incision should be wide enough to expose the underlying tissues but not so deep as to injure the femoral artery or veins. After making the incision, carefully remove any necrotic tissue, pus, and other debris from the wound. Once the wound is clean, apply ointment-enriched charcoal to promote healing.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the shape of the throat; but I never saw anyone do it in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinting (squinance), the incision of the throat called "epiglote" should be opened; and it should not be helped by these [people], because all the veins and the passageway for the sickness are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in two mandibles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the passageway of the throat, it should be covered to avoid the danger of strangulation.   (When the sickness is located in the passageway of the throat, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to prevent strangulation.)
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it should be cut beneath three circles or four small incisions across, between the two circles or by the size of the incision according to the thickness of the cartilage; and such a place is suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no cartilage, and the vessels are long in that area.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 If the master is fearful, it must be that he stretches the skin of the throat entirely, then cuts the windpipe until it reaches the trachea; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the thyroid cartilage as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the laryngeal gland that swells when it protrudes through the broken trachea, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound with care and sew up the entire area against the cartilage; then administer medicines that produce healing, until it heals.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi says not to do this until the throat is completely stopped up and the patient has been judged dead, and then let the bird fly away.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then squeeze the epiglottis because the patient cannot clear his throat; and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death; and for this the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, which has passed in three or four days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal it, until it is healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 A maiden took the knife and thrust it into her throat, piercing part of the windpipe; and I was called to heal her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I found the wound and saw the blood coming out of it, and knew that she did not have any vein or conduit except for her throat, and the wind was going through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and healed it until it was healed; but the maiden had no fever except for her voice being hoarse, and she recovered afterwards; therefore I say that in such a situation of the epiglottis one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	from the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large one with a bluish color, and it occurs mainly in women; and it is according to two ways: natural and accidental; where the natural one has no device.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accidental one is according to two ways, of which one resembles fatty tissue, and the other way resembles an abscess that comes from us due to arteries; there should be fear, and it should not be operated on except in the case of a small one, and it must be proved and sought through all the opening: if you find it as hard as fat, and does not open in any way, strike it like one strikes fat, and draw it out completely, if there is anything; and closely surround it, and cure it as needed until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	We have found that... (Incomplete sentence due to missing text)
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways of ours are, which I will tell all similarities; and now it is necessary that I say all the differences between notch and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is heat and fever lasting, until the boils have passed and the porridge is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 The notch has no heat, fever, or pain, and contains the pus, which is its own sac and is like the color of the body, and starts similarly to an abscess, and becomes large; and they are similar in two ways, either fatty or moist, and they have much color as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the cure of the newt, that you examine and test first all the instrument which is called "entromissoire", according to its form or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 The method of the incision of abscesses for us is that you take a more moist place than you find in the abscess and turn your fingers little by little until you feel that the knife has pierced the core, then it should be according to the size of the abscess; then separate the edge, and pay attention so as not to let it burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs out from the abscess and colors it, treat it as I have said for other abscesses; and if afterwards no more moisture comes out, know that it is filled with pus, then make a cross-shaped incision, grasp it with forceps, gently scrape it lightly from both sides and pull the cotte where it lies that you draw it cleanly with the thread; and if you cannot draw it cleanly, then pull it apart piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 If nothing remains, the pus will return many times; and if a small amount remains and does not bother you, treat the wound with certain corrosive powders, hold the wound closed, put warm soothing things on the abscess, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the pus is large, cut two lips of the wound, and cure it with whatever helps to heal flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats against you or otherwise is opposed to you, or if you hasten and employ the leech of vitriol crushed, let it lie for 2 or 3 days until the wound heals, and let the boil of blood rest; then return to cover what has remained unhealed.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Behold the shapes of surgical instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three cross-shaped ones called 'albaret', and one called 'breb', and they also come in three forms: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses with fistulae; and they are similar to needles used for sewing sacks, and they are of citron reed, iron, or silver, and the ones that are yellow are more valuable, and are more experienced in dealing with black plugs for encircling fistula sores; and they come in three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The shapes of the tumors are much alike, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and some tumors have two bumps of three types; and some tumors have three bumps, and are also of three types; and some tumors have two bumps, and tumors with only one bump, and they are also of three types; and all this is necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The heads of these things that are cut are sharp, and those who do not cut it only from one side, from which the vein or nerve is not struck; and these intrusive things are replied in manacles so that the patient does not feel it at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three types: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they are not used anywhere except in charnut places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and bellies, and in similar places; and sometimes another instrument is made small, resembling fistula scissors, according to this form, for letting blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed at times on the place where wounds heal quickly from veins and arteries, and sometimes round in this large shape.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 At times the breasts of some men swell when they begin to corrupt, until they seem like female breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, should do so according to this form of this line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Then cut the fat, apply medicine to the wound made of charred linen, then bring together the two lips of the wound in stitches, and cure it until it is healed; and if the breast sinks downward due to its size, as happens with women, fold it into two folds, above each other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from line b to line g; then cut the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and introduce what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not complete because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then fill the wound with cotton wetted in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it digests the remaining fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	From abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are handled as hard scrofulas where there are coats and if it contains moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b up to the line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the boil that is in the abscess is emptied, use old cotton on the wound and leave it until another day, then remove all the cotton, and apply ointment afterwards until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, cut it as we have said in the incisions of scrofula, and if the wound boils again, apply a cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 If the artery is wide and the skin above it thickens repeatedly, abscesses occur, and this happens with a swollen vein and abscess; and if one knows it by the artery, the abscess is long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, it feels tight; and when it is due to the vein, it appears round and protruding; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the shoulders and angles, near the neck, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.
