Therefore, it is necessary to remove the iron cure, and he who has a head injury should also be treated likewise, and in the case of an inflammation of the artery, make an incision through the skin along its length; then open the abdomen carefully, and separate the artery from the lining, exposing it completely; then insert a needle beneath it, and pierce it all the way to the other side, and bind the artery with a double thread as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples; then press down on the gap between the two bands until the injury disappears, and remove the pus; then apply the cure of bow saw, until the ligament breaks; then treat the area with liniment until it is healed; and if the injury is due to a vein wound, dye your hand with what you can from the pus, then insert a needle beneath the area you hold, pierce it, and have thread there so you can pull it out from the other side; then tie the pus, as I said, or a ligament of one of the two bands with the thread; and if you doubt that the threads do not protrude, insert another needle all along the thread beneath the wound of the first needle, and bind the threads in four parts; then cut the pus so it disappears, then cut the excess fat and leave what is tied; then apply a damp cloth in wine and oil, then apply treatments of tenting and liniment until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses from nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As in the artery and vein come abscesses, so do abscesses of nerves when they are wounded or by excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this happens more often in the shoulders and elbows, and in all joints where there are joints, and it is the large abscesses, and its color resembles the body's color, and it is found in many conditions causing pain; and when it is stretched outward, the patient feels pain, and it is not entirely within the body, but under the skin; and it spreads well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, neither down nor up, and one who is in joints should not be covered by iron: perhaps contraction will occur; and one who is in the head or forehead, make the skin thin.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and strike its root; if it is large, squeeze it at the edge and peel off the skin, then break the bone and stitch up the wound until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	hanging large growths
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 At times, there occurs in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "funge," resembling mushrooms, and the roots are subtle, and the heads are large; and among them there are small ones and very large ones; and I have seen men who had two or more bellies that resembled mushrooms more than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had a thin root, and were cut open, and ran moisture constantly.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I weighed it and found one weighing eighteen ounces, the other six, and the wound in the incision is such that you look at it if the patient is moist, and the color of the arrowhead is white and moist with a thin root; then grip the spatula large, and the fire cautery be present.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For in the thigh, there often comes too great displacement of blood, if it escapes, then hurry to cauterize; and if you see the patient anxious and afraid of the iron incision, take a well-made thread, tie it around the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; then tighten it, and do not stop tightening the thread until it stops the flow of blood, and causes pain; and if the roots are large, be careful to cauterize in the same way due to the belly, but you can easily cauterize half of it, then cauterize where it has not returned; then cure the wound, and be sure to not cauterize the flesh that is of a dark color, poor sensation, and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an enlarged abscess, and I will come to the treatment of scrofula afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the buttock (or anus) is open/exposed
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of the boil comes through a cautery of a wound or a split in the sifac (a surgical instrument), and it is on the belly and among some of the buboes (swellings), as happens in other routes, or from blood that pours out of veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness; and if it comes through the sifac route and the exit of the stool, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body and is a light thing without pain, and open with multiple exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when it is pressed with the fingers if it shrinks back, and then returns, and possibly if it is hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and by great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing and open wide when you press it with your hand, do not constrict it; and if it is due to blood, then the abscesses are large and hard, and filled according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work is such that you look to see whether the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 You must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For it causes fear and doubt, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, you must command the patient to empty his anus, extend himself straight, then bend all around the feces; then command him to bear down between your hands, then go around the area that you have signaled with the spatula, then stretch half of the abscess above with a large spoon; then tie it tightly with a strong thread or a strong cord and let the nose be pulled away from the thread; then open the stretched abscess over the thread and insert your finger, looking for the intestine; if you find it caught in the thread, release it, push the intestine to the outside of the abdomen; and if you find the bowel, grab it with the spoon and cut off the excess; and if the artery or vein oppose you, go gently, then return to your work and take two needles and insert two fine threads, and place them around what you have made in a cross shape that you pierce; then press the abscess in four parts above the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the area alone until it dries up, and separate the dead flesh by itself; or cut it when it is subtle and can be pushed through, then cure what is necessary, and close the abscess as we have said; and drain the pus or moisture that you find, then cure the area.
dou chancre	two boils
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We said in the previous division the resemblances of boils and how one should treat them with medicine, and how to avoid the iron cure; and we say that a boil starts in the groin, and great caution is required in its treatment, and the ancients said that when boils are in a place where it can be shaved as in boils that are on the breasts or in the thighs, and in similar places, one should remove them entirely at their beginning; and when they are large and old, it should not be approached because I never knew anyone to heal it; nor has anyone healed it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when in a place where it can be removed as we have said, is that you purge the patient once with black bile; then make him urinate if he has manifest fullness, then cut the patient one boin (a small knife) to perform the operation; then throw down your oncines (bandages or poultices) or boil, and shave off all the hair from all parts, and remove all the flesh without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and be careful to anoint the place with your hand or something, and if the discharge of blood opposes the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood is coagulated; then cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
de ydropisie	Of hydropisy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have said in the division that the resemblances of edema are similar to idropisie; and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure made by medicine, and that which is cured by iron: only this is exuded; no iron should be used in these two resemblances: namely tympanites and yposarche, for it is a fatal thing; therefore, when you treat this edema-like condition called "eclites" with medicine, if the cure does not work, observe whether the patient is weak or has other diseases besides edema, such as dropsy of the belly and similar things; no iron should be used because there is doubt; however, if you see the patient to have strong constitution and having only edema alone, who is neither too thin nor too old, then you must work in this way: lift the patient upright on your hands, and the attendants press the belly towards the lowest part of the back, then take the pointed spatula according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut through the second part.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And let it be incised through the second part. It should not be so deep as to reach the intestine when punctured, and it must not be pierced; then examine if the hernia is directed towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision below the third rib on the left side of the waist; and if it is due to liver disease, the incision should be to the left of the third rib; and if it is due to swelling, it should be to the right. The patient should not lie down on the incision so that excessive fluid does not flow to that weak place; then puncture the skin with an instrument, push it, and move your hand along the entire spatula between the skin and the hernia sac as when peeling an apple of about the size of a nail or inwards around it; then pierce the hernia sac until the spatula reaches the watery area (the fluid), which is the location of the hernia, then pull it out, and insert the instrument in its form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And it resembles a silver-thin chain, and is of silver or light gold, and at its bottom part, there are three holes; and on one side, two holes; and one on the other; and the head of the shoulder is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes carve into a feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 Above the arm is the elbow, so that when the instrument comes to the point, now push it on the instrument; empty then either half or one third, for if you empty too much at that time, perhaps the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit by the weapon, or he will faint, or approach death; but empty according to its strength and according to what the conditions of its virtue indicate in the patient and his pulse; then draw the instrument and hold the point, and it is held now by the caution that stops the wound that I have spoken about, which you pierce in this way; then return the instrument the next day if you see the patient suffering from it, and draw a small amount of fluid; do this every day, and be careful not to let him keep too much fluid but just a little.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient's condition and leave him with moisture, cure him by burial or hot sand, by much sweat or bath and in the sun, anoint him with wine; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healthy, cauterize the stomach, liver, and spleen after the removal of the moisture, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of stopping the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes children are born without testicles or their testicles are small or not in the correct place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 When it is necessary to pierce through an abscess with a very thin needle according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 Then put the testicle of thin lead into the abscess, tie it and hold it for three or four days until he wishes to urinate, then remove the lead, let him urinate, and then replace it; and in case there is no need to do so, as the urine that comes out does not close the opening.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 The patient with a small putrid sore should be treated with a cloth of plaster, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those who do not have the sore in their place are bleeding, for no one is born with a sore on the head of the penis, therefore they cannot urinate before lifting their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the marris, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of work is that the patient lies supine on their back, their head should be slightly elevated and the neck similarly to the thickness of a feather, so that the patient's chin touches their chest, as required; and guard against bleeding which occurs frequently, and if it happens, stop it by pressing the area that is bleeding, and treat the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	of boils on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often this albathion appears in the penis, and it is an appearance of ugly genital warts; and there are both malignant and non-malignant ones; you should take them one by one with a subtle instrument, cut and clean all of them, then put cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment on top; then treat it with the ointment diafinicon until it heals.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the anus is infected with pus-like color and discharge, then you must apply fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have cauterized it, and the anus is on the side of the penis, with parts inside the skin and parts outside, you must first remove the infected anus that is inside. And when it has been removed, heal the part that remains outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you are treating it together, the genitals of the penis are not always certain that they will not be perforated; and blackness and corruption come into the penis and around it; if it is necessary to remove all that is black and corrupted, then lay it on a plaster of honey and flour made from pumpkin shells and sometimes, then treat it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cautery and its aid are assembled together: that is to say, for the removal of blood and corruption; and if the genitals of the penis are corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you pass or lead a pipe from the penis, and make the patient urinate; and when the hairs reach the tip of the penis, which occurs in those who have not been circumcised, or it occurs due to injury or abscess, then it is necessary to shave it with an instrument having fine hairs, until the ligaments are loosened, and the genitals of the penis are delivered from all sides; and if this is difficult to speak about, it is necessary to shave it at the spatula a little distance from the tip of the penis and the skin; then separate them carefully, and put a thin linen cloth dampened with cold water between them, which should not come apart immediately.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not just a cutting like other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own will and specifically on infants, it is necessary to make the best and easiest work for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not circumcise their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the greater part of masters and saints who perform circumcision around day one, and for forces, and in all cases with a novacule; however, it is feared because there are two layers, and by chance if one above is cut, the one below may remain.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now it should be covered, and the pain is doubled; and at the amputation which is deep in the limb, there is no assurance of the point of the member; and during the amputation of the nail, by chance the iron may slip, and spoil the work, and many times it is not necessary for amputation, and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	In amputation which is done with the forceps, I have found the advantage of the experiment, because the forceps cut evenly both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you press your hand, you should cut it evenly all around; but the thread should be well tied around the skin; and the method of the first work is such that you make the child understand if he can, that you tie the thread only around the rod, and then let him rest in every way that you can; afterwards, let him stand upright between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them or any tools; then press your hand onto the rod and blow or pull, and draw it up until the head of the rod is in; then clean it well of the accumulated filth, then tie a suture made of double thread, then tie it underneath the skin to the other suture; and hold it with the second suture at the pouch and the index finger, and strike between the two sutures, then remove the thread as quickly as possible and pull the head of the rod; then let the blood come out freely as it wishes, because this is the discharge; and put powder on top and more powder stick with a soft egg yolk mixed with rosewater, boiled and finely ground oil of roses, and leave it on until the next day, and treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for cleansing is as follows: the two heads should be tender and sharp, and their heads should be as large as a hand equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in the incision of the womb is when the bowels inside are cut; therefore it is necessary that you stretch it with your nail so that the opening resembles an abscess, and then press it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your nail, grasp it with forceps, and then press.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they exceed three days, and what is beneath the scrotum swells, leave it until the abscesses are appeased and gently incise the skin; then press as you can move it, and be careful of the part of the scrotum, which will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, treat the limb with things buried in a wound with the powder we have mentioned or how to treat wounds with powders, and if you press too hard, it will go upwards, but it will not harm; therefore, treat it as we have said until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to a stone, or congealed blood, or pus, or frozen semen, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not dislodged, and you see that it is retained because of the stone which is in the bladder or urethra, then you must make the patient bend over their knees; put their feet on the back, extend their abdomen from the part above the lower back, and restrain the patient as much as they can; and then the lower part of the bladder to the expression of the stone above is compressed, so that the urine is dislodged; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, you must administer extraction with all the instruments called "syringe", of which this is the form: and it should be made of thin silver and lightweight feather-shaped head, like a bird's pen; and the tube should be one and a half palms long and subtle at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the method of discharge of urine is that you take a doubled thread, tie it to the tip of a cotton or wool swab, and push the swab's tip through the syringe; then pull off the excess thread and push it up to the tip of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a chair, and anoint the bladder and penis with oil moistened with oil from olives and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis over towards the belly; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and make the patient feel as if he is about to void into an empty container, and this is not done according to this order unless because the conduit through which it goes is twisted; then tie the thread to the entire swab, and the urine will follow the swab, then remove it forcefully, and straighten the urine; then repeat the syringe until the bladder is empty, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorching or blood comes into the bladder, or pus is collected there, and you see it distill liquids and medications, do with all the equipment that is called "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed and has three openings: two of them, and one from the other side, as you see; and the medicines are placed in such a way that they stop the worm without addition, if it can draw out moisture, and push when needed; and when you want to expel your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the catheter into the moisture, and pull on the string attached to it; if you pull out the moisture with the catheter, then forcefully push the string back in; the moisture will enter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle clister for filling the bladder: thus it is.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is made of silver or copper, and the head [of the shoulder] is higher; underneath at the chest or ligaments falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put moisture in it which you have prepared to moisten the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts using a good thread double, heat the moistened wool over fire; then push the head of the clistere into the rod [arrow], then hold your hand above the bladder with all the moisture facing towards it until the patient feels that the moistened wool has reached the bladder; if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment and make a circle, puncture it roundly; then push a strong thread into these holes, assemble the circle like a drum, put inside it what you wish of oil and moisture and water, seal it in an instrument; and perform as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand firmly until the moistened wool reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division about the ways of stone, and extraction combined with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone embedded in the flesh, and all the signs, and when to operate on it by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the member; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	The stone embedded in the bladder often happens to children, and this is a sign that the urine jumps from the bladder like urine in its subtlety; it opens a hole, and makes the patient's member swell, and he pees many times, then strangles himself; and many foundations occur due to these jumps; and it is easy for children to heal until they are 4 years old, but it is severe in adults, and it is in the middle range for those who are between youth and old age; and it is easier to cure those who have large stones than those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema, in order to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes blocks inquiries into the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet, and turn them over and move them downward, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and moves upward occasionally; then have him sit with his hands between your hands, and his hands should be below his hips, so that the bladder is completely declining downwards; then press and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall upon touching all around, then anoint your right hand with oil, if the patient is a child, or use soap, if the patient is an adult male; and push in its foundation, touch the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, press it towards the neck of the bladder; then press in your finger, and push it out at the place where you intend to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the scrotum in the part where the cutting is done; then insert the spatula covering it, which is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And it should be made between the one who is between the eyelids and the socket base, not at the medial canthus but along the outer side of the left eye; and it should be straight across the bridge, and your fingers should be close to or against the socket, and the incision should be wide enough to allow easy removal, but narrow within, according to the size of the stone, not too large; in case the finger that is against the socket presses on the stone, causing it to jump out without effort; and know that there is a stone where there are angles or margins, and it should be carefully removed; and if it is soft like a bean and round, whose issue is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 If it has angles or margins, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, you must pull it up with forceps that are like a lime with a narrow handle, to press the stone so that it does not escape; or push something sharp and curved under it from above; and if you cannot extract it in this way, you can drill a small hole using a burr, and draw out the stone with tweezers; and if there is more than one stone, pull out the largest first, then cut along its side, then remove it, and the smaller ones after.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, you must make a larger incision.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 The following happen to the patient: either he dies or urine comes forth where the joints cannot be sutured; but nevertheless try to drain it, or break with pliers, as long as you draw it in pieces; and when you have completed your work, fill the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, bind it, and put on it a damp cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and cold rose water and cold water to cool the abscess; then resolve the patient on his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen the bandage, clean the wound very well with oil and water, then treat it with ointment of defyacinicon and basilicon until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 If abscesses and corrosions come into the wound and congealment of blood in the bladder occurs, causing urine to be retained, which is known to cause a dangerous situation without passing urine; then you must squeeze your hand into the wound, draw out that blood, because if it remains, it will cause the bladder to burst and leak; lift up the wound from pus, pus and moisture, and help in every way that you know, until it heals; and it is necessary that all the wounds that you treat, you tie the two legs together, and mix the medicines on the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 If the wound is small and is from the penis and pierced with a probe, and urine cannot be released; then treat it as I say below: cut it several times, and make an incision in order to excuse the urinary passage due to this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already experienced this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod of this form and sharpened at four angles on one point:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take the thread and tie it around the shaft of the arrow beneath the stone, so that it cannot return into the bladder; then gently push the awl into the shaft of the arrow; then turn the awl towards your hand in the shaft little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side; soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is within the shaft.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is broken and jumps with the urine, the patient is cured; but if you cannot do this for some reason that prevents it, tie the thread beneath the stone and another above, then push the shaft towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; and treat it until it heals.
de la piere des femmes	Of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone appears in women, and if it ever occurs, it is a great grief for the woman, and it is forbidden for four reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows herself well enough to be examined by mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is that sometimes it cannot be found a woman well skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is deeper than that of the man, which requires a more profound incision and great fear it brings about. If you find yourself in need of such, it is necessary to take a midwife who knows, and if one cannot be found, then cast a subtle doubt; and present a wise woman in the matters of women's life, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to perform the incision of the stone; and observe very well that the woman is a virgin: thereupon, she must push with her hand or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she must restrain it beneath her hand, and you command her to push with her hand or with the patient, and press her left hand upon the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If it is found, you should move it gently from the entrance of the bladder all the way down to the root of the thigh, until it reaches the root of the hip; then strike above the hip on the bone at the root of the thigh against the point where it is moved, so that you feel the bone in that area; and do not move your finger above or below the bone, and make a small incision; then push the flesh into the incision, if you feel the bone closely seal the wound so that the bone can protrude, and know that there are many kinds of bones: namely, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and those with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 Know the appearances to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the wound opens without treatment, place pulverized vitriol on it and hold for an hour until it stops bleeding; then return to your work when the stone is loose, and have instruments as I told you for removing the stone from men to assist in your work; and if the wound opens again and it is an artery that has been cut, put powder on the place and bind with tent-cloths and bandages, do not touch it again, and leave the stone and do not draw it out, because the patient may die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the heat of the blood has subsided and the swelling has decreased, return to your work while the stone remains hard.
de hernie carnouse	Of a carnous hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aqueous is not otherwise called an accumulation of moisture or white chyle, which is beneath the bladder, containing the egg; and it is called "chyle," and sometimes it is properly in the egg's membrane, if one thinks that it is another egg; and it is the skin of the bladder between the white chyle we have mentioned; and this does not happen except when there is an empty space.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the growth of this aqueous is due to weakness that comes from the bladder, and that matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes percussion comes on the cheeks, and this moisture appears in many colors: it can be declining to yellow, or without redness, black, white, or watery whitish; and this happens more often; these are signs for recognizing this assembly because if it is as white as we said, it is a sign of an abscess, the pouch is long like an egg, and do not open the cheeks because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the very cloth (bandage), it is thought that the abscess has been reborn with part of the egg; and if the moisture is between the skin and the subcutaneous tissue, one can feel it clearly; therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, probe thoroughly, so that you may discern its form, as described earlier.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, judge what is inside through the intruder.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we treat it with iron (cautery), the patient should be anesthetized to the best of our power and as much as his body allows; then lie on his back, on a small raised object, and place many cloths beneath him; then lie on his left side, and command the assistant to stand on the right side, and extend the arm from which the skin of the shoulder is affected; then take the spatula (tweezers), and cut the skin between them along its length, down to the subcutaneous tissue, and cut it delicately as far as the white fat, and peel it carefully according to our ability; then pierce the subcutaneous tissue with a needle full of water and drain all the water, and place a dressing on it; and touch only the subcutaneous tissue but not the skin; chop the entire affected area delicately into pieces, so that if you do not do this carefully, the water will return; and if the egg bursts during your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the subcutaneous tissue treatment; then bring together the two folds of skin at the shoulder joint into a suture, and treat the wound as one would other wounds until it heals.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	If the egg (fetus) is corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to tie the vessels that are suspended, fearing the release of blood; next, cut the cord entirely and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if an ulcer is assembled in two parts together, know that these are the branches; if you cut off the other part as you did the first equally, then draw out the blood, and put moistened linen in oil of roses into the wound; and put another moistened linen in wine and oil, and put two sacks over it, and bind it all with a cord according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take the two sacks and use them with dampened linen according to this appearance and sew them together into a collar for the arm, one of the heads taking up the base until the back, and the other at the handle part; and the other two heads above the two angles, and hold all together in the buckle of the bandage; and sometimes is the branch of cautery used instead of iron cutting, and it is that you take the pointed cautery, cut the skin of the hairs, and heat it as we have said, so that the white pus containing the ulcer is exposed; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce the white pus with holes, and scrape off the cautery hot.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And the cup in all ways that you can, as long as you are heating it; and ensure that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more salve (or save); and carefully guard against the leakage of blood, and be aware that the surgeries of incision; and if anything prevents you, or abscesses or the leakage of blood or something else, cure what prevents you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 If the patient is afraid and does not want to endure this work due to its horrifying nature, you should perform perforation, as I have told you; and it is that when you are certain by the signs we have said that ramice aquouse is present, you should make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below with a spatula-like tool, long along the body; and let the perforation be wide so that all the pus can flow out; then put cotton over the area, hold it in place, and allow the remaining pus to drain, then heal until the wound is healed; if the white cloth does not stop the pus from coming out through the opening of the wound, you should insert a reed or instrument used to treat dropsy, as the shape is described earlier; enlarge the opening of the wound, and know that the pus will return, and it will be collected after 6 months or more, and when it is collected as mentioned before, the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the tonsils
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the treatment of this condition, there is fear in many positions, so it seems to me that one should not move [the patient]; and I will tell you the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Then, many abscesses come from bodies or heads; this happens often.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 It is by excessive sour and hot air that is spread through the kidneys or from impact; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; there is no pain found, and it is a painful abscess; and sometimes an abscess becomes swollen due to fear or stones, and of this color, and occasionally it comes from the artery or the inflammation of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is from the artery, it can be known by the hot position of the abscess when pressed with hands; and you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 One who is inflamed by the swelling of a vein is known by his disposition at the expression of the touch on the fingers; and he can well make an incision on this likeness, and on other things; it is that you cut the bone's core, then the yolk is above, and the white part is split, and release the suspensioner from all parts of the yolk.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the yolk is already solid with these things born, then you must draw the yolk and cut it; if it is hard at the white part or in that which is inside the vessels, you must release all of the tender part and cut it sharply.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the bladder is at the back, you should strike it all, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, you should apply the wound with damp wool in oil of roses and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the tonsils
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess enveloped by an envelopment resembling a boil, with the softening of the bones, and the patient moves hardly when he goes; and the cure for this disease is very dangerous as described above, and nevertheless we will tell you its work according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 You must make the patient sit on the elevated seat, then push the suspension device for the eyes downward towards your hands, to all the instruments near the penis, and touch them with the master's hands and stretch them out properly; then you should cut a wide slit in the sphincter muscle in front of the vessels, until they are exposed, and then scrape from both sides, as we have said in the extraction of arteries in temples; then insert a double-threaded needle and sew it to the first place where the vein appears, and tie it straight to the other end; then you should pierce everything straightly according to the length of the body, and draw out corrupt matter; then heal the wound as with other bowels, so that no vessel leaks the fluid from one eye; for this there is no harm. If all vessels appear, you must drain both eyes; so that the eyes do not lose their fluids due to the incision of the vessels, and dry up and cannot be healed.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the sinus (or sinew)
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The occurrence of this ailment is due to a section that opens suddenly or an extension on the abdomen in the area of the intestines; because the intestines descend from that rupture towards one of the kidneys. This rupture can be either sudden or due to extension, and these two types come about by various causes: either through impact, jump, fall, lifting heavy objects, or similar things. The signs that it is an extension of the rupture are that it occurs gradually over a long time and does not happen suddenly; and the abscesses remain equal up to the full extent, because the rupture follows the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs when it is of the section of the fracture, that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear variously under the skin near, and this is because of the issue of the intestines and the body turning away from the fracture.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines protrude through the circle, and it is retained, causing great pain to suffer by the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, there is fear, so it is fitting to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	 The method of treatment is that you instruct the patient to manipulate the intestine back into its place within the wound if it can be returned; then press on the neck between your hands, and lift the legs; then hold the kidney above, and chop all the skin of the kidneys with long strokes; then push in the fingers of the groin, as many as needed to open the wound, and ensure they are large enough for the intestine to pass through; then scrape the rupture that is under the kidney skin until the white rupture becomes completely exposed on all sides; then insert your index finger into the area between the white rupture beneath the kidney skin, between the second and third ruptures, and detach what is behind the kidney, and between the second ruptures; and then move your hand to the right of the kidney within the rupture, and lift the white rupture towards your left hand, and remove the kidney away from the entire rupture towards the groin; and instruct the assistant to stretch the kidney upwards, and detach what is in front behind the attachment; and check with your fingers if there is any of the intestine entwined or white rupture hardened, and if you find anything, push it to the abdomen beneath; then take a needle with a thick thread made from ten threads, and insert it into the rear part of the rupture, which is behind the kidney skin, followed by the tail, then sew the threads that appear, as many as needed until there are four threads; then arrange them in the form of a cross, and tie the rupture, as we have previously mentioned beneath the kidney skin, with a strong ligature of two fingers wide; then wind the threads around the rupture, ensuring no vassals who feed it can enter it, unless pus comes out from the wound; and place the ligature in its original position along the length of the first ligature, and after these two ligatures leave a large gap beneath the kidney, equal to one finger; and after this, leave the rest according to the round shape that the kidney bears; then chop in the area that is behind the kidney skin, until it softens, and bores, as we have previously mentioned above; then bring moistened linen in oil to the wounds, and place it there, and bring the ligature we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes white boils are cauterized as we have said, after incision, out of fear of the discharge of blood.
