Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 For this often occurs and let the ligament be loose until it falls by itself; and if it delays in falling, warm it with hot water, and apply what has been said to it, until it falls; then treat the wound with another cure until it heals completely.
de hernie carnouse	Of a carnous hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is made like a graft which is attached to the bone, in this manner you bind the vessels, above the wound lightly beneath; then cut through the middle, and treat the abscess of those who work on it, until the vessels fall; and heal it as we have said, until it heals.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 Sometimes it comes to rupture in the anus, as we have said, and open the area; and do not remove any of the intestines from the anus, and if some are removed, it is a mistake, and repair it every hour; and even if it remains too long in this place, the wound or syphilis grows, until the intestines are being removed; and this happens due to the extension of syphilis which is in the anus, as we have said, because it is extended, then it becomes softened and inflamed the area and opens; and the healing is by cautery as we have said before; and sometimes it is healed by iron in this manner: and the patient lies prone on his back between your hands, then cut the swollen anus with a large knife according to the size of three fingers; and then draw out the syphilis which is underneath the skin that sticks, then take the rail and place it on the visible syphilis area; and press the full belly, then sew the two visible parts of the syphilis to the head of the rail, and sew one and the other; then draw out the head of the rail, and do not cover or extend the syphilis or any other thing, as I have told you in the cure of intestinal graft; then heal by the wound treatment.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the threads, if they bleed and heal the wound, let it be until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The ointment is confined and has no appearance in the wound, and cauteries are made here and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	Of the softening of the skin around the eyes
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin around the eyes becomes soft in some men, because the glands within are softened and there is pus to see; and when it is observed that it needs to be cured, it is necessary to make the patient lie on his back, and to strike the softened skin with the natural skin; then bring together the two lips at a stitch, and if you see, sew the excess of the softened skin at three or four stitches firmly; then strike between the stitches, and let the cure be as for other wounds, until it is healed, and stitch the threads.
dou chastrement	When struck with a blow
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 Know that castrations are considered sinful in our law, and for that reason I will not speak of it in this book; however, it is necessary to know about it in two ways: the first is that the mirrors in castration respond when asked, and it is cured in castration; and the second, because we often need castration of certain animals to help us, such as bulls, sheep, goats, and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 Therefore, castrations are performed in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the one we do by attraction, let us sit the beast in hot water until its joints are softened and relaxed; then hold it firmly with your hand, until it is set and you no longer feel any movement.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 For the branding of size: it is necessary that you dye the beast, and press the skin of the joints with your left hand, then tie the harness, and strike on each one as it calls for it, when you have thoroughly scorched them; leave a small amount of fat and delicate fat which is on the vessels; and this kind of branding is more reliable than the one made by attraction, because at the attraction sometimes there remains something of the joints, so that the beast desires lewdness; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	The translation for "des hermofrodites" in this context would be "hermaphrodites". This term refers to individuals with both male and female sexual characteristics or reproductive organs. In medieval times, such individuals were often considered abnormal or even monstrous by some societies due to their ambiguous gender identity.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 Hermaphroditism is according to two ways in men: one is when there is an opening between the two coccyxes as in the figure of a woman's nature, where it has hair, and sometimes it flows urine inside the court.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other way is in women, who have growth on top like a penis and two coccyxes.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 The cure for a man and a woman is that you cover the adjacent wounds all over, and treat them like other wounds; in the second way, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of the coccyx, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	Of the torture
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 Tumor is an adjacent wound on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as big as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 It is necessary that you dip the excess of the tentigen at your hand or with an oncyon, and strike it lightly; and do not go too deep, so as to avoid bleeding; then treat it with another remedy until it heals; and at another place where a boil arises at the mouth of the marsh, and the bump, and possibly a hole forms, and resembles a cow's teat, and for this reason they call it the old disease "kowe.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 If it is necessary that you strike (the abscess), as we have said, and treat it until it heals.
de erratique	Of the eructation
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 An abscess is erratic when the nature of a woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; it can be natural by birth or accidental due to disease; or it can be due to a swelling caused by hot or thick pus, and is formed in the marsh or the costez (sides) or below, and cannot be conceived, or the child born, and possibly flowers (pus) are produced; and recognition of these things is by observing the state of the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the stoppage is close to appearing, it may be with your hand or eye.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 If the swelling is subtle and near the liver, hasten to do this: place your index fingers together, let the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then form the two livers, while the subtle swelling is round and over the liver; then take wool and moisten it in oil, and place it on the area, and let the woman rest for each day so she cannot congeal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the swelling is hard and large, it is necessary that you cut into it with a knife resembling a mirror leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the swelling is of pus, suspend it in onion juice and cut it off; have medicines that stop blood, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with a lot of egg; then bring a wide-mouthed straw, so the wound cannot congeal; and thus be long, and bring a tent of dry linen; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when during childbirth snow comes, it should be covered in this way, unless the abscess becomes aggravated.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For an aggravated abscess that occurs during childbirth, no action should be taken.
des emorroides	Emorroidal lesions
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that usually require cautery, and when hemorrhoids become old, they turn into piles; and we have said in the division their similarities, their signs, and I will say here those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and piles, when they appear in the fullness of birth and cannot be felt, are not cured by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those at the mouth of the birth canal, which can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 Therefore, you should place the woman in a cold house, then attach the iron to the roots, and apply powdered medicines that restrict blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then keep her feet exposed for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, have her sit in a decoction of sumac, apple bark, holly, and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and egg white, and apply it as a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If it does not, make bladders full of air on the back and at the breasts without piercing them; then take linen, wet it in juice of plantain or elder with old wine, and apply it at the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess rests, if you heal the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to a rough crust, if it must be covered as I have said, then heal it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	abscesses in the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many kinds of abscess come in marriage (i.e., the female genital area), such as scrofula and pus-filled abscesses, herpes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 Therefore I must tell about the hot abscess that comes in the marriage area (i.e., genitalia) in this treatise; it is not one of those that adhere to the bowel (perianal abscesses); and if you wish to know the work with iron, observe whether the abscess is acute at the beginning of its coming, full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Therefore, do not hasten to pierce, but let it heal as the pain subsides; and then make the patient sit on a chair, and provide him with two small chairs or a stool where he can lean, and support his back and place his feet at the sides of each footrest; his knees should be spread apart, and put his arms beneath his thighs and tie them firmly with a good rope; then approach the patient from his right side, and bring the instrument used to open the mouth of the anus, so that the shape follows; and it is necessary that when you see the instrument brought forward, you pierce the rectum first to know the depth of the anus, so that what enters the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; if the instrument is large, it is necessary to cover the depth of the anus with cloths so that the instrument does not harm; and it is necessary that you put the nozzle of the instrument above, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess opens, and one touches it with soft hand, it must be covered with lard, using a spatula; and when the boil is emptied, you should put woven cloths moistened in oil rose or green dry oil into the wound; place the cloth further into the wound to the full depth of the flesh, then over the flesh and the clean linen cloth moisten with vinegar or malmsey wine soaked; then cure for two days with ointment following this procedure until it is healed; and sometimes lift the flesh and the wound by clysters of vinegar and honey, and then vinegar or long-cooked roots of lilies and Aristolochia are used; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is healed over with a scar, you must be careful not to burn it with iron, but treat it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 Firstly, the maid must recognize the figure of natural childbirth, and signs to watch out for when you see a woman in labor, and desiring to bear a child: then hasten the birth of the child; then know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the afterbirth comes out with the head, and the second one follows it; and when you see these signs, you must gently press on her belly so that the child comes quickly; for when it descends toward its head, it is accompanied by the afterbirth, and the afterbirth is discarded from its superfluidities through good cleansing; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 It sometimes happens that something falls upon the feet, and the body or the shoulders, or the hands, or it falls upon the abdomen, or the head, and turns by chance around the neck, and in other evil ways; therefore it is necessary for the physician that she be wise and skilled in such matters, and warn of errors and deceptions, and I will show you all the figures as to how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes out over its head naturally and the woman gives birth painfully, and her strength is weak, make her sit on a saddle or have other women hold her; anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, then the midwife should insert a small spatula of this shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 And split the afterbirth, and strike at its edge with a fingernail until the moist thing that is within comes forth; and take hold of the woman's abdomen as the child descends, and if it does not descend, you must cleanse the woman with muscillaige of fenugreek with oil of cumin; then make her take and vomit from chamomile, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: now the child will come forth.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if the two hands come out [of their place], you must gently pull them back bit by bit; and if they cannot be pushed in again, lay the woman on the seat, and lift her feet upwards; then turn the seat on the ground, and bind the woman so that she does not shake during the turning [maneuver]; and if the hands cannot be pushed in and the child dies, you should cut the hands with the knife that is placed here before, extract the child, and pull them back equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 of the birth of the child over its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes over its feet, you must push it upwards; and then turn it bit by bit, until it is even; then take one of its feet and stretch it bit by bit.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 The patient cannot jump up to such heights if commanded to do so, and causes himself to vomit in distress; if he jumps anyway, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, turn it bit by bit, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Then it will be easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 And if he does not come [down] as we have said, give him a mixture of alum, oil from sesame, melted gum, and grind everything in the mortar; then put it inside the nature of a woman [or womb] and apply this ointment outside; then make her sit in hot water up to under the ribs; when she becomes softened below, take mirabalm oil, and place it on top, and leave for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her vomit and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, as the infant is now coming.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the birth of the child on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the child comes in this form, place the child's hands palm to palm; then lay its head on its neck, and hang its legs downwards, and let it lie on the bed; bend its arms little by little, and then grab its hands above the belly, and break the hips bones beneath, until it is prepared below; and if the child does not scream, take its feet and bend them forcefully, then bend the belly upward, then push your hands; and handle the child palm to palm; and command the woman to hold herself as much as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	The discharge from the child comes down one hand wide.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to engineer a way to return the hand: if it cannot be returned, lift the woman and go; if she cannot walk, make her lie on the bed, bend her legs forcefully; then bring the mustard plaster that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on the chair, then study how to return the hand; and handle the child according to its natural shape, make it vomit, and command her to hold herself as much as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Hold the baby by its neck and spread out your hands, then turn its face towards the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary that the maidservant holds her hand, then turns it little by little and gently; and when it is equal, place on top of it a plaster made of alum and oil, as we have said, then command that she move it little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on the chair, and command her to grab it; and make her vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same way, you must follow it through to the end.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When the afterbirth comes in this manner, seize the afterbirth with your nail until the membranes are empty; and if the child presses against its face and neck, seize it from the buttocks so that it is not held back, and let the child die; then push the child inside, as much as you need to, and command the woman to grab it lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born often, and sometimes triplets or quadruplets; and this is not strange and rarely happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 These are strange things that do not live unless they are named; I know that they multiply, and are desired by the one who invented them, which is linked to the devil; and sometimes they issue forth as naturally as grass grows, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 And if they issue forcefully, the treatment should be as we have said, and make the poultice subtle, and do it quickly and easily whatever it requires; and do so as much as is needed for healing.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 They are sometimes formed in the shape of a man or two or three or four or five or six, or even up to fifteen, and they are all shaped like a child by the measurement of the wise healer, and it is necessary that the poultice knows this because similar things often happen; so do as needed.
de l’enfant mort	Of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you cure the woman of a dead child or womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come naturally, and you are forced to perform manual work; then you must know if the woman is in good health and has no accident or fear of death; then the woman should be supine on her back, and her head inclined downwards, and her legs raised; and the attendant should tie her with strips, or she should be tied to the bed so that she is not treated at the removal of the child; then rub the wife's mouth with oils moistened with musk and aloes and linseed; then anoint the helper's hands with these oils and these musks; then place them gently into the wife, then hold the place where the fingers are inserted so that they are comfortable to her, and be aware if the baby is exposed on top of its head; then insert the fingers in her vagina or neck or mouth or palate or below the beard or in the navel or near the sides or near the costal area; and it must be held by the right hand and the curvature between the left hands, and pushed gently into any of the places that we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty place; and this is the form of the fetus:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 Then, push against each other in opposite directions, or use whatever tool you need to make the extractions equal; and then straighten them equally by moving from one side to another to bring them out, and keep the bones dented to hold them while they are being moved, as shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 If there remains a part of it, then the physician should insert his fingers with oil into that part and push out the other part; if no part remains, then place this bone higher in its joint and perform this action until it completely emerges.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be brought back by holding it, then you must roll up the cloth over it until it is completely rolled; then you should break it at the joint of the foot or the toes, and you must perform this action on both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the child's head is large and it is difficult during delivery, or if the baby has a swollen head assembled, you must insert the pointed sponge between your fingers and push to extract the water; or you may use the instrument called "almidach", from which the form comes with the tools or chapter following this one; and do the same for the child naturally born with a large head; then pull the bones apart using the pliers, and if the head jumps out and is held back by force, it should be cut, as far as the moisture that is more difficult to deliver; and if it cannot be delivered, you must chop it into pieces where you can. If it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, you must pierce it until the moisture comes out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the baby is above its feet, it moves lightly, and the alignment towards the mouth of the birth canal is slight.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is strained in the abdomen or hip, you must straighten it on the drapeau (folded cloth) suspended over the hand; and make the abdomen or hip, as far as the moisture that is there recedes; and if other members are dislocated, and the joints remain, press the ball of your hand deeply into the wound, and drag it until the wound opens; then insert the thumb or finger and pull further; and if the wound opening is constricted by an abscess that has come there, you must not work on it, but administer moist and fat substances instead; and administer plasters, and soak in warm, softening and moistening solutions.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the infant is on its side, and you can put it straight, apply what has been said in the live child; and if there is no ability to do so, tear it apart piece by piece, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 And when this has been done, apply what has been said in abscesses that come in marriage; and if there is a discharge of blood, it should be put in a tight restraint, and other treatments applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman whose belly had been stillborn, then consulted with another on this matter, and revived the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in the armpit, and swelled so much that it opened, and began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to heal, and I thought for a long time, but could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong plaster of attraction, and afterwards, some bone came out, and after several days another one did.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled much, because the stomach has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I will treat the wound and break many bones while the woman is in the best position; and the woman may live for a long time in this state, and then a small amount of bone will protrude; and I have not found this chapter except because when masters find an unusual thing that they know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the husband to his place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the first sentence to translate:
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 The first corn should be more subtle in the restrictor, and it should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the opening of the rod's mouth should be wide, and the tree bark edges must be smooth, and a half palm long; and between the two limbs there should be two alignments of the same rod, which are tightened in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two alignments are inserted into the mouth of the keyhole for opening when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 Another form, similar but more subtle and lighter, should be made of a rod of ebony or boxwood in the shape of pliers; and have two alignments for both horns, as you can see, each one a palm long and two fingers wide; and when you are ready to open the keyhole with all the tools, make the woman sit on the bed, her feet dangling and legs spread apart, then insert the two alignments together into the keyhole, and hold the head of the tool under her thighs; then work your hand with all the tools as you did with the pliers equally, according to the quantity that you want to open the mouth of the keyhole, until the bail does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These tools are all mounted, and have similar appearances; and when the smith has equipped them, he works more quickly, and higher for men according to their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disdain the tool that you have not equipped, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the afterbirth is retained at childbirth, it is necessary that you command the patient to hold back her lochia (afterbirth fluid), then make her vomit with something bitter, and hold your hands on her mouth and nose; and if she jumps because of this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If it does not work with the hand or a spoon, and you take a pot or cover and put herbs that can open the mouth of the woman, such as rue, anise, camomile, cassia, centaurium; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled in water over fire; then put a chain or spoon from the pot and the other end into the woman's mouth, and hold it until the vapors come into the woman; then make her vomit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the patient suddenly falls down.   In this medieval medical treatise, the author provides guidance on various medical procedures such as cauterizing wounds, treating dislocations, and administering herbal remedies. The text also acknowledges the potential dangers of these procedures, such as the risk of death due to fear or complications. It is important to note that while the language used in this treatise may seem archaic and difficult to understand, it provides valuable insights into medieval medicine and healthcare practices.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this treatment and does not break as commanded to the woman that she moisten her left hand in sesame oil or musk-garland from aloes, then she should put it on nature and wait for it to swell; and when she has found it, she should take and stretch it gently straight, so that the mice do not choose to leave at extraction; but it must be moved lightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and detach itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 If the mouth of the mouse has been stretched wide, we have said the cure for it is to poultice and fumigate with herbs; and if it does not heal as we have said, be careful when pulling it out; but whoever is at the mouth of the mouse, tie them to the woman's leg, then clisterize with ointment four-formula; she will hold and pull it out, and it will break; however, when she pulls it, if a bad smell comes from her stomach and head, and makes the patient ill.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is necessary for suitable fumigations for this purpose: no ancient one has proven the fumigation of dill and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of flowers and the expulsion of the afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 And it appears to be a piece of glass resembling a dog's head, and the soft part is placed in nature, with the broad side over the fire; and let there be fumigation on the coals, and let the tar continue until it is wasted, then start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced but rather stopped up by some obstruction; so it is necessary to make an incision in that obstruction at the correct point, and do not cut it with a sharp spur, and ensure that the membrane is not touched; then place moist linen on it in wine and oil, and let it be cured with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will stay in place, then insert a wooden peg, and leave it for many hours, and remove it when the patient sees fit to move to rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes there comes a sudden swelling of a wound or an abscess; in this case cover it with lard (i.e., pork fat). If it is to be treated, do as we have said about the wooden peg.   This text suggests that the authors are discussing how to treat wounds and abscesses. de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula (a passage between two organs or cavities that is not supposed to be there, such as an anal fistula) from its base    This line suggests that the text is discussing a medical condition known as a "fistula" which is an abnormal passage between two organs. The phrase "de la fistule dou fondement" refers to treating this condition from its base.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come below the foundation are nodules and grow larger when they come out from the foundation in the space between two parts, or there is one fistula or more; and when that nodule is old, it opens up, and moisture causes swelling or a slight bowing, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are recognized by those who can see if there is discharge or ventosity, when the patient makes discharge, and in some cases they may cause a sudden jump upward.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if the fistulas penetrate to the bladder and halfway down the penis; and they reach as far as the knee joint, and into the hollow of the cavity of the hip.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And thus one recognizes the persistant fistula at its base, and not a non-persistent one: and it is that you place your finger at the base or foundation, and place a fine needle of brass or iron in the fistula where there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 If there is tortuosity, place a fine probe of wood or horsehair until you feel the probe or hair at your finger; and if you don't feel it, and it does not produce pus, gas, worms (as we have said): know that it does not pierce; hasten in the treatment.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or the urinary passage, if it urinates through it and cannot be sealed with medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it is pierced to the joint of the thigh, then the probe goes to its place; if there is no tortuosity and the pain disappears around it, it is that it has healed, and no medicine or salve through ointment helps it; and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure except labor, and the vanity of foolish people who interfere with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In one who is not paralyzed and not old, in hope of healing with iron, as I have tested, the patient lies between your hands on his back; you lift the legs up to the thighs, and keep the thighs inclined towards the abdomen; then press a tent of iron or wood, if there is tortuosity, until you know where the dislocation comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels it around the foundation, you must press your index finger there, then if it feels as if the tent has penetrated; and if you find a gap or flesh there, know that it is paralyzed; do not move it, for it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 One should know that some can be healed well, but it happens rarely; and the aid one gives, it is this: one heats the cautery subtly according to the width of the fistula, as previously said; and pushes it all hot into the fistula until it reaches the base; do this two or three times, until you know that these charred parts are burned, which resemble a feather of an eye; and then cure them with dampened rags in butter, until those charred parts are gone; then apply ointment soothing and binding.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 But if this is done well, it's good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If this cannot be done, and if the tent enters into the wound until it reaches the base, and between your hand and the tent, place a thick covering of skin or silk, so that the fistula remains covered with care; strike at the beginning of the fistula, then advance towards the tent, and apply the cautery after, until it reaches the top of the tent; then the tent will be released, and charred; remove those charred parts which resemble a feather of a bird, and nothing remains.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the flesh wounds itself, cut between you and the wound; then cauterize it with fire or medicine ointment.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 The fire cautery brings about two good things: the burning of these attached charms, and the stopping of blood and removal of moisture; then it treats wounds moistened with boiled tent-linen or cheese crushed to a pulp until the flesh boils, and then the burned char should be placed on the wound of hardened sores, and the medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it becomes healed and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up to the full depth and is removed from the body, push it down towards the foundation and examine it.   The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the tent, and between it is linen or silk or charms, or it is about to be pierced, there should be no hope but faith and expectation through the administration of one of the three ways: either cauterize as we have said, or strike to the bottom, or if you can, place a tent and treat as first mentioned; do not go too deep, making sure to cover the underlying tissue, and let the pus come out by its own will; then treat, as we have said; it may heal, or you remove that covering which is above the bottom, either with a tent or another instrument appointed; then discard the char that has been placed on the wound, as much as possible; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula away from the underlying area: this will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes fistulas occur in this manner: and it is when you bite the tent (intestine) at the fistula, and it is where it adjoins to the bottom of the skin above, take a pierced tent (intestine) by the head in this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	and push one thread of cord through it (the small hole), and push the tent into the fistula all the way to its end, along with the thread.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it is pierced on the margin of the foundation within, then draw out the thread (intestine) from that wound, and pull out the head of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and bind them to each other, and leave for a day or two; and press occasionally, until the threads touch the hard parts that are between them, and open; then cure the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If there is no fistula, make it pierced in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.  \[Fistula is a tube-like passage between two organs or through the skin.\]
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is not right to cover the fracture with a bandage immediately upon setting it, and then heal it as we have said, until it heals completely.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The form of the spine-like splint used to make a fistula is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other; not so, because it should not be struck where it should not be struck, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Emorroid formation comes in two ways: either they are inside the foundation like grains of resin, with both small and large ones, and on the outside there is blood and one or more; and are deflected from the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are deflected have little moisture, and either a small amount of citron juice or a small amount of blood, and have the body's color; and the treatment for those that are inside the foundation is to instruct the patient to strain in bed until the foundations go away, and the threads appear; hurry up, and grasp it with pliers, or with your nail, then strike at its roots; and if the threads cannot hold due to moisture, grab them with a cloth or cotton, or a piece of camel's wool; and stretch them out, then strike, and sprinkle some hot powders that serve as cauterization on top; or you can cauterize them as mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, followed by other treatments until they are healed; and if the foundations cannot go away, treat the patient with a biting and sharp enema to clean what is at the foundation, so that it can come out easily; when the patient strains and the threads are gone from the foundation, it is an easy cure; and you grab them with your nail or pliers, strike, and treat as we have said before, until they are healed, and be careful not to make an incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 You should stitch the wound in this manner: take a twisted thread, insert it into a needle; then draw the thread above and pierce the needle from the other side; turn both ends of the thread beneath the needle, making sure it is wide enough; twist the thread tightly, then knot it, remove the needle, and do the same with all the others; leave some room for the blood to flow; place a damp linen cloth soaked in rose oil or wax on the wound foundation, and command the patient to rest; leave it until it bleeds, and when it stops bleeding, apply ointment and other treatments until it heals.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of drying from the fire or foundation   (This seems to be incomplete as it's not clear what "of" refers to)
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying from the fire in the intestines and by the constraint of nature, and when the sickness is old and medicine does not work.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is necessary that you burn the bark of a splint or your nail with fire to prevent it from getting wet; then heal it until it becomes dry as needed; and if it cannot heal, repeat the shaving stronger than before, until it heals and becomes free from infection; then heal it until it is completely healthy.
dou fremit	great trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 Formices are small boils that appear near the body, and they grow quickly; sometimes they trouble the throat, and one feels them like death trembling, spreading throughout the body, and more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the cure is that you take a reed from an owl's feather or a strong bird's quill and place the reed on the trembling, making it red all around; then turn your hand around the entire reed until you cover the trembling completely and push it in deeply, removing the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this with a cane of iron or copper according to the following form, and it should be fine-tuned both inside and outside:  (no direct translation for "subtilz desoz et traians desus" which could mean finely made on the inside and smooth on the outside)
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, to keep it warm and press; and if you see it tremble, cauterize the quiver, as in the chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	Of the shape of the cluster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes they make a silver or arsenic suppository, or melted lead or wax; and sometimes they make small and large instruments, according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those who are treated in children's care or who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the cloister is both small and large, or the bellies are bound in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 And it has an opening where the belly is tied, as you see, and the shoulder is pierced within; and it has two holes on one side, and one on the other; and put a bladder of an animal or parchment into the belly, and pierce it all around with small holes, and there should be space between each hole; then put strong thread through these holes, crossed in X or any shape around, and assemble the belly like a goat's pouch; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument before a strong thread, then close; and this is the form of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And the medicine should not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clistere with oil or egg yolk, or similar things, then gently insert it; then the servants hold it in their two hands together until it is fully inserted, then remove the clistere, and make the patient lie on his back, and if the medicine is visible when released, squeeze as much as possible; and if it does not come out all at once, let him sleep all night, as it will be more help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you treat the disease of swollen stomach with a poultice, and the medicine comes out quickly, continue to apply it until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if the hemorrhoids are founded or abscessed, it should be cleansed as well with a very subtle enema; and this is the form of the subtle enema on which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	for the wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the previous section about the treatment of wounds; now we shall tell you the treatments for hands and medicines, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and for how they were made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things that wounds are done by are by the impact of stones, cutting with a sword and knife, or spear or lance, or similar things; whether they are made according to the laws of the body, such as wounds that fall on the neck, head, chest, stomach, liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with the simple wounds of the head, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound comes or an abscess, and the bone is not broken, beware if it is from arrow or similar things, and the skin is all torn and the wound is large; doubt the formation of an abscess: let it purify itself from the head itself immediately, even if blood comes from the wound; purge the patient of repletion of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it does not want to purify itself, let its food be reduced, and do not drink wine or eat meat; and put on the wound, if an abscess comes, soft cotton in rose oil only, or in stiptic wine; and if there is no abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, a little powder, which I will say hereafter; and if fire has moved it, put some ointments on until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, such as the size of a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by tension, then bring them together by stitching, as I will say about abdominal wounds, of the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is opened to the bone, gaping, and does not hold together, press it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick foods such as roasted meat (like beef and wheat), poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find or skin putrefaction not reaching the bone, press it all together and throw away the pus, then cure it; and if there are arteries in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped without cutting, try to tie them up with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light: it is that you put this powder on it which will harden as soon as the arsenic moves it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; three parts of live coal, and grind it finely, and apply it to the wound, press firmly until it dries well and joins with all its blood; then bind it well, and leave it to dry if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
