Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	Occasionally, one does this with alum only, when there is no incense or dragon's blood, but the sore has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the fire has burned the wound, it is necessary not to put this powder on it; but place some soothing ointments made of flour of barley boiled in water and honey, until it stops weeping; then heal it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if the bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, extract it with fine tweezers; I will tell you about the fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound on the neck   (or "wounds of the neck")
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the neck and it is simple (without complication), it does not differ from that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the arteries are severed.   (or "If a wound comes about or on the neck and it is simple without any difference with that of the head, but if the nerves or arteries of the neck are severed.")
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is nerves, there should be no other instrument but to let them heal naturally and not put anything restricting; because this hurts the nerves and makes them recede; and do not put anything cold on the wound, as the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuation with the brain, which is the highest member; however, let the medicine be warm, such as warm water washed in sweet oil, and cooked again in warm water in the same way, and other similar stones according to this method, and immediately moistened.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, tie it with strips, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and filled with pus, pierce or cut it lower; if the arteries are severed, bleeding will ensue, so stop it, lance it, and cauterize if necessary; if the spine of the throat is severed, or if the carotid arteries, keep them closed, so that the meat goes upwards, and do not touch the throat but move it as naturally as possible; then pull it out gradually, and leave it for some days, then treat with strong herbs until it heals; if the pressure has made an impression on the bone, drill it; if there are fragments of bones, remove them all as you can, and leave the rest until the wound discharges and aligns its exit; if the wound is fresh, sprinkle powder over it, as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, treat it as I said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a wound from a lance or sword
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a spear or knife wound and the injury is deep, check if bubbles rise from the wound as the patient exhales: know then that the wound is fatal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it at first hour nor bind it for the blood that dissolves completely, and return to the patient; but apply atracite ointment, and reapply twice a day; and if you don't have ointment, apply old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound 3 or 4 days, or more; there will be no spasms, nor bad heart tremors or strange signs of pain; and when you see good conditions, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Treat the condition and other remedies while the patient is healthy; and if it cannot heal, open it up, because there is a fistula; treat it as necessary.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 If the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is simple, deep or shallow, treat the front part of it; if it is large, stitch it up; if it is small, apply powder; if it is embedded in the bone and has pieces inside, either pull out the pieces, and stretch the wound open if necessary; if they are not separated, let the wound drain until the pus collects; and for other wounds on other limbs, the treatment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	1. The dislocations of the abdomen are great, medium, and small; from a large wound, the intestines may protrude once or the intestine's nerves, due to which the insertion is difficult; and the stitching is more troublesome, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one because it requires more effort to put the intestines back in place if not done carefully. This is because the intestines inflate quickly and return more easily, making the medium-sized wound more manageable because you can repair the protruding intestine at its proper place rather than other wounds. You should know that abdominal incisions are according to four types: the two common stitches occur in abdominal stitching, and the stitches for other body parts and others specific to other wounds are common for other wounds; but they are more specific with abdominal stitching, and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the intestines protrudes, it is easily set right in one of two ways: either because of the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen from cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, heat it in one of these ways: moisten a sponge or wrap a damp cloth only in warm water, or cook in warm wine and cinnamon and juniper and spike, and rub the intestines until the swelling is removed; and sometimes make this wine restraining, and it will be moistened so as to dispel.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling recede, if you moisten the intestine with warm or hot water and herbs such as mallow, for it closes the entrance to almost nothing; and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision at the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is moistened like cutting, and one should not cut too much unless there is great necessity; and this is the instrument to split: cut inside along the curve and do not pierce through, and look for this shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is widened and the entrails leap out, put them back in place according to their natural form in their proper position, if you have the power, for it is necessary.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is in the part beneath the stomach, you should make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part beneath the stomach, you should raise the head and buttocks higher than the parts beneath, and similarly, if the wound in the abdomen is in one of the two parts, you should attend to making the affected part higher than the other, and similarly administer this for large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 For small wounds, you should prepare what is needed, then use a thin tool that covers the entire wound with your hand and hold it together; this is the common way of suturing, and you should take an awl or more, according to the size of the wound's width, then leave a gap at the top of the wound and insert an awl with a strong thread; pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the sinew that is beneath the skin inside, as far as you can pierce it in this part, and bring together the four edges; then wrap a double thread around the awl on two sides, then bring together the two edges of the wound accordingly, leave a gap, and insert another awl; tie the thread in the same way as you did with the first awl, and do not stop until the entire wound is sutured; and the awls should be medium-sized, neither too thin nor too thick, because thin awls pierce all the flesh, and too large awls cannot enter well: therefore they should be medium-sized. And do not insert the awls excessively far from the skin and fat, lest they cut and open the wound before suturing; then close the edges of the awls so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and put weights or bandages on the edges of the awls to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; this method of suturing with awls is more suitable for small wounds, as one large awl or two secondary stitches are sufficient, and it is that you bring together the two edges of skin and sinew together with a medium-sized awl and a strong thread; when you have pierced all four edges entirely, remove the awl to the part where you started, in the manner one cuts drains. And leave a gap between each stitch as wide as a large egg. I sewed a wound of a man whose abdomen was cut by a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, and his intestines were about two palms long, and the wound was inside the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I brought back the intestine as it had been away for 24 hours, and the wound was healed up to 15 days, and it healed, and became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 They had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; I did not anoint it with any ointment because I was in a place where none were found, nor any medicine; I put wool on the wound twice a day, and washed it with water of honey until it became healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and thrust it from the outside to inside; when it has penetrated the skin straight through, if the tip of the skin or place where you have thrust the needle is raised, puncture it again from the inside to the outside at that point; and the meaning of this stitching is that you sew in a way like furriers sew fur, and leave a space once on one side, and return to it on the other, until the stitching is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second method of stitching, which Galen calls specifically, is like any who join two parts together naturally, and apply one head to the other head in this manner: thread a needle or head of the mirror nearest, and pierce only that place; then turn the needle, and pierce from the outer part to the inner, through the two heads of the joint; then pierce both from the outer part to the inner, in the two other heads of the mirror that are opposite each other; and this is the turning method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galen says this, and others testify to it, that the belly should be sewn with two needles, each having thread in them; one needle must be inserted from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets; and know that when the wound is within the belly, the stitching is more difficult than on the other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgments of the wound are similar to those of other wounds: and it is that when you probe the fresh wound with all its blood, before the arse has moved [the intestines], you should then return the intestine and the caul; afterwards put powdered herbs on it, and if the arse has moved [the intestines], apply any ointment that is present, until the wound swells; then sew the edges, and bind the sifac [sphincter]; then treat the wound as other wounds, until it heals; and if you have no medicine, immediately put old cotton on it, and stir it two times a day, until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 You do not need any other medicine for the treatment of many simple wounds, except when you doubt that the wound may spread to the principal members; then moisten light linen in warm oil or rose oil and place it around the injuries and under the buttocks; if there is pain or pus in the belly, which often happens, cleanse it with black wine vinegar, and especially so if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; puncture it and find that when it is the large intestine, it heals more easily than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is perforated, and this is due to the planting of veins within it, and the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the hernia jumps from the wound, reset it in the same way as the intestine while it is fresh; and if it becomes old and turns dark or black, you must tie the dark part so that no blood comes there, for there are veins and arteries; then seize what is between the hernia and the flesh, and hang the two heads hanging from the part beneath the wound to align the extraction when the hernia falls out, and the wound swells.
de la routure dou boueil	of the swelling of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, for I have seen a man pierced or stabbed by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, became abscessed and turned into a fistula, and there was evacuation and bloating; I cured it according to what I knew, and did not stop healing until it healed, and the wounds were sutured.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I see it sutured, I feared that the patient had pain in his stomach; and there was no pain, but he stayed better, improving with diet and drink; and any experienced person said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner: take strong farts, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the fart has opened the mouth, place it on the two lips so that it stretches open; and then strike the head, and hold it so that it cannot slip away, then attach another fart in the same way until the wound is fully grasped; and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 If the head (of a body part) becomes inflamed in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and the intestine can be tied with a thin thread cut from an animal's intestine in this manner: take the end of this thread of intestine that is very sharp, then tie it to the head (of the body part) with a fine linen thread twisted around, then push the thread through the needle, and sew up the intestine, and pull the thread along its path; and this method of sewing does not help but according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the great intestines, there is no remedy or cure, unless through subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or that it be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it swells, is universally called "fistula", and similarly when it bursts and releases pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And fistula is according to the truth, a hard and white nodule, where there is no pain, and it is as swollen as the feather of a bird; and sometimes it bursts clear, and other times thick; sometimes small, and other times quite large; and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh there, it is neither healed by any of the 9 causes: namely, due to the smallness of the blood or body; or due to its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and above the lips, where no flesh grows; or there is too much pus; or the place is pressed, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or the corruption is a type of plague; or due to the slowness in the region's digestion, the healing is late, and the flesh shrinks by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the medicines for cures in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	And I must tell you the cure for a fistula that is made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that fistulas occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, nerves, or the stomach, intestines, bladder, one of the ribs, spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and when it comes to the property of the main member, and similar locations.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all these fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if any fistula does not come up to the level I have mentioned and you are certain of its cure, and you recognize it, take a tent of hog's bristle or iron, if the fistula is straight, use it; and if the fistula is twisted, look for a thin probe made of wood, as the splinters bend around the twist; and if the fistula has holes and you cannot find it with probes, cauterize it through one of the holes, for moisture goes from one hole to another and cleanses it; then clean it carefully to your ability, knowing whether there is bone or nerve, and if it is full, ask the patient about the pain he feels in pressing your hand, and where he feels it; and when you know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, vein, or one of the places I have mentioned, then cut according to what I have said, and remove the damaged flesh and corrupted char that are inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply embedded in the correct place, you must cut through it completely, as much as you can, then put moistened medicine-soaked probes into it, and push them up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; and then put healing ointment on clean char, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this means, cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is rotten from the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If vein or nerve does not burden you or your main limbs as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, remove all the corruption while it is still soft, then treat with healing herbs until it is healed; and if it is not healed and returns bowed as before, know that you are not yet at the fountain: expose it further and dig until you reach the bottom, remove all the corruption, then restore its place; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If the corruption is too deep that you cannot reach it; and if there is only a little corrupted bone, which you can extract with pliers, then extract it as far as possible to that place; and if there are many bones, extract them all without leaving any; and if moisture opposes you and there is no error or fear, strike and press the moisture and the flesh, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something stinking on the wound and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bone, and then the bones will be more easily removed; and if it is a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh, press only the corruption until all blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of decay and comes up to the bone mole, it must be cut off and covered up to the decay, and then heal it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened in a man's leg, so you can take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 The young man was about thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the body, so that the matter came to the leg and became an abscess, but he did not have a cause to drain it; however, they operated foolishly on it until the abscess opened, and they corrupted much of the matter, and it became a fistula, and many more problems came up that all went bowel and moisture from the body; and many physicians tried to cure him for two years, but he had no wise man in the art of hands, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they treated him, and what escaped through the sores at great cost; and the young man's body became red, and he had a citron-colored complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I applied a patch to one of the wounds, then I searched for all the wounds and found that some were coming together from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 I hurried and cut into one of the wounds as deep as I could find a part of the bone, and it was rotten and pierced, and the corruption extended to the bone within; what I saw of the rotten bone seemed to me to be the only corruption, and I thought that there was no other corruption except for this one that I left; and I began to heal the wound with salves for a long time but could not close it; then I tried again, and found the bone as before, and the corruption continued in the bone, which I saw and left; and I attempted to set the joint, but I could not until I wrapped around a palm of the bone, and pulled it out completely, then I set the joint with salves; and it healed and closed quickly, and no further work was needed except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 Because of the blood evacuation, it often became healthy completely, and a hard cyst grew in its place on the bone, and it was well-disposed with no harm or contrary effect in any way, neither inside nor outside coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated thus: take a thread and tie it at the open end of the bone, and command someone to pull it upward; place another thicker thread on top of the cyst that is away from the bone, hold it firm so you draw out the corrupted cyst below, exposing the healthy cyst where you wish it to be, ensuring that it does not pierce the healthy cyst; place a splint or a hot iron under the bone to cover the corrupted cyst; continue this as long as you can see and feel the corruption, and do so again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in a specific area or in the middle, you should remove all the flesh surrounding it; then insert the iron beneath, and press the affected part of the bone against each other to the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is at a joint, you must break the corrupted joint, and hold the bone on either side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other choice but to cut it; and if the corruption is at the tip of the finger or toe, this is a difficult thing, but nevertheless it is necessary that you explore the corruption, how it will open; and clean it in all ways possible, but be careful not to damage the vein or nerve; and know that the cutting instruments and pliers for breaking bones are numerous, according to the nature of the bone and the appearance of the affected area, its thickness and thinness, its size and smallness, and hardness; and therefore it is necessary to equip each work with the appropriate tool; and know that the work will show you the tool that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the evidence of the nature of the disease; so choose the tool that you need based on what is required.
dou feu	The fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The head may become rotten due to an internal or external cause, and when you have applied the corrosive medicine for its treatment, but it does not help, you must cover that member up to where the rot originates; otherwise, the patient will suffer death from this, or a more serious malady due to the defect of the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, as if it were burned by fire, and afterward it turns blackish, since the rot spreads from member to member, taking over the entire body; hurry up with covering, and if this is due to the sting of certain venomous animals such as sea scorpion, viper, and similar, cover the head, and do not give it any space to reach as far as your hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it reaches as far as the hand, strike at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, strike at the bone; and if it passes the bone, it is death, and nothing can be done but to administer the quantity of its virtue; and thus do when the corruption comes or falls: if it comes at the first joint, then strike after the other joint; and if it comes or falls, strike the entire joint; and if it reaches the leg, strike at the knee joint; and if it goes beyond the knee, there is no other remedy for the patient but to let him die; and the manner of striking or soothing the limb is that you bind it above and below, and extend one of the bandages downwards, and the other bandage upwards, and you sever the flesh that is between the two bands with a spatula wide enough to expose the bone; then strike or soothe, and put a linen cloth on each side, so that the soothing does not touch the healthy part, and bring about another injury and abscess for the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	1. If bleeding occurs while you operate, cauterize the area immediately or apply some powders that restrain bleeding; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then tie the limb with a suitable bandage and cure it until it heals; and I will tell you what happened to a man in my town: he had a blackness that looked like a burn by fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his foot, consuming all the foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he cut off the foot, and it healed; and for a long time afterwards, the corrosion returned to his hand, or a finger of his hand, and came to me, and I gave him medicines after cleansing his body, but the corrosion could not be stopped; and he asked that I cut off his hand, but I refused because I had no hope of stopping the matter; and I also feared that if I amputated his hand, he would die, for the vitality of man was weak; and he despaired completely and returned to his land, and again cut off his hand, and it healed; and I have never heard of this happening except as a result of someone doing something different, if it is needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Aposteme sometimes occurs in charnut place and remains for so long that it forms a large abscess; and then it grows and bursts, and the abscess stays open, as a wound does, and the flesh that is over it is as thin as cloth unraveled, and it will not reach the bone or nerve, and such disease is called "sain", not "fistule"; but if it extends to the bone completely, it is called "fistule"; and the skin should be cut all around, and similarly when it is thin, as cloth unraveled; and it will not heal due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	1. And if the skin hardens and corruption is not complete, and the flesh is thickened, cure it with a suppository in this way: check if the nipple is large, and the abscess that is under it smells foul, then use the Egyptian remedy for suppositories which is made like this: take asafoetida, oil, and litargyrii, equally, cook them together in a pot over fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey; then take as needed from this mixture, make it into water and honey, and insert the suppository in the nipple, and press firmly; leave the medicine for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this often, until the nipple is healed and the pus is expelled; and sometimes use a suppository of vinegar from burnt vine ash, when the Egyptian medicine is not available, and take ash from a vine stick, pour water on it, then insert it as a suppository, until you feel that the nipple has been cleaned well; and if the patient cannot endure it, or does not tolerate the Egyptian remedy or vinegar of burnt vine ash, use a suppository of water and honey or milk with a little pulverized litargyrii; or use suppositories made from various medicines and ointments, whose properties I have mentioned earlier; and if the opening of the nipple is small, and the size of the suppository cannot enter it, widen it with a bit of iron, and cover it with an Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment, until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, let it heal on its own, but allow the level or the suppository to enter, and if the abscess contains pus, press down or lower the nipple.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 When the intestine is fully protruded, do not let any char be introduced into it; and if you cannot cover the opening of the abdomen as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the intestine sinks to its lowest point, because when the intestine is fully protruded, do not let any char be introduced into it and if you cannot cover the opening of the abdomen as you see fit, arrange it in this manner: let the intestine move gently downwards, and do not leave anything from the intestine; take medicines for application on the wound, and place linen cloth over the entire wound; then press forcefully towards the wound hole that is larger than the first, then apply oil on the other cloth according to the size of the wound hole, and place it on the wound hole to align the intestine, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once; and he who is on the wound hole, frequently removes it in order to realign the intestine, and recognize whether it comes from the intestine, whether it is venom or pus or gas, or digested or indigested; be aware if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been applied in this manner and you see the nature that arises on the wound hole, recognize that the intestines are already closed, and approach the healthy state; then unfasten it in the morning or the third day, and when you unfasten the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the oil.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts are swollen improperly after many days, know that the breasts do not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poisons act after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 For there are people who have delay in healing of flesh in their wounds and those who act contrary to it; and if the breast swells indigestible for many days, know that the breasts do not heal; and if the breast is slow to swell, it hardens and becomes hardened, then apply medicines drying moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as linseed oil, for there is great part of vitriol and this is the last medicine; take linseed oil, and make it with rose oil, and equal old wine in substance; then boil it and use it; and the same can be done better cooked when linseed oil is not present, or you can take myrrh and aloes and incense, grind them, powder them on the honey when it is above the fire; and then glue the cloth to it, and apply it to the breast, and sometimes administer long Aristolochia root, and celestial roots, which is like flour and centaur; and use simple or compound remedies: grind them, make powder, put on the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if the cure is slow, and not cured by this cure, then know that corruption is complete, and makes impression in the bone or hard members or ligaments; if the cure of fistula is used, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess at the nailbed
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 Parasite is an abscess that grows under the nail of the finger or toe, or it may grow in other places; and when it swells and care is not taken, if it bursts out, it runs and spreads as it runs along the root of the nail, and sometimes it spreads completely; and the corrosion goes up to the bone, until there is a foul-smelling pain, and the joint becomes wide, and the color turns yellow.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the previous section, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the excess that remains of the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is very helpful if the bone is healthy and the nail (claw) is also healthy; and if the nail grows into the flesh, starts to thicken, and becomes swollen, you must put the iron under the nail so as not to touch the flesh, push it upwards, strike the swelling gently and lightly, and apply on top of the remaining swelling, burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corrosion is in the bone, strike it and draw out pus, for as much as the bone is corrupt, it cannot heal; and if you see it becoming more corrupted, strike it with the iron as described before, then heal it until it is healed; and if it is pierced and swollen, and causes great pain, it must be drained first; then cut the nail with a sharp spatumile (instrument used for removing the nail) from one side cutting across, but ensure that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, place something to alleviate the pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain in the hand is fading
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The one born on the hand of some men by chance is entirely fleshy, and by chance it has skin or bones, and sometimes it has a nail; and none of them are born in the root of the joint, but rather they arise in any of the fingers of the hand.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 The one who is born in any nail of the hand does not move, and the one who is born at the joint of the hand, by chance may move; its size is light in this manner: cut it off from its root with a broad lancet.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	One born at the root of a joint is difficult to cure; keep it covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one who is born or should be in the little finger, it is necessary that you first cut the round flesh up to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and heal it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The dislocations that come to the joints all at once are due to birth, or from a blow to the wound, or by burning, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 If you need to suture that wound, it should be repaired according to its natural forms; then put between two tents or dampened cloths anointed with oil rose, so they do not stick together; or put between two thin pieces of wood until the edges are sutured, as necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If one of its two sides comes with the palm, then strike the splint as required.
des vils	 peasants
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 The swellings are large, enveloped, full of melancholic superfluity, which come upon many members of the body; and it happens more in the legs of those who walk much and work and carry things, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must sometimes administer cleansing with vinegar, and then apply the basilica (a medicinal ointment or paste made from powdered herbs).
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The iron cure is according to two methods: one is that you cut them and draw out black blood; the other method is that you tie the swelling and drain it all.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The thigh is to be treated in this manner: first, boil the leg in very hot water strongly until the flesh softens, then hold the patient's leg above the knee up to the part below the groin; then cut open the vein in one of the places (I, II or III), of a large size, then separate and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the sickness can bear; and then tie it, and command him to eat food that is darkening the blood; and start the evacuation and bleeding again when the veins are full, and this helps the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The swellings are to be treated in this manner: press the sick person's leg, if there is much hair, then put it into water (or boil it), and boil the leg in hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if there is no water available, heat the leg over a fire, and then cut on the long side of the thigh towards the knee or below at the ankle; peel off the skin around the vein from both sides, as much as you feel, until it appears red and black, and when it comes out (the blood) it looks like a white cord; push the finger down, making the blood come up through the skin, and then lift it to the edge, and do the same in another place; then make another cut, or more if necessary, lift, and press on the foot, then draw and lift until the second cut; pull out piece by piece until all is emptied, then press; and if you cannot draw it out, insert a sharp double threaded needle into it, tie and draw, push the needle down, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out; be careful not to burst it, because if it bursts, you cannot draw or lift it, and this would harm the patient; and when you have treated it all, place damp wool soaked in vinegar and oil over the wound; and let it heal until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the face is contracted, twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it forcefully, but do not cover it; drag it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron used to pierce the face is curved and does not cut the vein; it has a large curve because if it were fine, it would pierce the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is engrafted in the legs, in warm areas where no grass or trees grow and in soil without moisture; it may also sprout elsewhere but this happens because of the corruption that comes from under the skin, as it comes out of the body towards and through the serpentine path, engrafting between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a very large inflammation comes in the leg and then the vein starts to burst out, just like a plant's root.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the joint opens, you should wrap around a piece of cloth from 7 to 10 inches wide and sew it up, and leave the cloth in place on the leg, and each time it leaks out, you should rewrap around the cloth and sew it up; if it is too long, cut off part of it and rewrap the rest, but do not cover its root, until it is completely out; for if you cover it, it returns to the flesh, causing abscess and purulence or a bad disease; therefore, it must be treated gently and gradually up to the neck, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this vein, when it is treated, can be 5 feet long, or even 10, and once a man came to me, whose vein was 10 feet long, and when you cut it open, you should push out the pus or blood, pierce it through to the bottom, so that everything comes out; empty the material inside, and apply medicines against purulence for several days, then treat as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes in opening this vein, and especially when it opens at the joint of the arm or leg, much bleeding occurs, and it can jump around; heal it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called "cattle disease" on our land because it often occurs in cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and moves throughout the body expanding and shrinking, and it can be felt in one member after another, until it reaches the skin or leaves, and jumps away; and it is poisoned by putrefaction of some humors, as snakes and serpents and worms from the stomach come; and there is doubt about its malice, for when it moves through the body, and goes to the head, and comes to the eye, perhaps enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you wish to cure and draw it [the affected part], one can force it out only when it moves: therefore, you must hold the limb above and below with a strong and tight ligament, then strike upward and pull it out, and if the end enters fully into the flesh and you cannot extract it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does is that it burns oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the oil, hold under it the cautery in shape, then strike upward, and pull it out; and it is necessary to use the patient with purification of the body with soluble medicines for bad humors, and avoid eating sour foods that produce putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 Pain from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that arises in some members, and it moves from member to member; and I have seen this myself.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was summoned to a sick woman, and when I examined her arm, I found a small swelling in the armpit; then afterward, I saw it rise like a worm toward the shoulder more quickly than anything else, just as quick as hot silver cuts from one thing to another; the pain separated from that place and pierced into the shoulder, and shortly after that it ran all over her body until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it repeatedly returned around her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled greatly how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 I wished that many had moved the pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that was because the woman had dry body and open veins, and because of this appeared the constrained ventosity; and it does not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.
