And when you wish to cure this disease and the patient feels that pain, if she opens as we have said, then hold her quickly above and below, and then strike on it until the constrained ventosity goes out at the place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it in your hands, then cure it with those who expel the ventosity, such as fetid pills, and pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	 arrows (in modern French)
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the parts of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The various types of them are that there are those with large points and small ones, sharp and blunt, straight and barbed; and those with two edges, and those with tongues, and those with fragments; and one that strikes in any member does so in several ways: either in a principal member like the head, heart, liver, spleen, lung, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it strikes in any of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you afterwards will appear: then you must be cautious about removing this arrow, for death comes after in many ways; and when this ill sign does not appear to you at all, and the arrow is not completely in, pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the sign of the brain when an arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and the swelling above the brain occurs, is when it becomes hard, swollen and twisted, inflamed and red in the eyes, burning and reddening of the tongue, spasm and confusion of understanding, vomiting of bile; and possibly without fever from the nose or ears; and perhaps loss of speech and voice; and a white moist discharge comes from the wound like pus, and also similar to charcoal; and if this sign appears, refrain from treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The sign of an arrow wound when it strikes or enters a hard object, and not empty, is that it feels like it has been lodged in something hard; the arrowhead may swell like pus, and emit black blood, coldness and sweat, and fainting: therefore, it is certain that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of the arrow that does not pierce the flesh is when bubbles of pus jump out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and breathes heavily and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrow falls on the bedcover of the sick person, it is dislodged from the side ribs; and it releases a lot of fluid and pain and heavy breathing; and all the limbs of the shoulder move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow or food sticks in its wound, by chance something from the indigestible meat might jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow or stomach, and something from the intestine passage might jump out, there is no hope in the treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow strikes in the bladder, and the urine jumps out and flows out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, shoulders, shoulders blades, spine of the back, wrists, hips, legs, and similar, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not poisonous, as I shall tell you what happened to me, you do the following.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 The arrow or spear struck the man in the root of the nose: I pulled it out from another side beneath the ear fat, and there was no pain sensation.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And pulled out an arrow that struck in the fat below the eye under the paper, and the arrow was straight, and could not be touched except the tip towards the wood, and the arrow was big as a Turkish bow, all iron on both ears; the man was unharmed, and no bad accidents happened.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was Arabic with iron ears; I shaved the beard, and made it thin enough to pull, and the Christian was unharmed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And draw out an arrow from a man who was struck or wounded, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrow, and pulled it out, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if an arrow strikes a man on the back or body, and the wound is healed over it; and the arrow remains within him, and his natural dispositions do not change, nor does he find any harm in his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And if another man is struck by an arrow in his face, and the wound heals over it; but he continues to suffer great pain for a long time, and many other similar things happen.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And I was summoned to treat an arrow that had struck the prince's arm, which was hanging limp inside the knee, slightly tilted to the right side; and the arrow was completely buried for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I pierced it with a very thin wire, and felt nothing; but there was a pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was the tip of the arrow. I put on a healing plaster, as the wound did not swell; and the arrowhead appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I left the plaster on for many days, and the wound healed completely, and the patient waited a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his knee for a day; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I place the wound with corrosive medicine for several days, until it is opened, and I probe it, and feel the head of the arrow which sticks in the flesh; then I bind up the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, as long as the head of the arrow appears visible; and it heals well within four months, and then the wound which I made the incision swells so much that I cannot insert the pliers; therefore I did not stop refining and devising ways to extract the arrow, until I made the pliers well on the fourth day, according to the shape that will come at the end of this chapter, until I pull it out and return the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the mirrors judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored: I shall then restore it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 And I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, but not all, for books cannot grasp everything; but wise masters learn much from very little, and from what is present and failing, true nine works, and find nine instruments, below the things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows enter the limb where they are thrust only in two ways: either by the side through which they enter or from another direction; and that which jumps out from the place it entered is an arrow penetrating into the flesh, and sometimes leaps away again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not jump now, leave it until the flesh is ripened around it and the opening is wide; and likewise if it is pierced in the bone, and it cannot come out, leave it for a few days and move it every day; then it will jump, and if it still does not, perforate all around with a sharp instrument until the surrounding flesh is widened, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 If the arrow is pierced in the head and goes to one of the ventricles in the brain, and any of the accidents I mentioned earlier occur: do not pull it out at all, but leave it until it is straightened after a few days, for if the arrow reaches the sinus, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not driven far beyond the bone but only scratches it and the patient remains with a bad condition for some days, then seek a means to draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be withdrawn, administer tourniquets around it, as I have told you; then heal the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is lodged inside the body and cannot be seen, seek it out with all your strength; if you feel it, use any device to draw it out; if you are unable due to the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve or vein in the way, open the wound as much as possible; draw the arrow out if you can, and if there are ears on the arrow like they are held, remove the flesh that it is stuck in by two parts as far as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; be careful not to break the arrow while doing so, but rather to draw it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, press the flesh around it, then pull it out, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood interferes with your treatment, follow what we have said in its chapter for care; and beware of incising the nerve and vein, and bring an instrument as you can draw out the arrow safely, quickly or gently; and place the patient according to the shape he was in when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot do it, then lay him as the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow that comes from elsewhere opens something of it or the skin is swollen in place where one can see or feel clearly; then cut above, as far as the pliers can take hold, and pull out; if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then round your hand and push it into the bone, expand the bone, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then continue the extraction until it comes forth; and if it is of an arrow and it sticks in there, push it all the way through; and if it falls off, you must manage to hold it tightly, for managing to administer a splint, so that the point of the arrow enters the hair of the splint; then push further, and if the arrow is in the splint, push the splint with pointed entry, to make the extraction easier.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is touched, you must cut off all the flesh around where the poison is, as much as possible, then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if the arrow falls or lies in the side or stomach or bladder or ribs and is near, and you can cover it, then cover it; and be careful not to cut into the vein or nerve, and pull it out, and then sew the wound, if necessary; and cure it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shapes of the tweezers used to extract arrows are similar to an eagle's beak, and here is their shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the growing hair is similar to that of a bird's feather, for pushing against the tip of an arrowhead, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of pliers for pointed and for measuring, as shown here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins in the human body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 The veins from which one recovers are thirty-one in number, of which there are sixteen main ones: two areas behind the ears, which are called "doubles herbech"; two arteries in the temples visible; two veins in the inner corners of the eyes, called "aspirres"; one vein that is on the forehead; one vein at the top of the nose; two gullets that are at the neck; two veins above the lips, and these are called "augeherich"; and two veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins commonly healed are V in each arm: one is called the cephalic, and it is located on the left costal side, and laypeople call it "arm vein"; the median is called "fistula", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and laypeople call it "vein of the heart"; the basilic is either on the right costal side, and laypeople call it "ventral vein", and is above the forearm, and it is the one from which bloodletting is performed, which opens clearly at the elbow.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 The cubital vein is the one that is between the ulnar and the radial, and it has two rains; and in the leg there are three veins: one is under the wrist of the left costal side, and the second superficial which is at the right costal ankle; and the vein called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The first hairs of the vein behind the ears aid the old-style cathartics and purgatives; and their quality, as I tell you, is that you seize the patient's head, scour the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then hold the patient's neck with a screw (a vis), until two veins appear behind the ears in their respective dependent places of the head: then, when you feel the pulse beneath your hand, press firmly; next, take the lancet and thrust it through the vein to the bone, then pull your hand all along the vein, striking and piercing the skin and the vein well two or three times, causing blood to flow; then tie and hold until it is healed; and I have already mentioned the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The first artery in each temple is useful for treating old, soft, and common otitis media, and for the treatment of tears of the eyes; the quality of the artery is as I say: the patient extends his neck, so that both veins are clearly visible; feel the pulsation below your ear, then press it upwards on the vein towards your ear index, push the lancet into it, raise the vein and cut it, as you have done with other veins, and perform bloodletting according to your need; afterwards release the patient, place your hand over the vein for an hour, then place cotton on top of it; then form a dressing and leave it until it is healed; we have previously spoken about their bandaging and extraction, which begins the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The vein of the forehead is worth as much as the cephalic vein in old facial diseases, and it has migrated and reddened; and its quality is that the patient stretches his neck while twisting it until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 And place the point on the vein and raise it with your hand, or something else, and let the blood come out according to the amount that you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and not used again with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Moreover, the flame should not be too sharp; and the vein should be cut across because the bone is nearby, and by chance, the flame may break if it is too thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The veins of the two eyes that are in the eyelids help with inflammation, redness, swelling, and oiliness in the eye, and old facial diseases; and the quality of their vein is that the patient stretches his neck while twisting it with a loop, as before; then tie it, and the vein should be tied with a small amount of flame, for there is no heat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is fine, perhaps it breaks; then make the sanitizer of the blood, as much as you need, and then lay it on cloth, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The vein of the nose in the nostril is useful for treating headaches, and scrofula (a type of tuberculosis), and diseases of the face such as migraines and redness that come from the face; especially when it is old; and the qualities of the vein are such that the patient bends his neck, then holds his nose with your left hand, takes subtle flame long, and pierces it through the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open easily and the wound will start to heal; do not go too deep, and make the wound bleed according to your need, then let it rest for a night, as it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The strain of the second anus [or intestine] aids in the treatment of the rectum, the beginning of inflammation, many diseases, worms, corrosion, herpes, and ulcers; and the quality of the straining is that the patient strains his neck under one and the other, as we have said; and the master being above the patient's head, and the patient bends over the seat, then opens the vein gently, then draws out the blood moderately, or as much as necessary; then he changes to the other vein, then unties the ligament, and holds all the veins moderately so the patient does not strain; and leaves it until morning, for the wound to heal.
de la sainie des leivres	 Of the liver incision
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of the wounds on the lips above helps with the congestion in the mouth and corruption of gums, and cuts or cracks in the lips, as well as toothaches and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of the incision are to seat the patient in front of you, hold his neck as I said; then turn the liver, and observe the two veins, one on the right liver and the other on the left, and they are recognized by the fact that they are black, and by the small veins surrounding them: cut one and the other, and if you do not know which ones to cut and you have doubts, cut the largest of each, and likewise for the veins above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 Of the incision beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The incision of the veins that are beneath the tongue is performed after the cephalic incision, and it is in the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the incision are that the patient should lie down between your hands facing the sun, and lift the tongue, and look beneath on each side a black vein: cut one and the other, and do not go too deep, because below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins from which one commonly heals are usually healed in two ways: either by burning them with a large heated iron, or with subtle olive oil as you sharpen a knife, and it is called "anesil"; and they are both wide and fine according to the size and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of fire mirrhine is very famous, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 It is necessary to open hairless, flat veins containing thick and turbulent blood, and this is the form of hot olive oil.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtly pointed out, and is for healing subtle veins where there is subtle, citrus-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The healing of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps diseases that are beneath the throat, neck, chest, and stomach; and it is necessary for the patient to heal quickly, and he must be cauterized under the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if it wounds the artery and bleeding comes out, it must be stopped, as I have said; and the flame should not be pricked, but cut as an aniseed.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the basilica does not open up clearly, you must force it and change another [opening], or you seek any other opening in its place, such as the vein in the arm; it opens up clearly; and cut into the flame with an aniseed, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you want to locate the place of the vein, then you must also forcefully pull on the arm and touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the location for incision, tie the arm, and cut into the vein with an aniseed; be careful not to cut in the artery when you see the vein swelling, for it is from the artery; avoid that.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it rise high like the urine of a child, and the wound is red and thin, know that it is not from the artery: hurry up then, and put your finger on it for a long time, then cut off your finger when the wound stops bleeding; often it happens. If the arm swells, leave it as it is, and do not move it. Let the patient remain in fear, and do not move it until it heals.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If the wound is not bleeding and it swells, and the medicine is not present, then cut open the artery if it is open, because it will shrink; and stop the bleeding from the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 Take a piece of fennel, break it and take one of its halves and hold it over the other day; if the wound stops bleeding, that is good; if not, treat it as we have said with powders that stop bleeding; and stopping the bleeding should not be rushed in many positions due to the small size of the wound and the thickness of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The first vein in the middle helps to drain blood from the head above and from the body below, as it is composed of basilica and cephalica, as we have said; and the healer should be careful not to pierce it too deeply, and if he does, he will find the nerve, swell and the patient may suffer harm, and in some cases it may not heal; and this nerve opens often, and if it does not open in any man due to his subtlety, you must cure it with an instrument of cautery; and avoid touching the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	If there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The first vein of the head helps to drain blood from the head and aid the eyes; and it should be cauterized with olive oil or myrtle fire, as it is the safest of all veins because there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Therefore, one should seek the easier joint and not be afraid if it needs to be moved for the first time, and you can try again; and sometimes joints swell in some men when moved for the first time, but do not be afraid in this case.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound, according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is not done for any other reason than to maintain health and avoid future illnesses; and bleeding should be performed in one of the three veins mentioned: cephalic, saphenous, and basilic; and bleeding should be done at the beginning of spring, in summer and in winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear; and bleeding should be done on the first or third day, after two to three hours or on the second day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The sacred art of healing that is applied to diseases has no fixed hour, but when need arises either during day or night, in all hours and at any time; and it is not advisable to heal children until they are fourteen years old, nor women carrying a child before the fourth month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	One should not heal the elderly who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 When someone wants to heal themselves in any manner, if possible they should empty their intestines with a gentle enema, especially if there is much gas retained, so that veins are not filled with waste products harmful to the main organs; nor should those who are overly fond of meat, drunkards, or weak from fluid retention be healed; and one should not heal after a colic attack, vomiting, stomach disorder, excessive urination, physical exertion, staying awake, eating too much, or consuming alcohol; also those whose vitality has been drained by some event or weapon wound, or by illness of the body; then refine the humors by diet and drinks and medicines if possible; then immerse oneself in a bath, unless there is something preventing it, to soften the blood, and heal the vein from below the third, as we have said; and on that day avoid labor, pain, lust, and similar things; and be relaxed and cheerful, and let the healer stand above the one being healed, and rub his arms two or three times, then gently pull the ligament above, for when it is too tight or constricted, it cannot heal properly; then rub the area with both hands until the veins swell, and feel them; then moisten the healer's fingers with a little old oil, then place his thumb of his left hand below the vein where healing is desired, so that the vein does not move away from the fire.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 For there are veins that run like cords in the body, and some of these are filled with pus, so that when heat is applied, it contracts and cannot open the vein; such is one's case; and if the vein opens, the wound is too narrow, thus the healers should be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, that is good; if not, then continue a little more under that level or quickly above it, if the area is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 If the limb is swollen and the patient fears, he should let it rest for a day or two without tying the arm: perhaps pus will come out; do not immerse in water, then resume healing if it pleases him; and if the wound is small, or the opening is narrow with subtle cautery, and you doubt that it does not let as much blood as you see, proceed with heat directly on that wound itself; open it slightly, so that the limb swells again; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the joint swollen, do not start draining it immediately, put a little bit of oil on it, because it softens the body with blood and oil is made in this place where the oil is applied; and in this way administer the oil to every wound you drain to stop the flow of blood; and this also works for scissors and saws when they are placed on the joint; if it is too subtle, it will spread when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if a large abscess occurs, which often happens when the opening of the vein is small, hurry and put wet sponge on it with hot vinegar for an hour; and it should be done after the blood flow from the vein has stopped, and if it remains in place after several days without any black or green discharge, it will not hurt; and if you see otherwise, put something of aloes or myrrh below the plaster or poultice.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and appearance in the sanctuary of the basilica; therefore, put your hand on it, and if you feel it soft under the pressure of your hand, then it is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not place anything on it from what we have said, because by chance, in court without the artery; but make one dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with other treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each according to the quantity of its power, and of the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it turns red; and if you see it thick, let it become thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary for those who are full and swollen, and have a need for bloodletting, to make a larger incision, and let the veins be wide; and for the weak ones, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed little and often, and it should be done by cutting across, not by pricking; and this method of bleeding is safe from displacement of blood and compression of nerves, and it is better than the long bleeding over the wide one.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 For the one whose body needs bleeding, it is necessary to give soft bread soaked in pomegranate juice beneath; if he is heated, bleed him 3 or 4 times; and for those of cold constitution, eat before bleeding soft bread moistened in sweet syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicory, and a fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if the hand is in pain after bleeding profusely, it is necessary to apply a paste of charcoal and a subtle-smelling syrup, and use other things mentioned in the section or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to dislocate his arm, and strain it another time, if necessary, when it is weakened by excessive strain, it should heal little by little, according to the quantity of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to dislocate his arm after the first strain, and it has rest for nine hours after the first strain, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to heal from another part, should heal within two days or three.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 For there is much blood inside the body that has already been heated and causes fever; it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, open the wound as wide as possible; then you must take care of all conditions of bleeding, place your hand on the pulse when it stops bleeding, so that death does not come in its place, and this happens many times when the bleeders are negligent; and it is not necessary to dislocate the arm, make blood come out a second time, and the wound is closed, but you press firmly; nor should it be curved, but leave it as it is until it stops bleeding the second time; or you apply the tip of fire to the frozen blood that comes out of the vein, and place a piece of damp cloth on it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not squeeze it until the abscess is soothed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, do so in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is drawn from the vein of the head because it is composed [of the same thing].
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of the vein-letting is that the patient puts his hand into hot water until the flesh becomes red; then it should be tied moderately, so that the vein appears well; then it should be pricked gently, not widely or deeply; and the vein should be cut wide open, and the vein should be let near the joint of the hand, and if one cannot draw blood from it, put the hand back into hot water, and let the blood flow in the hot water until you have enough; and if it is in the summer, do not pound the hand into hot water again, for it puts more in winter than in summer; and the vein-letting of this kind is safer than all other vein-lettings, for there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The salve for the swelling of the right hand is effective against all diseases of the liver, and this is the method: grasp the hand, and immerse it in hot water until the vein swells if you see it; and if the sore is on the other side, and if you cover it entirely with everything, it will cause no harm; and do not go too deep, for nerves are all exposed beneath the skin, and then replace the hand in hot water, so that the wound does not freeze up and cannot heal.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have bled the blood as much as necessary, put oil and linen on the wound to heal quickly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sore on his left hand is beneficial for the sickness of mice, and do as I told you regarding the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The salve for sores is effective against all diseases that are beneath the body, such as genital sores, retention of flow, rheumatism, and old legs and thighs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the quality of his wound is such that the patient places his foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it perishes, and then binds it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot goes a great many streams; therefore, open up or a larger stream, or at the ankle, is more beneficial.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if [you] pierce it through the skin that is below, pierce also in the same way as in cutting; and let the flame be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if [the skin] cannot be pierced out, place the point in the water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 If the wound needs to be cleaned for the first time, start again above a little, because the area is salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the sole of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The head of the sciatic nerve is located at the knee joint, and its pain resembles that of the heel when it is hot with blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And the quality of his wound is such that the patient immerses or bathes it, and twists above the ankle four fingers in order for the vein to open; otherwise, it will not open; and if it opens, clean it in all ways you can, and by crossing; and it is more beneficial to cover it, because the area is dirty, and it is easily contaminated by hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you don't straighten it, no remedy will open or close the back of the foot, and turn toward the little toe, and beware of the nerves; make as much compression of blood as possible, then untie the bandage, place cotton on it and hold it in place; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 of the blisters of the feet
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Venous ligatures (or stitching) are made of horns, antler, or glass; and venous ligation is done in two ways: by making an incision and drawing blood, or without making an incision.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 This blistering, which is painful when touched, may be of two types: either it is all fire or with fire; and the blistering made by wounding and bloodletting is performed in fourteen inches of the body, from which one is entirely at the head; and others are at the neck; and others in both shoulders; and blisters under the chin; and blisters in both armpits; and blisters on both legs; and blisters on both ankles; and blistering does not treat blood, except for small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it is not suitable for use unless as a venesection; and it should not be administered to any disease that comes from repletion until all the body has been emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if there is a need to perform cupping on account of illness or custom, administer it every hour at the beginning or end of each month, or whenever necessary; for there are those who, when they have to be cupped, have heavy heads; and those who experience distension and reddening in their faces, necks, and throats; and those who develop a spot of blood in their mouths, have swollen tongues, bleed, and similar symptoms.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially if it is within the month, we order to fumigate after 4 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The cupping of the nose helps to relieve headaches... that come with the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the entire body; this cupping is in place of cephalic cupping, and those who have a cold complexion or constipation should not use it, for it does them great harm; and therefore, it should not be used by those with cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who recovers often becomes negligent, and for this reason it is necessary to place the cupping glass slightly lower due to the doubt of negligence.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The ventosation in the neck is located near the throat and basilica of the head, which makes it valuable for compression of the windpipe, for slitting the channel of the larynx, and for strangulation and suffocation; and it should be used carefully, as if it holds too tightly, it can cause death by suffocation or obstruction of the stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 The ventosation on the costal cartilage of the neck is useful for headaches, otolaryngology, and migraines, strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth; it is located near the basilica artery; you must instruct the patient to press gently with his hand, not to compress the artery, and no loss of blood should occur.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventosations (ventosation) beneath the chin is useful for mouth diseases and gum corruption, and similar oral ailments; and it is located in the vicinity of the salivary glands of the two lower lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventosations (ventosation) of the shoulder is useful for diseases caused by heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 The ventosations of the ribs is worth as much as three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to press too deep, for the flesh is bare there, and knows nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The poultice that is on the buttocks is useful for piles from their foundation and diseases below, and it should be large, made of flax, which needs to be well drawn out; and by chance, if it were fine, it would break; and it causes big wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Poultices on the legs heal quickly because they draw blood from the entire body, and are useful for old pains in the knees and ankles, and bladder and urinary tract problems, and remove inflammation; and they are located between the two shins and two ankles, and weaken the body over a long period of time, causing swelling in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting on the bladder is that you first empty it, and fill it promptly, and place it hastily, and move it equally, and not cease doing so until you see the area turn red and swell, and appear the color of blood; then tie, and replace the bladders, and take care in the positioning of the body, for there are some who have soft flesh and clear veins: it is necessary to pierce only once, and it is necessary to make large incisions, and one shallow; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	If the flesh is thick, it is necessary to pierce twice: the first time to refine the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	If the flesh is very thick, it is necessary to pierce the third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we should only prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we want much blood, we should frequently let it out; and if the skin is thick, press deeply, and take care that the veins are pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those with thick and hard skin, and narrow pores, to anoint the places of the ventosations with stimulating and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, use oil of violet, or sweet almond oil, or seed oil of cucumber; and if it is in winter, use oil of parsley, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amaranth oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the person whom you are treating has tender flesh with large and open pores, no oil should be applied; instead, it should be washed after ventosation with rose water, cold water, water of morello cherries, water of cucurbits, water of porcelain, or other similar substances.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture should rise from ashes of myrtle, or water of bilberry, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 Those with large superfluities rise from old wine or sour milk, or decoction of anise or camomile, or other similar substances; and no one should saigne by ventosation before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and one should not sleep after ventosation, and it is necessary that he evacuate, when he should be ventosed and when he has been ventosed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And let the person who is healthy and bilious, and whose bile lacks being too sharp and inflamed; it is necessary that he take cold things, such as green apples, endives, lettuce and similar foods; eat little meat, and meat of chicken, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And the person with a cold complexion, let him take honey syrup and fragrant old-young wine, and eat little bread and little meat of birds and small birds; and on the day he will vomit, he should drink more than eat; it is necessary to give some men certain times triacetum or musk before or after the vomiting, to comfort the principal limbs; but let them be subtle, but not too hot for those who drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The hollow bladders placed on wounds are those placed on the liver, spleen, gout, stomach and the buttock, the backside, flank and haunch; for these limbs cannot be pierced elsewhere except to draw blood from one member to another, such as when we put them over breasts when a woman is lactating; to drain pus from the member, such as when we place bladders on the stomach or buttock to reduce swelling; and to alleviate pain when there is obstruction or stone, such as it draws out the obstruction by chance or expels the stone from its place. This is done when placed over the liver and spleen when there is retention of wind, and these bladders are administered empty for only soaking; sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in this way the bladder is filled with hot or cold liquid where it has been cooked with herbs such as cinquefoil.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the bladder (or cupping glass) treated with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should have a width of two fingers and half a palm's breadth, and have a notch around the middle, as to thrust an awl through, made of bone or soft wood in front so as not to hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and there should be a rod of the same length as the thickness of the middle crossing it, made of bone or iron, to hold a plaster in place, and they should be both large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; because the swellings of children are different than those of old people, and thin ones from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And this plaster should be placed on the limb: take the plaster made of wax or linen and put it across the rod that is within the bladder, so that the light is at the bottom of the bladder and does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb, as the fingers have been described above, so that when one looks, if steam goes out, remove the bladder; take the linen again as before and repeat frequently, if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the bladder, which is administered in pleurisy disease, not sharp or punctured, and is not brought forth except when it is full of liquid, and placed on the member only; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Without sores are not brought forth except in members where bladders cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in places denuded of flesh, such as palm or sole, and other similar places; and the quality of the user is that when you find bladders filled with sweet clear urine, you can take them; and put one nut in sweet urine, until they become accustomed and have nothing in their bellies; and then they are to be drained from vein and bladder, then rub the member as much as it turns red, and place the bladders on top; and when they are full and warm, if it is a place where a bladder can be placed, place it there, because this is very beneficial.
