Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If it is not so, lift the limb gently, then strongly and press; and if the limbs are healthy too close to the body, moisten a linen cloth with cold water and place it; until the swelling subsides; and if the swelling multiplies, place crushed vitriol or similar things on it until it subsides; or you may put half-peeled beans on the limb, and leave them until they harden to the limb, which will now stop the bleeding; and if necessary, take more linen cloths.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the swellings do not want to take, you rub the limb with fresh blood, or you pierce it with a needle so that the blood comes out, and then place it; and as soon as they feel the blood, they harden; and when you see that they bleed, you sprinkle some powder of aloes and soap or ashes on them, which will now stop the bleeding.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and concerns the treatment of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Inform the dear child that the fool who reads this chapter will never see any of the old books or read letters from them; and for this reason, the science is alienated in our land, for I have never found anyone good at it; and I know nothing about it, except through the knowledge of the old books, which I have studied extensively and treated the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained therein, and have abridged it in the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are brought about, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, let us now say the prologue of this book, the subjects in which wisdom places its understanding, and dwell on truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 When a fracture or dislocation or twisting or curvature comes to anyone, it is necessary that you treat the patient from both sides, unless anything prevents you, such as weakness of body, or infants, or old age; or if the time is not very hot or too cold; and avoid cold drinks, that is, chilled drinks and meat from the eye and shin, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, nor fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about the abscess heating up or the spreading of matter to the member; then the patient returns to his first natural government as he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that make good nourishment or have thickness, such as cooked wheat in water, meat, head, feet, pork, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this nourishment, the bones heal faster and sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that the broken bones of the old and weak cannot be well regained nor fastened according to their nature due to the decay of the limbs, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but it does not matter, place the large tendons on the broken bone which straightens and joins the limb together, until it enforces itself as it was before; and do not move it at all from its work, and for this reason you should feed it with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the hip, or the leg; and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that heals by itself, and another that becomes sharper, like the tip of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with an open wound, or one with just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each one has its tool and device in the restoration, according to what memory comes to its place; and it is known that the break of the bone by this means that the joint is twisted and clearly apart by displacement, and pressured by hand; and when there is no twisting nor touching, and the patient feels no great pain, there is no fracture; but it can have a twisting or fissure, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Do not move the hand, but put on medications that come after this, and then hold it gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the breaks which go into the armpit, and are the two parts disjointed, they must now be put in an even position, so abscesses do not grow there; and if abscesses grow there, leave it for a day as long as the abscesses are soothed; then make it equal to the joint that you can easily and skillfully move; and know that the restoration of it is lighter than the restoration where there are pieces; then straighten it, as necessary hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 If the bone is broken into pieces and divided into two parts, whether it be a hand or foot, or with your hand if it is a small member, or by two ropes, or one rope and your hand; then put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are dislocated, you align them all using every means, and ensure that by your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and join together well the two bones of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	Feel it with your hand if it seems not to be well aligned: straighten it nicely and do not strain or press too much as those who apply pressure through their work cause abscesses and contractions in the limb, as we have often observed.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limbs are set, punish the patient well so that he does not move them, neither by watching nor sleeping, neither by turning, nor in any other way; and take care that the limbs are as secure as possible, so that they feel no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 If they feel no pain, they are not set correctly; it is necessary to put them in such a position that they feel no pain; and beware that they are straightened, so that twisting does not come when they are restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs come in various shapes, sizes and forms.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For small members, such as arms and fingers: it is necessary to wrap linen cloths that are soft and thin; and for large ones, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to wrap with a wide and hard cord, because the thick cords encase the entire large member and tighten it equally on all sides, so that there is no swelling; then tie lightweight bandages around them three or four times according to the limb, and tighten your hand slightly on the cord, then go above the break and tighten less, than the break, then move a little away from the break; and soften the cord little by little, until you take a large part of healthy flesh; then take another cord, and twist it back over the broken limb; then return to the part below the break, and tighten moderately, neither too strongly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first rule above; then put linen or cloth bandages between the cords until they are all even, then tie them altogether with linen or cotton and finally place well-made splints on top if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is an inflammation or abscess, place a cooling substance over the abscess and one who removes it; leave it in such a state for several days; then hold steady your forceps, and they should be about half the thickness of a large cane, sharpened carefully, or splints made from palm leaves, and shaped as follows:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 However, the forceps that one places over the fracture should be slightly larger and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as necessary for the limb of small or large size; then hold steady the forceps in the same way as you did at the first location, then tie a suture above it, as in the first location over the fracture; closer together, less wide; and it is necessary that the suture be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of flax yarn; for if the sutures are thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish people who make their ties with twisted flax thread, and this is a great error, because the suture cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not have less than two finger spaces between each forceps.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient has a splinter in his shoulder bones after setting them in healthy places, place lin or wool padding over it to prevent bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a break and the veins are cut open, I will tell you the cure below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	Know that it is not necessary to set all broken limbs immediately on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 For when the limbs are large, no splints should be put on it before five or seven days, according to your certainty of the abscess healing; and here is the method for ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: and it is that you take flour which is held in the mill walls, mix it abundantly with egg, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster restoring the fracture in various positions, and especially for women and small children, because it is not either too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Here is another method of plaster for restoring fractures and dislocations and twists: take barley meal, linseed oil, elder, marshmallow root, mastic, anise, cinnamon, and gum arabic, mix them in equal parts; add myrrh, aloeswood, and seven times as much alkanet root; make this into a powder and mix it with enough egg; if the complexion of the patient is hot, use this plaster, for it has a good composition and restores broken bones quickly, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another plaster method for twists: take mugwort and mallow, boil ten parts; myrrh and aloeswood, nine parts; cumin six parts; Armenian bole ten parts, grind well and mix with vinegar or abundant egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another method of dislocation and dislocated bones treatment, relieve the pain that occurs, and cut off the bone using a tool, and break it: take new linen, soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and place it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This plaster does not restore, but it is good to relieve abscess heat and bone pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that sets broken bones: take dried leaves of the fig tree and leaves of ground ivy, grind them together, and make plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another method of plaster for the restoration of broken bone and to hasten the healing of abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, beans flour, each one in equal parts; grind them and mix with wine, and if the limbs are scalded, mix it with moist coriander water or vinegar and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of emplastrum (medicine) more forceful than the first, when an abscess hard comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of comfrey, flax seed, balm, clover, and wormwood, and flowers of violets and camomile, in equal parts; grind and mix with salt water or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that nothing other than beeswax and oil should be put on a broken limb to restore it, and it should not be too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It appears Galen says that dry and slightly warm substances should be put on a broken limb to restore it, such as myrrh, aloes, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plaster that is beneficial for injuries and pain: take ground mugwort and crushed human hair, or feathers of birds, and equal parts of vismale and oil, and grind them together, and make a plaster from the mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then untie a little afterwards, and make sure that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved out of its place; if it is not untied for many days and pain comes to the place, or there is itching, without rest or swelling, hasten and untie, and remove the emplastrum immediately; take a thin cloth and sea sponge moistened, dipped in water, and lift up the place, until the itching stops and the pain is relieved; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen moistened with water or rose oil, and tie above a nut, until you are sure of the abscess being hot; and let the inflammation of the member be quieted and the pain removed, then continue the subtle application, and a little emplastrum, and do not strain it too much as before; and make thin until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has subsided and the redness, pain, and swelling have been removed from all parts, and you need plaster and linen, then begin again as you did before equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 And if no swelling comes to the limb as we have said, do not dislocate it unless after three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it twenty days, according to what one sees, until the break heals and the joint approaches the flesh; then hold it more than before, and make the meat thicker, as I have said before; and if you see the joint drying out more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot enter; then pour hot boiling water on it every time you dislocate it, and every third day, and ease a little the swelling; by this work therefore cut off the swelling from the limb, and hastily correct whatever the foolish healer leaves twisted: this is bad, and it is a fearful work, and I see no other thing than to rest and work properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many types of fractures exist, and they have various forms, and their causes are determined; because there are fractures made by sword impact, breaking the entire bone from the shaft that is under the bone, as a hack or cleave does; and for this reason, this type of fracture is called "hack fracture".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword strikes the bone from above, it is called this type of break "absolute"; and the wound caused by these two breaks can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or a fracture or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent break that approaches the membrane located beneath the bone or above it, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if the wound is healed into the bone as fine as hair, and it is a small crack, and for this reason it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made by a fall or by an arrow or something similar, and it causes the bone piece to enter below, and the edges are sharp as a smith when he hammers on cauldrons; if an arrow enters within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this happens more in those who have moist bone-like heads, such as a child's head; and it occurs in all these ways of breaking that small bones are dislocated like joints; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	We should know all the ways of fractures by traction above them, and the probe for tenting, and the corruption of flesh that is above it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is known by this: when one exposes the bone and rubs above it, if the fracture opens black,
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be aware of the symptoms of the patient; and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of senses, extension, swelling, fever, and hairs to fall out and turn red, and other similar signs in various dispositions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an uncertain accident, and you hope for salvation, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when a wound first comes to you in winter, you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day if possible.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is a fracture, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone is not corrupted, and the consequences as we have said come about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 If the fracture of the bone reaches up to the covering of the brain, you must cut the broken part in this way: it is that you take hold of the patient's head, expose the bone on all sides as much as possible, and above the shape of the wound more gently than possible, and if blood discharge comes out when exposing the bone or abscesses appear, assist with whatever is necessary; it is that you fill the area with dampened linen soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscesses are calmed, and make sure there is no more blood discharge; then begin to remove the bone around it, and this is done according to two types of work: one type is that you make a narrow cut ahead, and this is the shape.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then make another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have many incisions of various sizes, some narrow and others wide, sharp and made of iron; and work gently so as not to pierce the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is pushed out and hard, you must pierce it around, so that you provide holes with drills, but not so deep that they pass through the bone to the skin; and it should have a margin or circle on top where the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each one comes in its place at the thickness of the bone, so that you have drills for all places; and this is the form of the four kinds of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you place one drill on the bone and turn it with your hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then remove the drill a little to one side, and do this all around, and then cut the space of the bone between the fractures, making it as thinly and gently as possible, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand or any of the tools you have, such as pliers or tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the marrow.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, if necessary, press the fracture that remains from the bone with all other similar instruments resembling an incisor, but it should be thinner and more delicate than the other incisors; and if any small bones or scales remain, lightly remove them with the instruments; then heal the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of work is that which the Greeks call, which is more secure; and they highly praise it, and this is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must cut open a part of the bone where the fracture has moved apart, so that when you have exposed that part, you will place the lenticular anvil underneath it as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not cut it from one side, but split the part into two pieces with edges facing the bone; then strike gently with a small hammer so you lightly break the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is under it; if it is adhered to the bone, remove it gently, for it is broken in vain and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone does not break through the cloth, and the bone is only chopped from above, and there are small pieces, then you must follow that roughness, and remove the scales with a sharp razor, which you should have in various quantities, to provide the most convenient amount for each place, according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If (the patient) shaves very closely at first, and afterward with something more subtle, and does not cease doing so until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each other type of haircut and break (injury), you must bring about the remedy according to his condition; this is not something that can be answered by one who has devoted study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 And if the wound is exposed, you should take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, wet it in rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another cloth doubled in 2 or 3 pieces, wet it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; do this as lightly as possible so as not to burden the wound, then provide a bandage, but do not tighten it more than necessary to cover only the wound; leave it like that for a day or two until the abscess has subsided, then remove it and administer medicines such as lily roots, oats flour, incense powder, arsenic, and similar things; make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and immediately administer faithful medicines without bitterness; ensure that the wound is always clean, do not leave any ointment or pus in it, for when pus accumulates on the cloth of the brain, it can rot and infect, causing great harm to the patient; for when something bitter is put on the wound, it stings through.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, beware of any bad accidents happening to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful with great certainty.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if blackness does not come violently except by medicine that has been placed there, which property it has, then you should take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and wax on the cloth; then apply it in this manner; afterwards treat according to the appropriate methods until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one by itself, because there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, but instead causes swelling or twisting, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 If one of the two parts is broken, you should grind your small finger or tooth and equal that break within your index finger, pressing it outwards, until the nail grows again according to its natural figure; do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and the finger cannot reach the place, you must place it equal to the knuckle of a finger (a thumb) on top of the nose.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 If the break is in two parts, do it again and hurry to restore it on the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, then insert linseed bandages at the base of the nail where the break is.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Tie another piece of linen on the other side if the break is there; let the cloths be thick enough to fill the wounds of the head.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And they said that one should soften the tents in butter, and stir them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 But it does not seem good to me, but they should be softened in the mixture of egg yolk and flour powder; then let the tendon remain until the bone is hard and the cartilages harden.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes feathers from an owl are placed instead of tweezers, and if there is a single soft cloth around it, and the breakage is held, and the patient breathes through it; then do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	If an abscess bursts while you are working on it, place camphor or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a pinch of alum.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If an abscess has not come, apply a poultice from linen flour and incense powder mixed with egg yolk, then put light bandages on top, but do not bind tightly; if the break in the bone is small and it is broken into small pieces, remove them with suitable instruments, then seal the wound, and treat it with charcoal and sulphur-like poultices and ointments; if there is no wound within the bone, treat the tendons, and put cotton pads on it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	The treatment for a jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible (jawbone) is dislocated beneath, and there is no wound outside, and the breakage is only external but not broken through, if it can be recognized easily, it is corbeled within.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the breakage is in the right part (of the jawbone), you must insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; if the breakage is in the left mandible, insert your index finger from the right hand and push gently towards the breakage and align it with the other hand.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced in two parts, then you must provide two equal extensions until it becomes equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the teeth occurs or breakage, hold them in place with a golden, silver or silk thread, then place a broken mandible splint on it, and put one double cloth on top; and place on the cloth a large well-made stud or equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the mandible, and secure it as you can, and command the patient to rest, and encourage them to eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see the figure change, dislocate it again on the third day, and then reset to its original position; put a plaster over it, made from milled powder with egg or meal of comfrey, after removing the splint; place a light linen plaster over the plaster, and if the plaster swells, remove it, and leave the dislocation until it heals; it often heals in four weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	If an abscess comes to the surface, bring what we have said before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, be careful not to remove any piece of the bone with the tools suitable for such.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, enlarge it as needed with fire.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all the pieces and there is no remaining part, close the wound, if it is wide, and apply one or more suitable bandages to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forearm
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks often in front of the shoulder, and the fracture is according to 3 types: either it is broken and dislocated in two places, and it is in several fragments, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedures are when the fracture is with an injury, that you have two assistants, one holds the shoulder where the force is broken; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then align the fracture to your fingers, so that the form should be as it should be, and not have any appearance or protrusion.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, place a round cushion of cloth or linen under the patient's shoulder, and make it as large as necessary; stretch and lift the fracture, and pull the cushion towards your hand, so that you align the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder out by force because it comes in fully, then the patient should lie on his affected side, and place one small pillow under the shoulder; and push the ministers (assistants) downward on the shoulder until the bone of the socket is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then direct the fracture to your fingers, and if you find debris, then it is necessary that you cut above; and draw out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join due to any obstruction, strike one of the incisions you have made; but place this instrument under the socket to prevent dislocation.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 It seems like a spoon, and is not pointed, and should be as large as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the nature of the work; it has two prongs, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, like the opening of the wound that you have made when setting the bones; and when you are certain of the abscess being hot, if the wound is deep, you should cut it, but if you doubt the abscess being hot, you should use linen and bandages to dress the wound, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses are cold, moisten a linen cloth in rose oil and asafoetida and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The setting of the bone with open wounds and cuts is as follows: you place a plaster made from milled powder and goose fat on the bone, then put light packing on top, and place a spike under it if needed; next take a very broad bandage, one palm wide, then cover the packing with two layers of linen and the plaster; then take a subtle splint three feet long and wide, and wrap it around the bandage so that its ends hang out; and place the splint over the break, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the armpit, and under the sick person's arm; and pull each end from both sides, and when you see that the splint holds the break properly, and you clearly see that the splint does not move on the broken bone, you should check it every day, and when the ligaments weaken, you should tighten it; place the patient on his back, and put a small pillow under the armpit to raise the shoulder; this will align the break in the shoulder joint by the healing of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless a bad accident occurs, until twenty days have passed; then resume applying plaster if necessary, tighten it and leave it as is, until it has healed; and it will be healed in no more than twenty-eight days, and sometimes faster in some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	The break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 It happens that the shoulder breaks or is dislocated and only heals through touch; if it appears according to the shape of the break, and you reset it according to its natural form in all possible ways; then put powder from a mill with plenty of egg white, light feathers, and place it on a double cloth; then place a wide and delicate stick, slightly larger than the shoulder, and if hair grows anywhere around the shoulder, use linen feathers to cover it so that the stick heals evenly; and then tightly bind it all in one strong bandage so that the stick does not move from its place, and watch the ligament each day; and every time it softens, tighten it, and adjust the stick if it is out of its place, and make the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored within 20 or 25 days. When this number is achieved, unbind it, and be careful, for it is not easy for the bone to move lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone fragment protrudes in front and not beneath the skin, raise it up, remove it, and do as we have said in the treatment for abscess alleviation by hot cautery.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture with a splint
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The limb is sometimes broken in the middle, but it happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 When it is broken at the end, it slips downward, causing great pain to the patient, without help, immediately, and blood may come out, and the wound opens in the fractured bone, and he feels it all.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies down with his face on his back, and one cushion is placed between the shoulders, then the shoulders are pressed and the ribs of the two sides are assembled to your hands, and subtly put it all together in every way that you can, until the shape of the bone is as required; then lay on plasters and poultices of salt or another light substance, wrap it in one bandage, and place it on the broken bone so that it does not move; turn the limb roundabout, stretch it gradually, and every hour check the bandage, and if it becomes soft, tighten it; and if it requires dislocation due to corrosion or inflammation that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, hurry and dislocate it, remove the plaster, and address those who have come in methods of treatment; then reset the plaster, stretch it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the rib fracture
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of the ribs only comes from large falls on the back and in the chest, and they do not break except when they are slippery; and it is felt well at the investigation with hands.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the healing is that you align the fracture as needed.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then put plaster, and bind with a stick if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is concave inwards, the patient feels very great pain and shortness of breath, like with pleurisy, because the bone pierces through; and points at the end, and immediately vomits a large quantity of blood, which is a grave illness, and the ancients have made great efforts.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if those who say it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push the fracture outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not let hot irons come unless they have come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If they have come, we heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And someone said that we put leeches on the joint, to draw out pus, which seems reasonable; however, there is doubt whether the leeches will attract the superfluidities to the joint due to its weak composition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And someone said that one should cover the joint with damp linen soaked in hot oil and place a splint between the ribs to make the joint equal on all sides, then it should be cured with the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear due to the fractured bone not touching the cloth, and doubt is in the patient, then it is necessary to make an incision on the side of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put something under the instrument to prevent it from slipping; then you must split the bone, extract it gently, and then sew the two edges of the wound together if it is large, and treat it with plaster until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when abscesses swell up, lay oiled linen cloth on it and place the heated iron; and treat the affected area as needed for the abscess, and let it lie on the side where it should be, until it is drained.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Occasionally there is a break of the neck bones, and sometimes it bends; and similarly with the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And if it happens to anyone, and you want to know whether it will heal or not, take care if you see his hands becoming softened, swollen, and dead, and he cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick with a needle, he does not feel anything.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is mortal in various ways, and if it does not move or feel when pulled or pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient should be healed if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And if a similar thing happens in the spine of the back, and you wish to know if it is healthy or not, take care if the feet are numb, and if there is an accident that is within hands, and sudden movement occurs along the back without control; and when it has been brought above the stomach, it jumps without control.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it is brought above the back and wished to be stilled, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Know that it is deadly: do not labor at its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this event does not happen to him, it will be an easier situation.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you apply warm oil (either rosin or egg yolk oil) if there is an abscess, then place a comforting and drying ointment on top of it, bind it with a thread, and instruct the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on the part where he feels pain until it heals.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone is dislocated, cover it with oil; remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, by sewing them, and apply a healing ointment made of charred material until it heals; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the head of the cow", press your left thumb against it and align it with your right hand as far as you can, then place the ointment and dressing on top, if necessary; then tie it, and if there is dislocated bone, push it back, remove it, and heal the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break in the shinbone (tibia)
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, there is only a little lessening at the head; it extends long and breaks apart at the ends, causing pain to the patient at the place, and pierces and inflames what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as long as you are above the breakage; and learn which is the breakage and its shape; and if the breakage is only at the head, then equalize the breakage, while it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the breakage is long or it declines inside, then lay the patient on their belly, until the restoration of the breakage comes to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it even, place the splint upon it, then put a stick or a key on top, and hold the break steady so that it does not move; and keep the limb under the ribs until the break is healed.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If an abscess has burst, do not touch it until the abscess has healed, and place what we have previously mentioned on top of it; then return to treatment, hold it as needed, unless there is any bad incident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the shoulder break
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the neck and the upper arm, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two ways: one of which is that you take a splint made of large thread, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends of the splint with two cords, and raise them upwards, and position the patient supine on one couch; then lay his broken arm on the splint, until it reaches its place, and have a hump of splint in the middle, then raise something heavy above or the assistants stretch it downstream; then place the mirrors the break equal to their hands together, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is to lay the patient on his bed, and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants that one holds what is above the break with both hands, and the other holds beneath all the cord, and stretch each side separately.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you think the extraction is stronger, hold the ligament beneath the break, and above the break, and extend each of the ministers to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the break is close to the neck of the shoulder, you should place the splint beneath the joint, and on the other side towards the coste, beneath the break; and in the same way if the break is towards the coste, you should gently place the splint without labor, so that the break is equal to the joint, and to the coste; then make the fracture equal, as it should be, and hold it, provided that no abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If abscesses come, do not hold it for more than 7 days, and place soft linen with rose oil on top of the abscess to calm it; then you can hold it, and the method of holding is that you put a clamp on the break, then assemble the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or the chest; and put a cloth on it, and hold it on the shoulder and on the arm so that the arm remains in place, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moving.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone is moving, use wedges, and place a larger and stronger one on the break than the others, and have at least two inches of space between each wedge, and make each wedge so large that it passes over the break by four inches from each side; then hold them with wedges, as I said at the beginning of the chapter regarding the break, more firmly and less in alignment.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 And if you see the alignment of the bones and the ligature, as we have said, during the time that you are restoring the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is hot, leave it to bind until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at the binding every three days, so that swelling does not arise or inflammation comes to the place where the ligature is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If the direction, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And if no such accident occurs, do not remove the bandage for more than three days or longer, let the patient lie on their back and have their hands on their stomach; place a plain linen cushion under the shoulder, and observe every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move or becomes softened; if the direction remains by the power of medicine, and give them the meat as we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the meat is first finely ground; and when it begins to heal, let it become thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is custom that the shoulder and leg should be repositioned in 40 days; then remove the bandage and administer baths and ointments to guide the direction.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the structure is deformed and swollen, it remains to dissolve for days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	on the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "dui" ("two"); one is small, and it is the one that forms the elbow; and the other is large, and it is the one located towards the little finger near the wrist; by accident, only the large bone may break, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small sores are broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; but when the large ones are broken, the healing is bad, and more painful than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is only the small sore that is broken, it should be lightly stretched out and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large sore, it should be pulled harder; and stretch it on the pillow, and the thumb of the hand should be higher than the others, and the little finger lower than the others, and the patient should cross himself on it, and the pillow should be raised before him, so that the patient does not suffer any pain; then the assistants extend their arms to the part below his hand or his foot, and another assistant to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 Then, make the mirror equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken in pieces, place each piece back in its proper place, and if there is any dislocated part that refuses to return, set the bone as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the breakage in wounds, I have spoken about it in a separate chapter; take the treatment.
