Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And if at the beginning of restoration pusules occur, glue a cloth made of rosin and white wax on it, neither too hard nor too soft; and stick the cloth gently over it, until the pusules are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 Then remove the wax, and apply a plaster of flour from the mill with plenty of egg, then put on splints, and let the one at the breakage be more prominent, and slightly larger than the others; and know that it should have six splints or more in different positions: whether the breakage is in one bone or two; and tighten more above the breakage than elsewhere, and less in lining, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are above the breakage be soft and damp, but not hard nor rough; and let the threads, which hold it, be of flax, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And keep the member and the limb afterwards for some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if any bad accidents happen to the member, such as prurit that happens to the member, then it is necessary that you irrigate the member with hot water until the prurit is soothed; and let the member not rest at all.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 Then begin re-strapping, and if the ligaments are damaged and the bones separated, and similar things, advise accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the narrowing of the anus cannot reach the limb because it is too narrow, you should soften it a little and leave for some days until the narrowing comes, then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not undo it until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 Or if around it, then the hands are placed on his neck, and let his necks be even, and guard against movement and displacement, and sleep on his back; know that this break will be restored in thirty or thirty-five days, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the qualities.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	The fracture at the back of the hand and fingers occurs rarely, but it bends repeatedly.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or bent, the patient must cross his arms and sit straight in front of him equally; then he should place his hand on a cloth stretched out, and extend the broken bones, align them with mirrors as they are, until they are well joined; then apply the plaster and bandages, if an abscess does not occur, then place a splint according to the severity of the fracture, and wrap it in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the broken bone is at the groin area around the lower abdomen of the leg, make a splint from cloths, and instruct the patient to bind it to their broken leg; then bind it with a long cloth, and make sure the wooden splint is as thick as the hand, and bind it, as required.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is at the elbow, it is necessary that you place a splint above and another below in the hand, so that the fingers are covered and straight; then bind it all around the hand, and stop the flow between the two bones.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture occurs in any of the fingers, if it is the thumb, make it straight, as required; bind it with the palm, and if you see that it moves, place a small straight splint to hold the fracture steady; and if the fracture is in other fingers like the index or another one, make it straight, and bind it with the adjacent healthy finger; or tie them all together in one bundle, as appropriate, or place a splint on top of it, as with the thumb; take care in the healing and positioning of the abscess, and treat it as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken leg
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the leg are often broken and one sees it when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is such that one tie a splint above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his splint equally to their respective parts; and this is when the break is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is near the root of the leg, it is one of the ligaments towards the knee, and the other ligaments on the side of the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And if it is near the knee joint, then it is the ligaments below the knee and the extension distally; then place the hand on the bone equal to its two hands, as natural, and then apply the splint and tie, until the abscess does not come out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess that is hot, let it cool down first, then return to your work and your treatment; the process is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 You must wrap above the break and bind firmly doubled in two or three layers, and remove any excess, then turn the leg so that the heels are at the root of the ankle, and put a long thread between the leg and thigh, below the knee, and bring the ends of the thread to the top; then turn the leg upward and the bandage upward, then tie a splint above the break, and place a splint on the bone of the leg; then fold the levy (linen) between the leg and thigh for even tension, then begin to bind firmly three or four times above the break; and as you go up above the break, loosen the binding; then take the two threads that you have placed between the leg and thigh, and tie three stitches above, then return to below the thread's head, so that you are below the foot; tighten it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it in this state, until neither abscess, swelling, nor any similar thing comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it happens (that the broken bone pierces the skin), you should separate them, directing where they are coming from, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that are protruding, they must be cut off, if possible; and if not, the limb must be cut open, and the flesh removed; and treat it as we have said before, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thighbone is broken so that splints are set in it, as in the shoulder and arm; however, when restored in this manner, it does not cause discomfort to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thighbone is restored within a day, or slightly less or more, according to the variations of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the groin of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the knee joint occurs little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 And if it breaks, it is not really a break but rather a fracture or injury, causing all pain and swelling, which causes great discomfort.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when one equalizes the limb that is dislocated to its joints, as long as it can be assembled; then put the splint on, and place a round piece of iron, if you have need of it, and tighten it as needed; then check all the positions that we have said in other breaks, like an abscess and others; place at each accident whatever is needed, until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the break in the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is rightly called "malleolus", and the other is called "fibula"; and it breaks in the same way as the arm, and for this reason, its treatment is the same as that of the arm, and the operations are all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	If the slender bone is broken, it bends forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain and can be seen; it twists underneath.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then apply extension, make it even and tie the bones equally; however, if the fracture is misshapen and there are several pieces, then the extension should be smaller and lighter; align according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two fusts that hold the leg from one side and the other, and be as long as the leg from the knee to underneath; then wrap them in two layers, one above and one below, and secure it in the middle so that the leg cannot decline to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one should provide a splint of the length of the leg, and it be made from fust, and place the leg for prevention of movement, and properly make it at the break where there is pain; and move the leg every day, to see if there is abscess or another accident; cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the break of the bones from the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no break, but the bones of the foot sometimes have a break and the toes also, and it does not happen often except in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, place the patient's foot on the ground, as if they were walking, and then place your foot on their foot where the bones are raised, press it until they return to their places; then apply a splint and muffler, and place a small table with two flat cushions under the sole of the foot, then tighten the strap towards the affected foot, after you have wrapped cloths around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when four or six days have passed, undo the strap, because you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two bones are broken, restore them as we have said for the bones of the hand; then set a splint on the broken bone according to the length of the bone, and let it be slightly larger; then place the padding mentioned under the splint and tighten it; and if there are 2 or more, or more, break each bone with a splint, wrapped in one linen cloth, and tighten the padding beneath the splint; and let them remain above the belly of the bone, so that they cover it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other breaks, after we have said them; and treat each injury as necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the finger bone break
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the natural bone of a woman is broken, make her sit with her back inclined and hold her from behind; then fill the hollow of the wound with linen cloth as large as possible; then turn the woman on her side, lift the hip little by little, and pull out the linen when it reaches the entrance of the wound, and the bone returns with the stick; when she wants to urinate, remove the linen, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for 7 days or more: the fracture will be healed, and if you see, take a bladder from a sheep, fill its neck with straw, and push the entire bladder into the wound; then blow strongly through the straw until the bladder is inflated inside: the bone will return to its place; then fill it with linen, and leave it for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone at the elbow of man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said in the hinge-bone; and these nearby breaks are not concealed from him who puts his study and skill to it and reads my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 The break indicates various conditions of the proper way of restoration; therefore, consider this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis (verge), when it is broken, take a goose's throat and insert the penis into it; then wrap cloth around it, and leave it for three days or more, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	With break (or fracture) with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For the one who has a break (or fracture) with wound, especially if it is large such as the bone of the leg or shoulder or similar, it should be cleaned now, as the cleansings that we have said testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, anoint it with vinegar (or other solution), then proceed to restore the break in that same hour or on that day, unless abscesses appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If abscesses appear, wait until the ninth day for restoration, allowing the abscess to calm down, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, because you would bring about a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks and appears under the skin, it should be set gently with light pressure and small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the fractured bone cannot be set equal to your hands, it should be set with this tool which is of iron, about 7 or 8 inches long, and the width according to the size of the wound; therefore, it is necessary for the mirror that he takes 3 or 4 depending on what is needed in each treatment of fracture; it should be round and slightly large, so it does not bend during the setting process of the member in your work, and it should be sharp at the tip and thick from the middle forward.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 It is called "hinge-bone", so the curved shoulders must be placed on top of the visible bone and pushed once until it returns to its original position and is equal on both sides.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the break is subtle and the instrument cannot grasp the bone well, you must cut the top of the bone to allow the instrument to have power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, if you have an appropriate instrument such as a chisel or saw, at your power; then strike that part of the bone which remains in the bone with sharpness and small chips.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 Keep it in its place, then wet the cloth with black styptic wine, and apply it properly if it is hot; do not put any oiled bandage or other substance on the wound that could cause rot and corruption; administer stitches when you have restored the bone, leave the wound open, cover it completely according to the size of the wound, taking care not to strain the wound with the fracture; many times this has been done by foolish surgeons, causing harm to the patient or even death, and be aware that the bindings should be softer and more flexible than other bandages.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident will come, as we have said, and you feel pain at its place, do not put any splints on it; but wrap around, instead of splints, hard bandages and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And if the following day or two you see a swelling at the wound, remove whatever you have put on it and apply healing ointment for wounds, such as theriac or similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	You should loosen the limb two times a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	The limbs should be arranged in such a way that the bone moves downwards gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it remains for many days and cannot heal but continues to boil, know that there are small bone fragments, which is why you must be careful with the wound and remove all the loose fragments that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula appears in the place or any kind of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it, according to what it says in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And if the bone is broken and opens on the limb, such as the hip or shoulder bones, and similar in large limbs, do not draw it out, for many times death comes from this, but leave it until it can be pulled; perhaps a chance will come after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; otherwise, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	broken bones that come upon a suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often encounter [the condition] after health following the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a disfigured sight to see the form of the limb; and unfortunately, the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, take care of the fracture: administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, saracolle, acacia, and similar others, taking any one of these things or all together, and grind them with a stifling wine or with a lot of egg white or ashes; and put it on the knot in bandages, and tighten it well, and do not loosen it for many days; and then dislocate it, and start another, until the swelling is removed; or you hold above a piece of plank well made; for the properties of the plank are such that it removes all inflammations from the limbs; and if the nodulation has turned into hardness like stone, it must be removed, if the head is exposed, and make the excess apparent; or you shave it with any rasp, until it is removed, and cure it when it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the limb that is weak after treatment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is set and remains afterwards, the limbs are weak and delicate, this happens for various reasons: one reason being that it was tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many ligaments, and the nourishment could not reach the member; or due to an abundance of swelling; or because of excessive movements, not within its hour; or because it has little blood in its body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and to make his body lean, until the blood is multiplied in him; then provide baths, and give joy and sweetness; afterwards apply ointment on the member, so that the ointment attracts great nourishment, and reduce the swelling often with cold water, until the nourishment goes to the member; and return it to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When members are twisted after restoration and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say that a member must be broken anew, and many fools have done this in our land; this practice is condemned, and it brings great harm, and perhaps death. However, if the nodulations and tortures are fresh, it is necessary that they should be softened with hot water or with softening herbs such as violet leaves, roots, medicks, and similar things; and you make a soothing poultice, like daqquilon well made. You also take the musk of violets, and mix it with ginger oil or linseed oil, and apply the poultice on it. Or you take figs oiled, grind them with colon flour, and similar medicines that reduce inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes the dislocation is removed by rubbing it continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 Bring movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortures are old and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to cut it with iron, it should be covered up to the bone, at the incision made gently with a sharp instrument; and put cushions and soft fabrics in the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in anyone, now it must be returned with care.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 For if one delays (the treatment), the limb swells, and in case it is put back into place with difficulty; therefore, it should not be moved when the limb is swollen: many times this causes spasms and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, let the patient purge, then let him rest until the abscesses have all subsided; then wash the limb with hot water and oil, then gently reset the dislocation, and treat each limb according to its location.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the head from the neck to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	1. It often happens that the lower jaws are dislocated, and the dislocations of both sides are in two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their place and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the lower part, and the saliva drops out of the mouth that it cannot hold, nor can it close its mouth, and envelops its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is slight, it returns in more ways.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 If it is whole and complete, you must reset it quickly without delay, and hold the patient's head with one hand while pushing a small pad of one of your hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is on two parts; and the other hand should be turned aside to make it equal; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the fingers are equalized, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reset, then immerse them in hot water and oil, until they are gently reset, do not force it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are reset evenly, the patient's mouth should be closed well with soft fabric made of rose oil and wax, then tied lightly with several strings; and the patient should sleep on his back, with his arms between two cushions so that it does not move neither to the right nor to the left, nor make any effort to improve, but takes light food until the pains are removed, and the jaws are healed; then eat whatever you want lightly, and do not strain to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaws are well healed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be set right within an hour and are not converted to their proper place, fevers and accustomed sweating come, and possibly rupture of the stomach, and possibly vomiting clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is ruin; and many times he who experiences this dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the noose   (specifically a noose used in executions)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The splint cannot dislocate within the ribcage and along the spine, and it is dislocated once to the side, and this is felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 Then press the joint firmly with your palm, and it will return to its place; then put the splint and bandage on, and tie it; the arm that is towards the shoulder cannot dislocate again; if it does, reset it to its place as we have said; then put the splint and bandage on, tie it, and tell the patient to rest until he is healed; in the same way, the shoulders are also reset when they are dislocated from their place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	When the shoulder joint is dislocated.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one of which is when it dislocates at the neck area below; and the second is at the hip area; and it may also dislocate above, but this rarely happens; it does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor inside the nerves; and it often dislocates below towards the neck, especially in those with little flesh, as it can easily spring out; in those with enough flesh, it leaps out a little, and returns a little.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes happens to some men, percussion or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you should verify [the shoulder], until you are sure; and then start the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 Also, recognize that the dislocation is downwards towards the neck, and make a distinction between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them; and you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and below the neck touching the top of the shoulder, just as there is an eye socket; and the sick cannot return their hand to its place, nor make any movements; and in the same way, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you can clearly feel it; and this type of dislocation is not only difficult to correct when it is new, but also when the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister lifts the patient's hand up high, then places his thumbs underneath the joint, and forces the joint upward to its place; the minister lifts the hand, and stretches it up, puts it back down; it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said in a few days, the patient should be bathed in hot water; and bring soothing, softening and calming ingredients such as a decotion of althea, fenugreek and melilot in water, and apply it; then have the patient lie on his back, and place a piece of linen equal in size, neither too soft nor too hard, under the affected shoulder; then place a stone on the patient's heel, and carefully lift the patient's head towards the affected shoulder, pulling the hand of the patient; and another minister should hold the patient's head still so it does not move backwards; this shoulder will immediately return to its place, and if you see that it dislocates again in this way: it is necessary for a person larger than the patient to be present; and be straight towards the side, and push the affected shoulder under the patient's shoulder blade, lifting the patient's shoulder upward so the patient hangs on the arm; and another minister pulls the patient's hand downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too lightweight, they cannot bear any heavy thing with them, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And it can also be done in another way: and it is that one pushes the long needle into the ground so that the head is like the pistil, and neither too thick nor too thin; then it should be placed beneath the patient, but with cloth soft above, and the patient should be lying on his long side; then stretch your hand below on the other side forming a shape, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return due to everything that we have said, then do this cure: take a needle from both hands, four inches long and wide, with a head rounded for insertion full depth into the anus, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay the rod, wrapped in cloth, on top of the patient's head, so that it does not prick the patient, then place him under the cushion of the patient; extend his arm above the long rod, and tie the shoulder to the rod, and the forearm at the end of the upper arm, then lift the arm onto one iron hook of a scale with a large hole, and spread out the hands below, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will be relocated in this manner.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, whichever way that may be, you must put an equal piece of wool under the cushion, then apply the plaster made of mill powder, along with incense and egg whites, over the entire shoulder and around, then tie it under the cushion with a thread, turn the thread around the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and keep the hands in this manner.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary to give food, as long as the limbs are comfortable, because it will heal faster; and then give more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it becomes hard and does not soften, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is displaced due to moisture or for another reason, then you must apply cauteries at three places, as it is stated in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you do all of this and it still dislocates again after 7 days, and the joint cannot hold and cannot lift its arm above, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is either cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint can never be pushed back into place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the thighs or hips, and the backside, is caused by forceful pushing and stretching with hands, and another method of treatment is applied; and it is cured when it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after the healing comes swelling to the member, and it moves slowly; have the patient use baths many times until the swelling subsides, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of the dislocation, the cost is great.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the jointure of cost is dislocated at points, and at points it returns; and if it is dislocated in all parts, both front and back, and the dislocation is not repaired, for it can be seen well and felt well; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 When joining the wound with healthy flesh, make sure you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is bound, and the arm cannot bend or touch the shoulder completely.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	Then you must reset the dislocation as soon as an abscess opens up, for if an abscess opens up, it is harmful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be fully reset, especially when it is at the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and in many cases death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is when it can be reset that you extend your hand to its two hands; and his arms should be spread out, and the hands of the mirror according to the shoulder around it, above and below, and push the joint back to its sockets together, or to the root of the palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when it doubles its hand to its hand, and pierces the root of the palm that has been dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 If it does not return to its place, apply strong extension; and two people must extend the arm and hold it still during extension; then turn the arm in each direction, after you have wrapped a double-length and wide cloth around it; when the healer joins the joint with his hand, oil it for softening the joint, then press the joint firmly until it returns; and when it is at its place, apply dry plaster with egg, hold it still and let the arm rest on the neck of the patient for some days, then unbind it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firmly held in place, remove the bandage and leave it alone; if you see that the joint does not hold properly, repeat the plaster and bandage, and leave it like this for some days until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if it feels pain after the repositioning of the joint, and it becomes stiff, bathe and rub it well, and press until it is soothed; or you place a sheep's fat pad on the jointure, leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and let him enter the bath; and when it sweats, rub the jointure gently, then replace the fat pad, and then enter the bath again; and do this two or three times until it heals; and if you see, place warm moistened hay stack on it and hold it in place; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	swelling of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is quick to dislocate more than other joints; it must be returned to its place quickly as soon as it is dislocated, unless the lews are swollen or there is hot abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the repositioning of the hand, you put the sick hand on a table, and extend the assistant's hand, and the assistant places the hand in equal position, so that he puts his palm over the appearance of the jointure, and pushes it back until it returns completely; it is necessary for you to check if it is in its proper place; then put the patient's back of the hand on a table for extension and repositioning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, have the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and have the attendant place his hand above that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it recurs now, it is good; if not, hold down plasters or soothing poultices on the abscess and let it start again with sensation.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if he cannot endure it and you cannot put it back after some days, the dislocated joint remains out of place; and it does no harm to the patient as long as the hand is paralyzed and cannot tighten anything; then know that the nerves or arteries are cut, or there is no other means but to tighten it with a cautery in this case, and by chance nothing else helps.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put the poultice we have mentioned on it, then compress and leave it for 5 days, then release and let it be as it is.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is no grating, moist warm water, and rub it until it becomes clean.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocations of the fingers of the hand.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 In some cases the fingers of the hand are dislocated on both sides, in some cases on the back of the palm or the belly; then you push the dislocation into the pockets as much as it will go back, then hold the head of the finger and turn it towards the side where it is disjointed; and leave it for two days, and then make it straight that day; and bind it, as we have said, and unbind it from day to day, and make it move, and bind it again; and do this often, until it becomes narrow, and similarly do, if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it heals; and similarly do, when it is dislocated from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	the dislocation of the vertebra in the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebra in the back or neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, as death quickly approaches the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the signs are that the exits jump uncontrollably, and cannot be held, and many times some member is softened, or the two legs or the two arms or the spine; and many times the spinal cord becomes paralyzed at four parts; this which becomes paralyzed at the back is called "gilbositez": the cure is that you observe whether the gilbositez has come from childhood: if it has not, there is no cure or healing from then on.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And the one that falls or from blows or similar things, the ancient methods of cures spoke in great words, but there is no real benefit in all; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the hernia that comes before, there is no trick or healthiness; and similarly the one that comes straight into two places, and cannot be cured except by him who comes from behind, as I said; and it is that the patient should be laid out on his back in an equal position, and have a support underneath him, so he does not bleed; then insert a needle in the head of the hernia in the earth, and another at the feet, and tie a rope over the patient's testicles, and another at the thighs, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two ministers should know the ropes, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two needles; and they should be well tied, the needles as we have said, and the mirrors place their palms on the spine formed, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if the dislocation does not return through this treatment, take a board that is three feet long, hollow it out underneath, and position the patient on their side. Push the upper part of the board beneath the hollow, then place the middle of the board on the spine; place your hands on the other end of the board and press firmly until it returns to its place. And if you see, do it with a turner who turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And take two thorns of a great length, one on the head of the patient and the other at their feet, with a palm's distance between each thorn; in each thorn, place the turner's iron rod, and make sure the thorns are firmly fixed to the ground so they do not move. Between the two thorns place another thorn for turning, as rope twines, and have two small thorns of a palm's length for each turning rod; then tie the ropes that are around the shoulders to both turners, and one rope to the head and another to the feet, so each minister turns their turner all along the rope. The master aligns the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is aligned, place a drying plaster with plenty of egg on top, then bandage it, and then put the patient on a table three feet long, which presses the affected area and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a rope as we have said, and make the patient rest until he is well; and if any thing comes at the end of recovery, administer softening and calming medicines, along with the tool mentioned above; sometimes a piece of wood is also administered, and sometimes the appearance is in the back spondyle, and it is thought to be dislocations; and this is the bone that opens up, which should not be assumed: by chance it might bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of the dislocations of the shoulder
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Note that the dislocations of the shoulder and the shoulder joint occur only due to dislocations and not like other joints; and the shoulder joint is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more on the inside, and less so in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the recognition of his dislocation within is that when joining the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick genitals are wider than the healthy ones, and the sick person cannot bend his knee in fire; and it is the joint which is dislocated swollen with abscess that heats up, because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that whose it comes to dislocation, is that this event is opposite to those mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that whose it happens before, are that his leg is well set according to the completion; however, do not double the knee pain, and if you wish to make him walk, he cannot move forward, and he retains his urine, and swells the ankle, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that whose it happens after, are that he cannot extend his knee, nor double it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is in the place beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The re-alignments of this kind of dislocation are such that you observe whether the dislocations are old and remain according to their position without any treatment; and it is not necessary that there should be any assumption made about it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	In the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four kinds of dislocations, you hurry up to turn the joint, and push it inwards and outwards, and move it left and right; by chance if it returns, no further treatment is required.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this way, then you must prepare a strong man as the assistant, and hold the leg firmly with his hands, or tie him up at the knee; and another assistant extends his hand above in such a manner that he puts his hands under the buttocks, then tightens a rope around the thigh; and another holds the head of the rope; and all extend upward and downward simultaneously, until the sick person rises from the ground once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common for the four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If it isn't so (dislocated), you must apply treatment to its appearance. When there is dislocation at the joint, you must have the patient lie on his healthy side, then tie a rope around the thigh's root and the protruding part below the angle; next, raise the rope towards the angle and toward the joint; then take another assistant, grasp the large part of the affected thigh, extend it outward in a stretching motion: it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 If you cannot fix it in this manner as we have said, then you must tie the two feet of the patient firmly with a soft rope above both ankles and knees, and the affected leg should be extended two inches more than the other; next, hang him by the head from a pole, and his hands should be suspended for length; then command the assistant to seize the thigh's head, while another assistant holds onto the patient, who grasps the thigh, as the joint will return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is at the shoulder, if the patient lies down, as we have said in the case of shoulder pain, and pulls the ligament above the affected leg properly, and above the pelvis likewise; then place two needles, one at the head and another at the feet, then thrust the needle between the knees toward the patient; and wrap damp cloths around it to prevent burning the patient, then extend each minister (helper) toward him, and the mirror place equal to his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place it on a table and press as we have said in the case of shoulder pain, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it should be extended immediately, as I have said; and place the mirror on the opposite side of the diseased angle, then press with the other hand, and draw it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is to the side, it should not be extended below, nor raised above ground; rather, the patient should remain as he was when dislocated, as we have said in the lying-down position on two pillows; and above his face, and the limb extended as we have said before, and must press on the joint at the table; and will be right when the patient extends his legs and they are even; then adjust the thighs, and apply a splint, and bind with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and rest for three or four days, then release, and apply the splint again; and if you see that they are even, bind as before, and leave for three days; then release, and let him walk gently until the limbs are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: inside, outside, and backside; do not dislocate it forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.
