And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if it does not bend at the knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is that you make the patient sit straight, extend his leg if he can, and place your back on its face, and place his foot on your feet; then take his thigh with your hands, pull it apart between your hands, then bend both sides of the thigh inwardly forming a figure like a "V"; another servant extends his foot until the thigh returns to its place, and the signs are that it should bend his leg lightly at the knee; apply ointment, and bind the leg to the knee tightly for about three or four days, then release it; and do not let the patient walk, until the limbs are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not dislocated, provide strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the dislocation, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes smashed, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the signs are that the ankle is sprained, and it tends towards the part where it is dislocated; the repositioning should be easy, and it must be extended slightly with hands when it is only swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is completely dislocated, you should make the patient sit straight, and hold the leg with one hand above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then towards the left hand twice, then lift it up, and push the foot up forcefully; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, repeat the procedure, for it will return; and if it cannot return, place the patient on their back on the ground, and drive the splint firmly into the ground between their knees, and wrap cloths around to prevent bleeding the patient; then hold the leg with one hand and another holds the healthy leg below, so that they hold the foot above the knee; then each helper should extend equally, and the splint should be close between the patient's knees to keep the patient when lifting; then place the mirrors equal to the dislocation on their hands, and another holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is ready, place the plaster and wool on top, press firmly, and tie the leg to the foot, watching that the ligature is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligature softens, press again; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and let the patient walk for four days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that he will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If an abscess comes to the surface, you must drain it, as we have said before, until it is healed.
des dois	The two [hands]
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two hands are dislocated, they must be carefully extended without exertion, and it is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the dislocation is in any way on the back of the foot, you must make the patient sit flat on a level surface or table straight, put your foot on the opening of these jointures, press firmly until it returns; and when it is even and there is no gap, place a two-fingered table under the foot's heel, then tie it firmly, and leave it for three days, then untie it; let him rest until he is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	About wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with dislocation and it is seen to be restored, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in treatment, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, nor hasty; and begin first with soothing abscesses, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, as soon as the abscesses heal; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing abscesses, and treat the wound, as necessary, with dry ointments; and if there is a break with dislocation and small bones are crushed, then set the bones, and do what we have said about simple diseases; and beware of entering into fear, as I have said, for this will bring about your fate according to your Creator, and for the sake of your weaponry and body.
Amen	 Amen (This word is from the Latin language, used as a concluding formula in Christian prayers and rituals.)
